And if you can imagine a thing, it could be true...

How to read this book

This is a story where you have to choose how your adventure unfolds.

Each chapter has a number and when you have finished the chapter you will have a list of options. Each option shows the number of a chapter you can choose to go to next.

Sometimes there will be lots of options. Sometimes just one.

The options at end of the chapter are not links - you can't click them and go to that chapter.

Instead you have to bring up the list of chapters on your reading device and scroll to the one you need.

Why did I do it this way?

Well for some of the options you need to figure out the number of the chapter. If it was a link you could just click and go without figuring out anything - much less fun!

But also because scrolling through the chapters brings the feel and excitement of turning the pages in a 'real' "choose how your adventure unfolds" book to find the next part of the story. Who knows where you will end up next?

The story begins...

1.
The mysterious letter

"Arthur come here quick!" says Evan to you. "You've got a funny letter!"

You yawn and get up from the breakfast table. You can see your little brother Evan holding a large old fashioned looking envelope that has just been posted through the front door.

"Lemme see" you say.

Sure enough on the front of the yellow-brown envelope is your name, Arthur Otley, written in spidery black ink. How curious. You turn the letter over and are surprised to see a big blob of red wax holding the envelope closed, not the normal spit-glue.

You don't get many letters and you have never got a letter that looked like this before. It looks like it was posted 100 years ago.

"Morning my little munchkins!" Dad cries out as he bounds down the stairs in his dressing gown. "What's that you've got there Arthur?"

"It's a letter, but... it looks a bit odd" you reply.

"Junk mail eh?" says Dad.

Will you:

............................................................

1. Examine the envelope more carefully, perhaps it will reveal some clues about who sent it. ~ Go to number 50

2. Rip open the envelope immediately and see what's inside. ~ Go to number 9

2.
Snako Malboy

"Hello," you say to the boy "my name's Arthur Otley and I'm going to Hogsnorts. Who are you?"

The boy does his sneering smile at you again.

"Snako Malboy. Yes I too am going to Hogsnorts. My father went to Hogsnorts. My grandfather went to Hogsnorts. So did his father and so on up to 72 generations and the founding of the school. Sylvester Snake - yes the Sylvester Snake is my direct ancestor. And my mother and their mothers too. So yes I am going to Hogsnorts."

"Who is Sylvester Snake?"

"Sylvester Snake is only the founder of Snake House! The best house in the school. I'm going to be in Snake House. Snake House is for the really powerful wizards, like I will be one day. You will be in Hedgehog House I suppose."

"I haven't decided yet" you reply.

"Well if you want to be Snake House like me you have to be strong and ruthless. Snake House rules yah sssssssss!"

Snako Malboy stuck his tongue in and out of his mouth like a snake and hissed - not an easy thing to do at the same time. You are impressed.

At that point the magic tape measure is finished with Snako and moves over to you.

............................................................

1. Get measured for your robes ~ Go to number 32

3.
Up against a brick wall

The brick wall stares back at you blankly.

A plastic bag rides a gust of wind past your ankles.

You will have to try something else.

............................................................

1. Try something else ~ Go to number 40

4.
A spellbook puzzle

You walk further into the book shop and spy a cheerful looking old witch wearing a black t-shirt with the word Watertomes on the back.

"Excuse me," you say "Can you show me where the year 1 spellbook is?"

"Off to Hogsnorts are you young man?" replies the old witch with a little cackle. "Yes I can show you, follow me!"

You and your mum follow the Watertomes witch as she shuffles off to the back of the bookshop. She picks up a heavy red book.

"That will be 14 Frigates please."

"Ah yes," replies your mum, "We've only got pounds. Is that a problem?"

"Well to tell the truth I don't really need money because I can magic up anything I like anyway. But I can't just give it to you for nothing... Tell you what, if you can solve my puzzle you can have it."

"What's the puzzle?" you reply nervously, you never did like puzzles that much.

"My lovely spell books are all about turning words into magic. And one of the magic things about words is that you can turn them into numbers.

For example the word CAB can turn into the number 6. C is the third letter of the alphabet, A is the first letter and B is the second. 3 + 1 + 2 = 6 so CAB turns into 6.

If you can magically turn my name into a number I will give you this book. My name is BOB. The old witch called Bob smiles at you encouragingly.

"Hmmm let's see" you say. As you are thinking the boy you saw at the front of the bookshop pushes a piece of paper into your hand.

"Here!" he says, "this should help!"

The piece of paper has all the letters of the alphabet next to their numbers:

A=1, B=2, C=3, E=4, D=5, F=6, G=7, H=8, I=9, J=10, K=11, L=12, M=13, N=14, O=15, P=16, Q=17, R=18, S=19, T=20, U=21, V=22, W=23, X=24, Y=25, Z=26

............................................................

1. You turn Bob's name into a number, and go to that number ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. You don't fancy maths right now - you go to get your magic wand ~ Go to number 5

5.
Wanderful Wands

You decide to visit Wally's Wanderful Wands shop next. Now that you are looking good in your pointy wizard hat, you want to get your hands on a wand as soon as possible and start doing some real magic!

The sign above Wally's shop is a giant wand dangling from a chain above the shop door. It swings gently to and fro even though there is no breeze to speak of, and little crackles of electric-gold magic arc over its surface.

You can't help thinking that this wand must also double up as Wally's security system.

With a nervous glance upwards you and your Mum enter the shop.

The inside is sparklingly clean and glass cabinets are artfully arranged around the shop. Each cabinet contains three or four magic wands, resting on little red cushions with gold tassles. It all looks very expensive.

"Arthur are you sure this is the only wand shop?" asks your mum. "Perhaps there is another one that is not quite so err... so un..."

"Welcome!" a smooth rich voice startles them from the back of the room. "Welcome to Wally's Wanderful Wand shop! And madam I can assure you that this is the only wand shop in Hippoto Mews. But fear not I'm sure we can find a wand that is the perfect match for young Arthur."

"How did you know my name?" you ask in surprise.

"One of the many branches of magic in which I am an expert, young Arthur, is mind reading. Just by looking into your eyes I can see the entire contents of your brain. I can also do it by looking in your ears, in your mouth, up your nose... any hole works to tell the truth. But I usually prefer the eyes. Also your Mum called you Arthur when you entered my shop."

"And you are Wally I suppose?" says your Mum.

"I am indeed, dear madam. Did you divine this from looking in my ear hole? Remarkable!"

"No I figured it out when you said this was your shop."

"Quite so. We are all mind-readers to some degree."

"Mr Wally" you interrupt "can I have a wand please?"

"No you cannot have a wand Arthur. But what you can have is the wand. Every wand is unique! You are unique! You require the exact match for your particular thaumaturgical resonance. Your thaumaturgic twin as it were. The most powerful - the only! - tool you will ever need as a magician."

"That sounds nice," says your Mum, "but we don't want anything too fancy. The thing is we don't have much, or in fact any, wizard money. Frigates I mean."

"The wand is of course priceless. I do offer a 10% discount for Hogsnorts' students in their first year. But for you I will increase this discount to 100% if - if! - Arthur and I can establish a true connection of minds, and I can see that you Arthur are a worthy wandholder."

"A 100% discount you say? That's a good deal. Arthur see if you can connect up your mind with Wally's love." your Mum suggests.

Wally crouches down in front of you and holds your ears gently but firmly forcing you to look deep into his blue grey eyes. At first nothing happens. But after just a few moments you get the strange sensation of being pulled towards his eyeballs; his black pupils feel like they are dragging you inwards.

"Good Arthur, very good!" says Wally. "I believe that the magical connection between our minds is now established, and astonishingly quickly too! You must have deep reserves of magic.

"Arthur I need you to think of a number. If I can read your mind and tell you the number you were thinking of this will be proof that the magical mind connection is working properly.

"First I need you to think of a number between 1 and 10. But don't tell me what it is! Have you got one?"

You think of a number and nod your head.

"Now" says Wally, "I need you to multiply this number by 9. 9 is a number with strong magical properties" he explains.

You multiply your number by 9.

"The next step" he says, "is to split your answer into the two digits and add those two digits together. For example if your answer is 13 (and I know it is not!) then you would split it into 1 and 3, then add that 1 and 3 together, so 1 + 3 = 4.

"Ok" you say as you do the sum in your head.

"Now take that answer and multiply it by 6. Can you do that?"

"Yes" you reply.

"Now turn to that number! And we will see if our minds are connected."

............................................................

1. Turn to the number that you have thought of ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. You are not in the mood for mindreading, go to get your spell book instead ~ Go to number 26

6.
Back on the street

Back on Hippoto Mews, the crowds of witches and wizards seem even thicker.

When a small child magician walks past because the pointy end of their hat is about the same height as your face and when one of them turns round quickly, it could easily poke your eye out if you are not careful.

But this doesn't really bother you, it's so exciting to be around real magicians!

"Do you feel better after some fresh air Arthur?" asks your mum. "We still need to get your wizard robes before you can go to Hogsnorts. Come on, let's go back to see those witches"

............................................................

1. Go to Spellwitches to get a wizard's robe ~ Go to number 46

7.
Pigeon holed

You elbow your way to the front of the queue. You can't wait to see what will happen next!

"Arthur Otley" says Slumblebore, "as you are first in line, please go down into the hole."

You feel very excited and a bit nervous. What amazing things could be down there? Will you have to do a test to get into a House? Fight a monster perhaps? Fight this mysterious singing Percy?

You carefully go down the steps into the darkness. You descend until all you can see above you is a circle of light and the noise of the hall fades to nothing.

"Hello? Percy?"

No answer.

Then: "Coo coo come closer, so I can see you better!"

The voice emerging from the blackness in front of you has a strange high pitched musical quality to it. Fear closes your throat and you are rooted to the spot. Then... ouch! Something has bitten you on the bum! You see a small spider dropping off your robes and scurrying away into the darkness.

The pain in your bum gets you moving. You slowly walk forwards.

As you get closer you can just make out two round yellow eyes staring back at you, and between them a large... beak? Is Percy some kind of monster? It doesn't look or sound dangerous...

Your eyes adjust to the dark and you realise that you are staring at a gigantic pigeon, that's as tall as you are, even sitting down.

"Who are you?" you ask.

"Coo coo I'm Percy the Picking Pigeon and I will choose your house for you coo coo! Look into my eyes Arthur, look into my eyes..."

You stare into the yellow eyes of the pigeon which seem to grow until they become the entire world.

"Coo coo, well, you are brave Arthur to come here first," says Percy. "Ambitious perhaps, and clever too. You could be a Lionpaw fighting for the truth. Or a Snakefang rising to the top. Or a Ravenwing mastering the secrets of the universe. But certainly not a cowardly Hedgehog House. Coo coo."

As Percy the Picking Pigeon probes your mind, you concentrate with all your being, repeating to yourself:

............................................................

1. Lionpaw Lionpaw, please let it be Lionpaw! ~ Go to number 15

2. Ravenwing, I must go into Ravenwing House! ~ Go to number 23

3. Snakefang, Snakefang is where I belong! ~ Go to number 192

8.
Crash landing at Hogsnorts

"Hey, I'm bored, just sitting here" Robert says suddenly. "I'm going to fly this car myself."

"Are you sure that's a good idea?" you say. "Your Dad enchanted the car to fly all the way to Hogsnorts. I mean, do you know the way?"

"How hard can it be?" says Robert, getting out his wand. "We just follow the train. Autopilotus stoppus!"

With that, the car gave a little cough and a splutter, went silent, and gently started a death dive to the ground far below.

"Aaaargh Robert, what have you done?!" yells Aaron. "Turn it back on!!"

"Hmmm which one is the 'engine on' button?" muses Robert as the car bursts downwards through the clouds, the shrieking wind all around them.

You are dry mouthed with fear, trying desperately not to scream as Robert calmly tries the different buttons on the car dashboard.

"Not this one... no... not that one either... Aha! There we go!" the car engine starts again, and the vehicle begins to spiral crazily as Robert pulls hard on the steering wheel to bring it back under control.

Just then you see something so amazing it makes you forget even your impending splatter on the ground below.

A mile or two away a colossal stone building stands at the top of a grassy hill. Towers sprout from the building like mushrooms, spiralling outwards at crazy angles. The roofs are studded with battlements. The walls are encrusted with beautiful stained glass windows. And over it all hangs a faint golden glow of pure magic. Hogsnorts School of Magic.

"Watch out Robert, flying monkeys below!" shouts out Alex.

You tear your eyes away from the building. Unbelievably Alex is right: a flock of flying monkeys is directly in your path. It is hard to make out but the flying monkeys appear to be carrying people...

The monkeys scatter in all directions as the car zooms through the middle of them, and you just have time to make out that each pair of flying monkeys is carrying a young witch or wizard. You realise that for some insane reason the flying monkeys are transporting the children to the school.

"Sorry!" shouts Robert out of the window at the monkeys, still wrestling with the steering wheel.

He just manages to bring it under control in time to make a very bumpy landing on the Hogsnorts school lawn.

You lean back in the car, your breath coming in short panicky bursts. You can't quite believe that you are still alive. Robert, Alex and Aaron seem amazingly unaffected by their near fatal driving experiment.

"Ok boys, let's get out of here before the Profs catch us!" shouts Robert.

All of you tumble out of the car, grab your stuff and make a run for the nearest entrance to Hogsnorts, your rubbery legs just about managing to propel you along.

You dash into the school and follow Robert, Alex and Aaron into the school hall to sit down with the other children. Sitting down at a wooden bench on the table reserved for first year students, you feel you are a long way from Leeds railway station.

............................................................

1. Catch your breath and wait to see what happens next ~ Go to number 53

9.
The invitation

You rip open the envelope and pull out an ancient looking piece of parchment.

At the top it says Hogsnorts School of Magic.

A school of magic? you think. What the...? Maybe this is junk mail after all. You carry on reading...

.........................................

Dear Arthur,

I am delighted to inform you that you have been selected to attend Hogsnorts School of Magic. You have hidden but powerful magical abilities :-)

As a new student you will need to bring the following items on your first day:

- a magic wand
- a wizard's robe and hat
- a year-1 spellbook

They can be purchased from the magical shops located on the magical street Hippoto Mews, London, just behind Gutter Lane.

Term will start on 1 September. Please come to Leeds Railway Station, from where the Hogsnorts Express will depart at 9.34 precisely.

Yours resplendently,
Zebediah Slumblebore
Headmaster
Hogsnorts School

P.S. Remember the secret code to enter Hippoto Mews is: TAP TAP TAP... TAP.

P.P.S. Note that due to the alarming recent magical disturbances at the school, the parents of all pupils are required to sign a "child's demise liability waiver" before arriving at Hogsnorts.

.........................................

You feel your blood prickle to the surface of your skin. Can this be real? Do you really have hidden powerful magic abilities? Maybe this is some big mistake? Or worse - a joke.

But then... there have been times where strange things have occurred without you knowing why.

Like that time you fell out of the apple tree in your cousin's house, but instead of falling down you floated down like a leaf, and gently landed on the ground.

Or that time you played hide and seek and wished that you could make yourself invisible and no-one could find you even though you were just hiding under the kitchen table and it should have been easy.

And the fact that every now and again you have a conversation with a spider and you can understand what they are saying.

A slow smile spreads across your face. It must be true!

You are going to magic school.

............................................................

1. Go and buy your wizarding things ~ Go to number 40

10.
A new friend?

It will be good to get to know someone you might be going to school with, perhaps he can tell you what it's like.

"Hello" you say to the boy. "I'm Arthur. Are you going to Hogsnorts?"

The boy looks up at you. "Yep I'm going to Hogsnorts. Did you know that they have the biggest magical library in the country?"

"No..." you say. You wonder how many other magical libraries there are in the country.

"Anyway I'm Daniel Colliers-Wood. And this is my little brother Robin Colliers-Wood."

You notice another boy sitting just round the next bookshelf from Daniel, reading a comic book about a policeman with the body of a man and the head of a dog.

"Daniel," you ask "Do you know much about Hogsnorts? What it's like when you get there I mean?"

"Yes, I've read all about it. Well the main thing to know is that there are four "houses" or teams you could call them. The best house is Ravenwing house, that's where I want to go, Ravenwing House has that big library I told you about. The Ravenwings love studying. The other houses are Lion House for the brave, Snakefang House for the powerful, and Hedgehog House for the prickly. You will probably be in Hedgehog House."

"No I won't!" you protest automatically.

"Alright Mr Prickles," says Daniel. "I was just trying to wind you up. Anyway no one really knows which house they will be in until they get to Hogsnorts."

"I want to go to Snakefang house, that would be so cool!" pipes up Daniel's younger brother Robin.

"Listen young man - Daniel was it?" your mum interrupts "I'm sure Arthur will be in Lion House, he is a very brave boy. Do you remember Arthur when you got stung by a wasp and you didn't even cry?"

"Mu-um!" you complain. Turning back to Daniel: "Anyway Daniel, see you around."

"Bye bye Arthur" says Daniel picking up his book.

............................................................

1. Look for your a spell book ~ Go to number 65

Snako Malboy

"Hello," you say to the boy "my name's Arthur Otley and I'm going to Hogsnorts. Who are you?"

The boy does his sneering smile at you again.

"Snako Malboy. Yes I too am going to Hogsnorts. My father went to Hogsnorts. My grandfather went to Hogsnorts. So did his father and so on up to 72 generations and the founding of the school. Sylvester Snake - yes the Sylvester Snake is my direct ancestor. And my mother and their mothers too. So yes I am going to Hogsnorts."

"Who is Sylvester Snake?"

"Sylvester Snake is only the founder of Snake House, duh! The best house in the school. I'm going to be in Snake House. Snake House is for the really powerful wizards, like I will be one day. You will be in Hedgehog House I suppose."

"I haven't decided yet" you reply.

"Well if you want to be Snake House like me you have to be strong and ruthless. Snake House rules yah sssssssss!"

Snako Malboy stuck his tongue in and out of his mouth like a snake and hissed - not an easy thing to do at the same time. You are impressed.

At that point the magic tape measure is finished with Snako and moves over to you.

12.
Arriving in Hognsorts

"Yaaargh!" you exclaim as the ground drops away beneath you. You have never travelled by flying monkey before and it's an unnerving experience, not helped by the fact that the monkeys are screeching and chattering constantly. They seem to be having an excellent time.

But then something else makes you forget about the ever growing drop to the ground, about the grasping fingers of the winged monkey on either side: Hogsnorts.

A mile or two away you see a colossal stone building at the top of a grassy hill. Towers sprout from the building like mushrooms, spiralling outwards at crazy angles. The roofs are studded with battlements. The walls are encrusted with beautiful stained glass windows. And over it all hangs a faint golden glow of pure magic. Hogsnorts School of Magic.

But you have no time to take in the view. A loud car horn honk comes from the clouds above you. You twist your head up to see...

...a dark blue ford fiesta corkscrewing through the sky, heading straight for the troupe of winged monkeys! A flying car - amazing! you think, momentarily forgetting you are about to be flown over.

Luckily nothing is more agile than a flying monkey and the primates pirouette away from the barely controlled flying vehicle as it zooms through the middle of them. From the window of the car you hear a faint cry of "sorry!" as the monkeys chatter with rage.

The car hurtles off towards Hogsnorts and you can just make out a bumpy but survivable crash landing and three small figures running out of the car towards the school. The car turns round and flies off through the sky.

The rest of the flight is comparatively uneventful.

The monkeys soar in through an open window of the Hogsnorts Great Hall and gently set you down on a wooden bench at a table reserved for first year students. You feel you are a long way from Leeds railway station.

............................................................

1. Try to recover your composure and wait to see what happens next ~ Go to number 53

13.
House picking

You get to your feet slowly and then pretend to tie your shoe lace as the other first years get in line. Then you join the back of the queue. By watching what happens to someone else, you can plan your next move.

"Aaron Bleezeley," says Slumblebore at last, "please go down into the hole."

Aaron looks very nervous as he slowly walks forward towards the hole, his red hair peeking out from under his wizard hat.

Better him than me you think.

He goes down the wooden steps into the darkness, and then there is silence. All the students are holding their breath, waiting to see when - if! - Aaron will emerge again. You are so nervous you can feel sweat trickle down your back.

Then, after what seems like an age, you see Aaron's pointy hat, then head, then body come up out of the hole. He's ok! you are relieved to see, although he looks a bit dazed.

In his hands, for some unknown reason, he is holding a large, beautiful, red and gold striped egg. The colours of Lionpaw House!

Professor Slumblebore sees the egg and shouts out to the hall: "Aaron Bleezeley, Lionpaw House!"

A great cheer comes from the Lionpaw table, and Aaron walks over to them, a huge grin on his face. Two other red heads, his brothers Robert and Alex, clap him on the back.

After Aaron the other children slowly go down... and then return, each with an egg in the colours of their house.

"Snako Malboy, Snakefang House!" shouts Slumblebore as Snako emerges with a green and silver egg.

"Daniel Colliers-Wood, Ravenwing House!" Daniel carefully holds his blue and copper coloured egg as he happily walks over to the Ravenwing table.

"Kensley Potato, Hedgehog House!" Kensley clutches a nondescript brown egg and shuffles over to the other Hoggers.

Now finally there is only you left.

"Arthur Otley" says Slumblebore looking at you with a twinkle in his eye that you don't trust one bit, "please go down the hole."

............................................................

1. There's no putting it off any longer. You descend into the hole. ~ Go to number 20

14.
The Bleezeleys

You walk over to the family of red haired wizards on the other side of the station.

"Excuse me" you ask, "are you wizards?"

The children look a bit shifty and say nothing, while the Dad answers for them: "Wizards? No we're err... on our way to a fancy dress party. Why do you want to know anyway?"

"I'm trying to find the train to Hogsnorts but I don't know where it is, and it is almost time for the train to leave!"

"Ah I see," says the mum, "that's the train we want too. Yes we are wizards but we try to keep it quiet, you know."

"Mum!" interrupts one of the red haired children, "now we are definitely going to miss the train!"

"We're going to miss the train?" you ask. "Does that mean that we can't get to Hogsnorts now?"

"Don't worry young man" says the Dad. "Where there's a wizard there's a way, eh? But first we should introduce ourselves. We are the Bleezeley family:

"This is Aaron, who is going to Hogsnorts for the first time this year." (The shortest red haired boy gives you a small wave.)

"These two are Alex and Robert. They are in year 4" (Alex and Robert nod their heads at you.)

"I'm Mr Bleezeley and this is Mrs Bleezeley." (Mrs Bleezeley gives you a cheery thumbs up.)

"Hello everyone," you say. "My name is Arthur Otley and I just discovered I was a wizard a few days ago. I'm a first year. This is my dad and my younger brother Evan" (Your dad and Evan have just walked up.)

"Of course you're a wizard Arthur," said the mum, "You've got red hair like us! Most people with red hair have at least a bit of magic in them and I can see that you've got more than most!"

You are pleased to hear Mrs Bleezeley say this, but still feel worried about the train.

"But M Bleezeley, Mrs Bleezeley, what about the train? How are we going to get to Hogsnorts?" you ask.

Mr Bleezeley taps his nose conspiratorially. "Follow me."

You:

............................................................

1. Follow Mr Bleezeley, even though he does seem a bit of an odd fish ~ Go to number 27

15.
Picked for Lionpaw

Lionpaw, Lionpaw please let it be Lionpaw! you say to yourself over and over again.

Coo coo are you sure it's Lionpaw? asks Percy the pigeon, speaking directly into your mind now.

Yes yes, I'm sure. Not a Snakefang bully, not a brainbox Ravenwing, not a boring old Hedgehog. Lionpaw please, please!

Coo coo as you wish young Arthur, speaks Percy into your brain.

Slowly the great yellow eyes shrink to normal size and you are just staring at a regular giant talking pigeon again.

Percy waddles over to the centre of the hole where the light from the hall shines down. He looks old and you wonder how long he has been doing this. For decades, centuries even?

He settles down on the floor, coos once or twice and then waddles back into the darkness at the edge of the hole that is his home, leaving right in the centre a beautiful egg.

The egg is covered in red and gold stripes. The colours of Lionpaw House!

Your heart pounding with excitement you pick up the egg and slowly walk back up the wooden stairs to the noise and light of the Hogsnorts Great Hall.

As you emerge out of the pigeon hole, Slumblebore sees your egg and shouts: "Arthur Otley, Lionpaw House!"

............................................................

1. You walk over to the Lionpaw House table, holding your egg aloft. ~ Go to number 43

16.
Back on the street

Back on Hippoto Mews, the crowds of witches and wizards seem even thicker.

When a small child magician walks past because the pointy end of their hat is about the same height as your face and when one of them turns round quickly, it could easily poke your eye out if you are not careful.

But this doesn't really bother you, it's so exciting to be around real magicians!

"Do you feel better after some fresh air Arthur?" asks your mum. "We still need to get your spell book before you can go to Hogsnorts. Come on, let's go back and see if we can figure out that puzzle"

............................................................

1. Go to Watertomes to get a spellbook ~ Go to number 17

17.
Watertomes

Now you have your robes and your wand it will be nice to have some spells to cast, you decide and head towards Watertomes bookshop, your mum following behind you.

As you walk down the street you overhear all sorts of curious and wonderful snatches of conversation:

"...I put in the eye of newt and you'll never guess what happened..."

"....then my hat blew off into a swamp..."

"...his own fault he never should have summoned that demon..."

Watertomes is a small shop with an old wooden door and cramped dusty windows. You push the door open with a creak and enter hesitantly.

The inside is enormous: by some magic it is many times bigger than the outside. Brightly lit bookshelves stretch away from you to the left and right.

You see a boy with straight brown hair, about your age sitting on the floor, reading a book. He looks up at you as you walk in.

Do you:

............................................................

1. Speak to the boy, maybe he is going to Hogsnorts too ~ Go to number 30

2. Look for your spell book, you've got no time to waste with chit chat ~ Go to number 56

18.
The letters keep coming

"Give me my letter!" you shout, as you leap towards your Dad, arms outstretched.

You just catch a glimpse of your Dad's look of surprise, before tripping on some of Evan's lego and landing flat on your back.

"Are you alright Arthur?" asks your Dad.

"Hnngh. Fine." you reply looking up at him from the floor.

"Good!" says Dad, tearing up the letter into tiny shreds as he talks. "Now let's put this junk mail in the bin. You know you really shouldn't get so worked up about it, I cleaned out our gutters just last month."

You close your eyes. Next time you will need to do better. But will there be a next time?

...

The next morning, just as the night is turning into day, you tiptoe carefully down the stairs before anyone else is awake. You position yourself at the front door, open the letter box and peep outside. No sign of the postman just yet.

You settle down to wait.

After 30 minutes... still no postman.

After 1 hour... no postman.

After 1 hour and 10 minutes... Dad walks downstairs.

"What are you doing down there Arthur?" he asks.

"Nothing, you reply," standing up quickly. "I was just err... was just.."

Just then there is a gentle thud behind you as the now familiar letter falls to the floor.

Both you and your Dad bend down at the same time to pick it up.

Do you say:

............................................................

1. "Aha! Now I've got finally got it!" Then dash off with the letter. ~ Go to number 50

2. "You have it Dad, I was just going to put it in the recycling bin anyway." ~ Go to number 22

19.
Your first spell book

"I've turned your name into the number 19" you tell Bob.

"Well done! You've transformed my name into a number... and that number into your story. I can sense that you will be a powerful wizard one day."

Bob hands you the red spell book. It is even heavier than it looks and feels as if it is vibrating very slightly, as if it is somehow... alive.

"Thank you" you whisper, as you hold on tightly to your very first magical spell book.

"Well done Arthur!" says your Mum as you walk out of the door together, "That was very clever! And you saved us 14 Frigates! Now let's get your wand!"

............................................................

1. You go to Wally Wanderful Wand shop to get your wand ~ Go to number 52

20.
Pigeon holed

With a lump of fear in your throat you slowly walk down the wooden steps that take you deep down into the dark hole.

What will you find down there? Everyone else emerged unscathed so it can't be dangerous can it? But will it be painful? What is this strange singing Percy creature?

You descend until all you can see above you is a circle of light and the noise of the hall fades to nothing.

"Hello? Percy?"

No answer.

Then: "Coo coo come closer, so I can see you better!"

The voice emerging from the blackness in front of you has a strange high pitched musical quality to it. Fear closes your throat and you are rooted to the spot. Then... ouch! Something has bitten you on the bum! You see a small spider dropping off your robes and scurrying away into the darkness.

The pain in your bum gets you moving.

You slowly walk forwards wishing you could run back up the wooden steps to the safety of the hall above.

As you get closer you can just make out two round yellow eyes staring back at you, and between them a large... beak? Is Percy some kind of monster? Is he going to leap out at you and attack?

Your eyes adjust to the dark and you realise that you are staring at a gigantic pigeon, that's as tall as you are even sitting down.

"Who are you?" you ask.

"Coo coo I'm Percy the Picking Pigeon and I will choose your house for you coo coo! Look into my eyes Arthur, look into my eyes..."

You stare into the yellow eyes of the pigeon which seem to grow until they become the entire world.

"Coo coo well, you're cowardly Arthur, coming here last in the line," says Percy. "Maybe Hedgehog House is the one for you. Or maybe you are just a bit sneaky - and Snakefang House is best? Or perhaps hanging around last was a clever ploy? It does show that you can plan ahead, so Ravenwing maybe? But certainly not brave Lionpaw. Coo coo."

As Percy the Picking Pigeon probes your mind, you concentrate with all your being, repeating to yourself:

............................................................

1. Hedgehog House, Hedgehog House! I don't want any trouble, please let it be Hedgehog! ~ Go to number 59

2. Snakefang, Snakefang is where I belong! ~ Go to number 192

3. Ravenwing, I must go into Ravenwing House! ~ Go to number 23

21.
A new friend?

It will be good to get to know someone you might be going to school with, perhaps he can tell you what it's like.

"Hello" you say to the boy. "I'm Arthur. Are you going to Hogsnorts?"

The boy looks up at you. "Yep I'm going to Hogsnorts. Did you know that they have the biggest magical library in the country?"

"No..." you say. You wonder how many other magical libraries there are in the country.

"Anyway I'm Daniel Colliers-Wood. And this is my little brother Robin Colliers-Wood."

You notice another boy sitting just round the next bookshelf from Daniel, reading a comic book about a policeman with the body of a man and the head of a dog.

"Daniel," you ask "Do you know much about Hogsnorts? What it's like when you get there I mean?"

"Yes, I've read all about it. Well the main thing to know is that there are four "houses" or teams you could call them. The best house is Ravenwing house, that's where I want to go, Ravenwing House has that big library I told you about. The Ravenwings love studying. The other houses are Lion House for the brave, Snakefang House for the powerful, and Hedgehog House for the prickly. You will probably be in Hedgehog House."

"No I won't!" you protest automatically.

"Alright Mr Prickles," says Daniel. "I was just trying to wind you up. Anyway no one really knows which house they will be in until they get to Hogsnorts."

"I want to go to Snakefang house, that would be so cool!" pipes up Daniel's younger brother Robin.

"Listen young man - Daniel was it?" your mum interrupts "I'm sure Arthur will be in Lion House, he is a very brave boy. Do you remember Arthur when you got stung by a wasp and you didn't even cry?"

"Mu-um!" you complain. Turning back to Daniel: "Anyway Daniel, see you around."

"Bye bye Arthur" says Daniel picking up his book.

............................................................

1. Look for your a spell book ~ Go to number 4

22.
Just going to put it in the bin...

23.
Picked for Ravenwing

Ravenwing, make it Ravenwing please...! you wish fervently.

Coo coo are you sure it's Ravenwing? asks Percy the pigeon, speaking directly into your mind now.

Yes I'm absolutely certain. Not a slimey Snakefang, not a meathead Lionpaw, not a slow old Hedgehog. It must be Ravenwing!

Coo coo as you wish young Arthur, speaks Percy into your brain.

Slowly the great yellow eyes shrink to normal size and you are just staring at a regular giant talking pigeon again.

Percy waddles over to the centre of the hole where the light from the hall shines down. He looks old and you wonder how long he has been doing this. For decades? Centuries even?

The giant pigeon settles down on the floor, and coos once or twice. He then stands up slowly and waddles back into the darkness at the edge of the hole that is his home. On the floor he has laid a large and beautiful egg.

The egg is covered in blue and copper coloured stripes. The colours of Ravenwing House!

Your heart pounding with excitement, you pick up the egg and slowly walk back up the wooden stairs to the noise and light of the Hogsnorts Great Hall.

As you emerge out of the pigeon hole, Slumblebore sees your egg and shouts: "Arthur Otley, Ravenwing House!"

............................................................

1. You walk over to the Ravenwing House table, holding your egg aloft. ~ Go to number 45

25.
Measuring up

"Toast will burn and porridge bubble, measure this kid and save me the trouble!" shrieked witch number 2.

The incantation complete, the magic tape measure zooms around your body like a whirlwind, measuring everything from your inside leg measurement, to the distance between your nostrils, to the length of your ear lobes.

At the same time a magic biro is writing down all these measurements on a notepad.

After a few minutes, in which you are frightened to move in case the tape measure accidentally shoots up your nose, the tape neatly rolls itself up and lands on a table.

Witch number 2 looks carefully at the scribbled numbers in the notepad and counts on her fingers.

She looks up at her sister and yells: "Small!"

As witch number 1 scuttles off to get a small robe for you, your Mum, who has been standing quietly to one side clears her throat.

"Ahem, how much do these robes cost? I didn't see any prices when we came in the shop," says your Mum.

"11 Golden Frigates and not an Acorn less!" replies the witch.

"11 Golden Frigates - how much is that in pounds?" asks your Mum.

"Pounds? Oh no deary, we only take wizard money in this shop."

"Never mind Mum," you say, "I'm sure we could just make the robes ourselves from some black material..."

Snako Malboy snorts and rolls his eyes.

"Wait!" exclaims the witch, "We don't take pounds but we do offer wagers."

"Ok... can we do a wager and not pay anything?" asks your mum.

"I wager you can't guess my age," says the witch. "If you can, you can keep the robe and get a free hat. If you fail you will stay in this shop for ever!"

"I'll do it" you say bravely, "but I will need a clue."

"How old are you boy?" asks the witch.

"I'm ten years old."

"Here's your clue. In ten years, if you double your age then, and then double it again, that will be my age then. But how old am I, right now?"

............................................................

1. Turn to the number that is the age of the witch ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. This wager is too risky, you decide to get your wand instead ~ Go to number 64

3. That witch could be any age up to a thousand! You decide to get your year 1 spellbook instead ~ Go to number 37

26.
Watertomes

Now you look the part, it will be nice to be able to do a bit of magic! You head towards Watertomes bookshop, your mum following behind you.

"...I put in the eye of newt and you'll never guess what happened..."

"....then my hat blew off into a swamp..."

"...his own fault he never should have summoned that demon..."

Watertomes is a small shop with an old wooden door and cramped dusty windows. You push the door open with a creak and enter hesitantly.

The inside is enormous: by some magic it is many times bigger than the outside. Brightly lit bookshelves stretch away from you to the left and right.

27.
The flying car

Mr Bleezeley gives his little blue car a proud tap on the bonnet. "She may not be the Hogsnorts Express," he says, "but this fine car will have you there in a jiffy, with a fair wind."

You are in the station carpark, all standing next to the Bleezeleys' car.

"Dad's enchanted the car to be able to fly," explains Aaron Bleezeley, "so in theory we should be able to follow the train from above and get to Hogsnorts that way."

"There's just one problem though Dad," says Robert Bleezeley, the oldest child. "There's only room for four people in this car. If me, Alex, Aaron and also Arthur are going there's no room for you or Mum. We won't all fit."

"Don't worry," says Mr Bleezeley, "I'll just cast a spell on the sat nav to fly you there automatically, and then you can go by yourselves. Mum and I will stay here. Come on, in you get boys!"

Robert and Alex get in the front seats and you and Aaron in the back.

Mr Bleezeley draws his magic wand, and gently raps the windscreen: "Fly, fly, fly up high, get to Hogsnorts through the sky."

He lowers his wand and smiles at them. "That should do the trick. Stand back everyone."

"Bye bye Arthur!" shout your Dad and Evan, as the car engine splutters into life. "Good luck!"

"Bye bye Dad, bye bye Evan!" you reply as the car starts moving forward and upward into the sky. "See you later!"

You watch the ground drop away beneath you in amazement as the car roars through the air.

Turning to the boys in the car with you: Aaron, Alex and Robert you:

............................................................

1. Share out your chocolate treats among your new friends ~ Go to number 33

28.
On the Hogsnorts Express

Neither the boy from the robe shop nor the girl from the spell book shop seemed that friendly when you met them before, so you decide to try another carriage.

Waving goodbye to your Dad and brother you run down the platform and leap into a carriage just as the doors are closing.

There are lots of children wearing wizard and witch outfits, some older, some younger. Most children are listening to headphones and playing with their phones and one or two are reading a book.

You spot a spare seat next to an unassuming young witch about your age and sit down next to her.

"Hello," you say, keen to make friends. "I'm Arthur Otley, what's your name?"

"Kensley Potato," comes back the quiet reply. "I'm a first year."

"So am I! Do you know what House you want to be in, when we get to Hogsnorts?"

A look of defiance flashes in Kensley's eyes.

"I know which houses I don't want to be in. I don't want to be Snakefang House, trying to take over the world. I don't want to be in Ravenwing House, thinking you're so much cleverer than everyone else. And I don't want to be in Lionpaw House, always right all the time and thumping anyone who is wrong."

"You want to be in Hedgehog House," you say, not quite as a question.

"Yes I do! All the other Houses tease the Hoggers for being boring, but they're not actually. They're not fighting, they're not power hungry, they're not clever clogs, they are just normal. Just normal, ordinary wizards trying to get through the term without getting our hats blasted off by a stray magic spell. And if you call that boring well then I want to be boring, thank you very much."

It does sound a bit boring, you think, but don't say anything. Instead you offer Kensley a Smarty from your sweet collection. She happily shares them with you and is quite excited when you choose a brown Smarty.

"Arthur, did you realise that brown is the colour of Hedgehog House? Maybe this is a sign that you will be in Hedgehog House too? Wouldn't you like that?"

"Well maybe. I don't want a stray spell blasting my hat off, I guess."

"Of course you don't," says Kensley. "That's why you need to keep your head down with the Hoggers - we call ourselves Hoggers in Hedgehog House."

While you are talking the train chugs into daylight, and the railway tracks emerge from the dark tunnel out into the countryside.

You twist in your seat to peer out of the window. As far as you can see there are rolling hills covered in pine trees. In the distance, craggy mountains emerge, their tops clouded in mist. It looks like nowhere you have ever seen before, except perhaps in the illustrations to one of your favourite books, The Hobbit.

You feel like you have entered a magical new land and your adventure has truly begun.

A magically amplified voice interrupts your daydreams of dwarves and dragons, trolls and treasure.

"Train terminates here. All change please, all change. Mind the gap."

Hogsnorts station! This is it. You've arrived.

............................................................

1. Alight from the train ~ Go to number 66

29.
A visit to Spellwitches

With your magic wand clasped tightly in your hand, you decide that you need to look like a wizard too.

The shop has large storefront windows. Inside the windows manikins have been arranged wearing black witch and wizard robes. The manikins are in a variety of action poses, such as just about to cast a spell, or frozen running away from a dragon.

But they have clearly been magically enchanted because every now and again one of the manikins will change their position to something else, moving smoothly with astonishing realism. You look at the manikins carefully - they really are amazingly life-like, even down to the expressions of surprise on their faces.

You and your mum make a little bell dingle as you push open the door.

In front of you are racks and racks of wizard robes, all black. Above some racks a sign says 'small', above others it says 'medium', and others 'large'.

Shelves cover the walls and the shelves are covered in pointy black hats.

"May I help you at all?"

You and your mum both jump - a witch with a totally green face leaps out from behind a rack of black robes just in front of you.

"Just browsing are you?"

You jump again as another witch, looking identical to the first, pops out from a rack of clothes behind you.

"Aargh!" you exclaim. You take a breath and calm yourself and clear your throat.

"Robes?" you squeak "For Hogsnorts?"

"You are in the right place my little dear" said green witch number 1. "Let's see how you measure up!"

The two witches take you to a side room where a magic tape measure is already taking the measurements of a pale looking boy about your age.

The boy looks at you with an expression that could either be a sneer or a smile, you can't quite be sure.

31.
Down the toilet

You decide to go to the toilet - apart from anything else you do feel a bit nervous and it is a good idea to have a wee before you get on the train.

As you approach the station toilets you look down and are surprised to see five spiders walking in a line one after the other towards the disabled loo. Reasoning that this is not typical behaviour for spiders, and that anything weird might well be magical, you walk in the same direction.

Your reasoning is correct. As you approach the disabled toilet you are excited to see that the door is outlined in a magical golden glow. This must be the right place!

You push open the door and you, your Dad and Evan go inside. Inside you see... just a normal toilet.

You look around for some sort of a clue but apart from a few discarded segments of toilet paper on the floor everything looks exactly as it should. Even the spiders are nowhere to be seen.

"Well it seems like this is a dead end Arthur, but you might as well do a wee now we're here." proposes Dad.

36.
Wanderful Wands

You decide to visit Wally's Wanderful Wands shop next. Now that you have your spellbook you want to get your hands on a wand as soon as possible and start doing some magic.

The sign above Wally's shop is a giant wand dangling from a chain above the shop door. It swings gently to and fro even though there is no breeze to speak of, and little crackles of electric-gold magic arc over its surface.

You can't help thinking that this wand must also double up as Wally's security system.

With a nervous glance upwards you and your Mum enter the shop.

The inside is sparklingly clean and glass cabinets are artfully arranged around the shop. Each cabinet contains three or four magic wands, resting on little red cushions with gold tassles. It all looks very expensive.

"Arthur are you sure this is the only wand shop?" asks your mum. "Perhaps there is another one that is not quite so err... so un..."

"Welcome!" a smooth rich voice startles them from the back of the room. "Welcome to Wally's Wanderful Wand shop! And madam I can assure you that this is the only wand shop in Hippoto Mews. But fear not I'm sure we can find a wand that is the perfect match for young Arthur."

"How did you know my name?" you ask in surprise.

"One of the many branches of magic in which I am an expert, young Arthur, is mind reading. Just by looking into your eyes I can see the entire contents of your brain. I can also do it by looking in your ears, in your mouth, up your nose... any hole works to tell the truth. But I usually prefer the eyes. Also your Mum called you Arthur when you entered my shop."

"And you are Wally I suppose?" says your Mum.

"I am indeed, dear madam. Did you divine this from looking in my ear hole? Remarkable!"

"No I figured it out when you said this was your shop."

"Quite so. We are all mind-readers to some degree."

"Mr Wally" you interrupt "can I have a wand please?"

"No you cannot have a wand Arthur. But what you can have is the wand. Every wand is unique! You are unique! You require the exact match for your particular thaumaturgical resonance. Your thaumaturgic twin as it were. The most powerful - the only! - tool you will ever need as a magician."

"That sounds nice," says your Mum, "but we don't want anything too fancy. The thing is we don't have much, or in fact any, wizard money. Frigates I mean."

"The wand is of course priceless. I do offer a 10% discount for Hogsnorts' students in their first year. But for you I will increase this discount to 100% if - if! - Arthur and I can establish a true connection of minds, and I can see that you Arthur are a worthy wandholder."

"A 100% discount you say? That's a good deal. Arthur see if you can connect up your mind with Wally's love." your Mum suggests.

Wally crouches down in front of you and holds your ears gently but firmly forcing you to look deep into his blue grey eyes. At first nothing happens. But after just a few moments you get the strange sensation of being pulled towards his eyeballs; his black pupils feel like they are dragging you inwards.

"Good Arthur, very good!" says Wally. "I believe that the magical connection between our minds is now established, and astonishingly quickly too! You must have deep reserves of magic.

"Arthur I need you to think of a number. If I can read your mind and tell you the number you were thinking of this will be proof that the magical mind connection is working properly.

"First I need you to think of a number between 1 and 10. But don't tell me what it is! Have you got one?"

You think of a number and nod your head.

"Now" says Wally, "I need you to multiply this number by 9. 9 is a number with strong magical properties" he explains.

You multiply your number by 9.

"The next step" he says, "is to split your answer into the two digits and add those two digits together. For example if your answer is 13 (and I know it is not!) then you would split it into 1 and 3, then add that 1 and 3 together, so 1 + 3 = 4.

"Ok" you say as you do the sum in your head.

"Now take that answer and multiply it by 9. Can you do that?"

"Yes" you reply.

"Now turn to that number! And we will see if our minds are connected."

............................................................

1. Turn to the number that you have thought of ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. You are not in the mood for mindreading, go to Spellwitches instead ~ Go to number 58

"....then my hat blew off into a swamp..."

"...his own fault he never should have summoned that demon..."

Watertomes is a small shop with an old wooden door and cramped dusty windows. You push the door open with a creak and enter hesitantly.

The inside is enormous: by some magic it is many times bigger than the outside. Brightly lit bookshelves stretch away from you to the left and right.

You see a boy with straight brown hair, about your age sitting on the floor, reading a book. He looks up at you as you walk in.

38.
A visit to Spellwitches

If you are going to be a wizard you need to look the part. You decide to visit Spellwitches to get your robes first.

The shop has large storefront windows. Inside the windows manikins have been arranged wearing black witch and wizard robes. The manikins are in a variety of action poses, such as just about to cast a spell, or frozen running away from a dragon.

But they have clearly been magically enchanted because every now and again one of the manikins will change their position to something else, moving smoothly with astonishing realism. You look at the manikins carefully - they really are amazingly life-like, even down to the expressions of surprise on their faces.

You and your mum make a little bell dingle as you push open the door.

In front of you are racks and racks of wizard robes, all black. Above some racks a sign says 'small', above others it says 'medium', and others 'large'.

Shelves cover the walls and the shelves are covered in pointy black hats.

"May I help you at all?"

You and your mum both jump - a witch with a totally green face leaps out from behind a rack of black robes just in front of you.

"Just browsing are you?"

You jump again as another witch, looking identical to the first, pops out from a rack of clothes behind you.

"Aargh!" you exclaim. You take a breath and calm yourself and clear your throat.

"Robes?" you squeak "For Hogsnorts?"

"You are in the right place my little dear" said green witch number 1. "Let's see how you measure up!"

The two witches take you to a side room where a magic tape measure is already taking the measurements of a pale looking boy about your age.

The boy looks at you with an expression that could either be a sneer or a smile, you can't quite be sure.

............................................................

39.
Where is the Hogsnort's Express?

You check your rucksack for the one hundredth time. Carefully folded wizard robes: check. Year one spellbook: check. One magic wand: check. Spare pair of socks: check.

You've got everything you need to go to the Hogsnorts school of wizardry!

The only thing you need to figure out now is how to get there.

You are waiting by the ticket barriers at Leeds railway station with your brother Evan and your Dad. Your Dad is checking his watch and looking up at the train departure board anxiously.

"Arthur" he says, "it is ten minutes until the train is supposed to leave and I can't see Hognsorts on the departure board anywhere. Do you know where we are supposed to go?"

"On the letter it just says: the train will depart at 9.34 precisely from Leeds railway station. But it doesn't say where in Leeds railway station."

Just then you notice something strange. One of the ticket inspectors by the ticket barriers is wearing a pointy black hat and sun glasses. It could just be coincidence or maybe he knows how to find the magic train!

"Come on Evan, Dad," you say and walk over to talk to the ticket inspector.

"Excuse me," you ask "do you know where we can find the Hogsnorts Express?"

The ticket inspector turns to look straight at you, and removes his sun glasses. You are startled to see that his eyes are completely white with no visible pupil at all. His voice comes out as a rasp:

"The Express you seek,
Will leave off-peak,
With a puff of steam and a piercing shriek.
But first you need to take a leak."

He then replaces his sun glasses, turns away from you and doesn't say another word.

"It's a riddle!" you exclaim. "The train will leave off-peak - yes that makes sense it will leave just after 9.30. With a puff of steam and a piercing shriek - that must mean it is a steam train with a whistle. But what does the last part about taking a leak mean?"

"I think he is telling you to go to the toilet before you get on the train" says Dad. "A last wee: very sensible advice."

Just then you see an odd looking family dashing through the station. The two adults are puffing and out of breath and the three children are wearing wizard robes!"

Do you:

............................................................

1. Visit the toilet to see if you can unravel the ticket inspectors riddle. ~ Go to number 31

2. Go and talk to the odd looking family, perhaps they can just tell you where the train is without any silly puzzles. ~ Go to number 14

"Hippoto Mews? Well I can't see it on the map on my phone." said Mum.

You and your mum have come to a dead end, just a brick wall at the end of a street. You are sure that you have followed the instructions correctly and Hippoto Mews should be just here. But... there's nothing.

Then it comes to you - the Letter! Didn't it say something about tapping out a secret code? You step up to the brick wall and take a deep breath.

Will you try:

41.
Measuring up

"Toast will burn and porridge bubble, measure this kid and save me the trouble!" shrieked witch number 2.

The incantation complete, the magic tape measure zooms around your body like a whirlwind, measuring everything from your inside leg measurement, to the distance between your nostrils, to the length of your ear lobes.

At the same time a magic biro is writing down all these measurements on a notepad.

After a few minutes, in which you are frightened to move in case the tape measure accidentally shoots up your nose, the tape neatly rolls itself up and lands on a table.

Witch number 2 looks carefully at the scribbled numbers in the notepad and counts on her fingers.

She looks up at her sister and yells: "Small!"

As witch number 1 scuttles off to get a small robe for you, your Mum, who has been standing quietly to one side clears her throat.

"Is there any chance we could do some sort of challenge or test?" your mum asks. "And get a discount of say, 100%? I'm afraid we didn't bring any wizard money..."

Snako Malboy snorts and rolls his eyes.

"A test? A challenge? No deary. What we like are wagers"

"Ok whatever. Can we do a wager and not pay anything?" your mum says.

"I wager you can't guess my age. If you can, you can keep the robe and get a free hat. If you fail you will stay in this shop for ever!"

"I'll do it" you say bravely, "but I will need a clue."

"How old are you boy?" asks the witch.

"I'm ten years old."

"Here's your clue. If you multiply your age by ten, then add nine... That's the age I will be in ten year's time. How old am I, right now?"

42.
The magical void

You find yourself in a magical place that exists outside time and outside space.

The only way to reach here is by powerful magic. No path can take you here. No decision you make will lead you to this place.

Only the very best wizards can command this level of magical power.

You appear to be floating in a sort of void. If you want to move you only have to think yourself moving. Across this void glimmer infinitely long twists and curtains of shimmering golden sparkles: raw magic.

It is peaceful. You feel relaxed and calm. The troubles of the world do not reach here.

You think yourself over to a golden pillar of glittering magical dust and let it run over your hand. You feel the magic enter your veins and your magical strength increases further.

Now that you have found this place and touched the magic dust you only have to think of the magic number "42" and you will be instantly teleported back here.

Looking around you notice transparent rainbow bubbles floating between the twisting columns of golden dust.

You look closer.

Each bubble is the size of a football. Inside the bubbles you can see figures moving - people. You recognise yourself in the bubbles.

You realise that the bubbles must be windows into your past - and your future. Each bubble is an important moment in your life. As soon as you realise this you also know that all you have to do is reach into a bubble and you will be transported to that time and place.

A feeling of deep happiness settles upon you. You can go to any back - or forwards - to anytime in your life it is your choice.

Or should you double your efforts, try two times as much as you are now, and explore this magical void a little more?

But anytime you want you can come back here, to this shimmering golden magical void, filled with peace - just by thinking the magic number: 42.

Will you reach into a bubble - or linger here a while longer?

............................................................

1. The bubble at the start, when the letter arrives. Go to number 1. ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. The bubble when you enter Hippoto Mews to buy your stuff. ~ Go to number 49

3. The bubble when you arrive in Hogsnorts for the first time. ~ Go to number 53

43.
The first feast

Everyone on Lionpaw table welcomes you with shouts of unrestrained joy.

"Well done Arthur!" yells Alex Bleezeley, looking none the worse for his crash landing. "You're in the best House now!" He and his brother Robert Bleezeley pound your back vigorously.

The children around the table spontaneously break into the Lionpaw House chant, prancing around and shadow boxing some imaginary foe.

"South paw, North paw, we score, Lionpaw!"

You have a huge grin on your face and it only gets wider when - the rest of the House Sorting complete - Slumblebore magically conjures up an incredible feast for dinner.

From out of thin air materializes platters of roast beef and boiled sprouts, Yorkshire pudding and mashed turnips, shepherds pie and boiled broccoli, toad in the hole and boiled potatoes, bubble and squeak and boiled carrots, apple crumble with strawberry ice cream, and spotted dick drowning in custard.

"Shepherds pie, my favourite!" Aaron Bleezeley, a boy who was also chosen for Lionpaw House, licks his lips.

In a rite of initiation all the first years crack open the eggs they received from Percy the Picking Pigeon and guzzle the contents raw.

You and Aaron, raw egg running down your chins, grin at each other, and you are certain you will be best friends.

Then you eat more than you have ever eaten before, enjoying yourself immensely. You wonder if Slumblebore is somehow making the food magically disappear after it enters your stomach, in a similar way to how he made the food appear on the table. But finally you realise you can't cram anything more into your belly, and let out a huge belch.

"Children!" Slumblebore stands, his beard streaked with mashed turnips and the odd boiled potato. He raises his hands for silence. "Children! Now we have eaten our fill it is time for bed. Prefects lead the students to the House towers. And remember: the dungeons are off limits this term. We don't know what's down there, and neither do we want to."

The children rise to their feet, clutching their distended tummies, and prepare to leave the hall.

You turn to Aaron Bleezeley and say:

............................................................

1. "Hey Aaron, let's check out the Lionpaw House dormitories, I'm sure they will be so cool!" ~ Go to number 219

2. "Hey Aaron, shall we try to break into the dungeon? I'm dying to know what's down there!" ~ Go to number 241

52.
Wanderful Wands

Last stop: Wally's Wanderful Wands shop. Soon you will get your hands on a wand and start doing some magic. Oh yeah.

The sign above Wally's shop is a giant wand dangling from a chain above the shop door. It swings gently to and fro even though there is no breeze to speak of, and little crackles of electric-gold magic arc over its surface.

With a nervous glance upwards you and your Mum enter the shop.

The inside is sparklingly clean and glass cabinets are artfully arranged around the shop. Each cabinet contains three or four magic wands, resting on little red cushions with gold tassles. It all looks very expensive.

"Arthur are you sure this is the only wand shop?" asks your mum. "Perhaps there is another one that is not quite so err... so un..."

"Welcome!" a smooth rich voice startles them from the back of the room. "Welcome to Wally's Wanderful Wand shop! And madam I can assure you that this is the only wand shop in Hippoto Mews. But fear not I'm sure we can find a wand that is the perfect match for young Arthur."

"How did you know my name?" you ask in surprise.

"One of the many branches of magic in which I am an expert, young Arthur, is mind reading. Just by looking into your eyes I can see the entire contents of your brain. I can also do it by looking in your ears, in your mouth, up your nose... any hole works to tell the truth. But I usually prefer the eyes. Also your Mum called you Arthur when you entered my shop."

"And you are Wally I suppose?" says your Mum.

"I am indeed, dear madam. Did you divine this from looking in my ear hole? Remarkable!"

"No I figured it out when you said this was your shop."

"Quite so. We are all mind-readers to some degree."

"Mr Wally" you interrupt "can I have a wand please?"

"No you cannot have a wand Arthur. But what you can have is the wand. Every wand is unique! You are unique! You require the exact match for your particular thaumaturgical resonance. Your thaumaturgic twin as it were. The most powerful - the only! - tool you will ever need as a magician."

"That sounds nice," says your Mum, "but we don't want anything too fancy. Or expensive."

"The wand is of course priceless. But you can buy one for 100 Golden Frigates."

"Golden what now?" asks your Mum. "Don't you take pounds? I don't have any Golden Frigates."

"It's wizard money only in this shop I'm afraid. I do offer a 10% discount for Hogsnorts' students in their first year... But for you I will increase this discount to 100% if - if! - Arthur and I can establish a true connection of minds, and I can see that you Arthur are a worthy wandholder."

"A 100% discount you say? That's a good deal. Arthur see if you can connect up your mind with Wally's love." your Mum suggests.

Wally crouches down in front of you and holds your ears gently but firmly forcing you to look deep into his blue grey eyes. At first nothing happens. But after just a few moments you get the strange sensation of being pulled towards his eyeballs; his black pupils feel like they are dragging you inwards.

"Good Arthur, very good!" says Wally. "I believe that the magical connection between our minds is now established, and astonishingly quickly too! You must have deep reserves of magic.

"Arthur I need you to think of a number. If I can read your mind and tell you the number you were thinking of this will be proof that the magical mind connection is working properly.

"First I need you to think of a number between 1 and 10. But don't tell me what it is! Have you got one?"

You think of a number and nod your head.

"Now" says Wally, "I need you to multiply this number by 9. 9 is a number with strong magical properties" he explains.

You multiply your number by 9.

"The next step" he says, "is to split your answer into the two digits and add those two digits together. For example if your answer is 13 (and I know it is not!) then you would split it into 1 and 3, then add that 1 and 3 together, so 1 + 3 = 4.

"Ok" you say as you do the sum in your head.

"Now take that answer and multiply it by 7. Can you do that?"

"Yes" you reply.

"Now turn to that number! And we will see if our minds are connected."
