53.
Welcome to Hognsorts

"Welcome students!" Professor Slumblebore, the headmaster of Hogsnorts School of Magic, smiles down at the assembled children, yellowish teeth glinting through his long grey beard.

"I have a few things to say to you before the House Sorting ceremony, where the first years are allocated to their Houses.

"Firstly, study hard!

"Secondly, five points deducted from Lionpaw House due to Robert and Alex Bleezeley piloting an unauthorised flying car in Hogsnorts airspace and endangering the lives of themselves and all the other children in the school when they drove straight at the flying monkeys carrying all the students to Hogsnorts."

A groan went up from all the children in Lionpaw House who shoot venomous looks at Robert and Alex.

"Thirdly, ten points awarded to Lionpaw House due to an excellent emergency landing by Robert Bleezeley on the Hogsnorts school lawn!"

Slumblebore beamed at them and the Lionpaw kids cheered, and slapped Robert and Alex on the back, laughing.

"Fourthly, we appear to have an insect infestation in the school. Our Care of Magical Creatures Professor Mr Knid is leading the eradication efforts - " Slumblebore pauses to acknowledge a flamboyantly caped teacher sitting next to him " - although so far the little pests have proved stubbornly resistant. So I would ask all students that if they come across a spider in a corridor or in the classroom, please tread on it."

You notice Professor Knid grimace, no doubt embarrassed about his failure to control the infestation.

"Fifthly, on no account are any children to enter the dungeon this term. We have picked up indications of some extremely malevolent magic taking place down there. I have cast an enchantment of locking on the door and we are going to leave whatever it is going on down there well alone, thank you!"

You notice all the other children whispering to each other - what could be going on in that dungeon that makes even Slumblebore afraid?

"Lastly, despite what I said last year I'm afraid Hogsnorts still doesn't have an internet connection. As you know the magical aurora interferes with mobile phone signals, and I'm afraid Professor Adeptus has not yet been able to figure out the correct incantations to get the WiFi router working."

Another groan, this time from all of the students, followed by disappointed muttering.

"But now, on to the child sorting!" Slumbedore raises his hands for silence. "Open the hole!"

A student scurries forward and pulls a lever by the platform at the front of the hall. Just in front of Slumblebore a huge stone flagstone slides slowly to one side leaving an opening in the floor.

Craning your neck, you can see nothing but darkness, and some wooden steps leading down inside. There is total silence in the hall as if the students don't dare even to breathe.

From out of the hole emerges... a noise. A sort of high pitched musical voice but made by what you have no idea.

"Silence everybody," instructs Slumblebore, "we are about to hear this year's Sorting Song."

............................................................

1. You have no option but to sit and listen to the sorting song ~ Go to number 60

54.
A magical connection

"Yes! 54 is the number - fantastic!" says Wally, beaming with delight.

"Our minds have a strong magical connection and I can see that you are truly a worthy wandholder, and deserving of my special 100% discount. I can also determine which wand will match you exactly."

Wally starts muttering to himself and he strides between the cabinets.

"Flexible? Yes but not too much... The action will be important... More benign than malign that's for sure..."

All of sudden Wally stops next to a cabinet and reaches inside.

"Yes!" he shouts and holds up a brown wand. "This is the one, Arthur. Hold it!"

You take it from his hand and it feels... right. Like it has always belonged to you - but that somehow you also belong to the wand.

"An excellent match!" says Wally "Made of wood from the wishing tree, with a core of spider silk from the bottom of the great spider king himself, and curiously enough, one of my own beard hairs. Give it a wave Arthur."

You give the wand a bit of a shake. Effortlessly little sparks of gold zap off the end and ping into the walls. You feel magical power surge through your arm.

"Thank you very much Mr Wally" says your Mum.

"Thank you Wally" you say.

NO. THANK YOU! says Wally speaking directly into your mind. He looks at you and winks.

The only thing you are missing now is your spell book!

............................................................

1. Visit Watertomes to get your year 1 spell book ~ Go to number 17

55.
All aboard

You do as your Dad suggests, letting out a sigh as you tinkle in the toilet. You were so sure this was the right place. Evan sighs too and starts playing with the toilet brush.

Curiously, as you wee in the toilet you notice that your urine is giving off a faint magical golden glow. Odd, you think, as you zip yourself up and press the flush...

...and leap backwards in surprise as the whole toilet and then the wall behind it disappears in a magical swirling spiral, leaving a perfectly round tunnel with steps heading deep down into the darkness. It is just like how the wall opened to get to Hippoto Mews, but this time it must have been activated by the magic sparkles in your wee!

"This is the way!" you shout, "let's go!"

The stairs go down and down for ages, but finally you see a brightly lit tunnel far below. Redoubling your efforts you bound down the remaining steps to find yourself in...

...a tiled white tunnel that looks very much like the tunnels you get in the London underground, except with strange magical sigils on the walls, emitting a warm golden light.

You run down the tunnel - it can't be long until the train leaves now! - and arrive at an underground station platform.

You see a tube train filled with children and a platform crowded with parents saying goodbye. You look up at the announcement board and read:

"Hogsnorts: 1 minute"

"Look Dad! The Hogsnorts Express is a tube train!" you exclaim. "And we're just in time."

"Goodbye Arthur," says your Dad "Good luck in wizard school! Write to us as often as you can. We'll see you in six weeks when it's the holidays." There is a tear in his eye as he gives you a hug goodbye.

"Bye bye Arthur," says Evan hugging your middle. "Teach me a magic spell when you come back home."

"I will Evan," you say. "Goodbye and see you in a few weeks."

You spot the boy from the spellbook shop in one carriage, and in another the boy from the robe shop.

A piercing steam whistle shriek sounds from the front of the train.

"Mind the doors please!" a magically amplified voice calls out. "Mind the closing doors!"

Do you:

............................................................

1. Go into the carriage with the boy from the spellbook shop ~ Go to number 61

2. Enter the carriage with the boy from the robe shop ~ Go to number 67

3. Go into a different another carriage altogether ~ Go to number 28

56.
A spellbook puzzle

You walk further into the book shop and spy a cheerful looking old witch wearing a black t-shirt with the word Watertomes on the back.

"Excuse me," you say "Can you show me where the year 1 spellbook is?"

"Off to Hogsnorts are you young man?" replies the old witch with a little cackle. "Yes I can show you, follow me!"

You and your mum follow the Watertomes witch as she shuffles off to the back of the bookshop. She picks up a heavy red book.

"That will be 14 Frigates please."

"Ah yes," replies your mum, "We've only got pounds. Is that a problem?"

"Well to tell the truth I don't really need money because I can magic up anything I like anyway. But I can't just give it to you for nothing... Tell you what, if you can solve my puzzle you can have it."

"What's the puzzle?" you reply nervously, you never did like puzzles that much.

"My lovely spell books are all about turning words into magic. And one of the magic things about words is that you can turn them into numbers.

For example the word CAB can turn into the number 6. C is the third letter of the alphabet, A is the first letter and B is the second. 3 + 1 + 2 = 6 so CAB turns into 6.

If you can magically turn my name into a number I will give you this book. My name is LIN. The old witch called Lin smiles at you encouragingly.

"Hmmm let's see" you say. As you are thinking the boy you saw at the front of the bookshop pushes a piece of paper into your hand.

"Here!" he says, "this should help!"

The piece of paper has all the letters of the alphabet next to their numbers:

A=1, B=2, C=3, E=4, D=5, F=6, G=7, H=8, I=9, J=10, K=11, L=12, M=13, N=14, O=15, P=16, Q=17, R=18, S=19, T=20, U=21, V=22, W=23, X=24, Y=25, Z=26

............................................................

1. You turn Lin's name into a number, and go to that number ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. This is giving you a headache, you decide to step outside for a breather ~ Go to number 16

57.
Magical mayhem

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlice menacingly and shout loudly:

"Dispara dinosaurio demente!"

From out of the end of your wand comes a faint but growing roaring sound, like an angry lion. The noise grows louder and louder until it is so loud it hurts your ears.

"Arthur, have you done?" asks Kensley in alarm.

"I don't..." you begin, but before you can finish your sentence, a huge golden dinosaur head somehow forces it's way out of the tip of your wand, and roars again deafeningly.

"ROAR!!!"

"Oh no, angry tyrannosaurus rexes are my number one fear!" Kensley is too petrified to move.

But there's nothing you can do, the spell has been cast. The enormous magical t-rex squeezes its way out of your wand and charges its way towards the woodlice, waggling its ridiculous little front arms in a demented fashion.

It launches itself at the nearest woodlouse which has no time to react.

But instead of crushing the woodlouse in its banana sized teeth, the t-rex - impossibly - just bounces off.

It roars and tries again, with the same result.

Then it hits you - woodlice are completely immune to magic.

The dinosaur appears to understand this too. It looks around for a better target. And it's crazy little red eyes fix on you and Snako.

With a sense of horror you realise that the t-rex is now hunting you!

The rabid dinosaur leaps at you and Kensley but instead of eating you it flings you both into the stone wall on each side and you bump your head painfully. The t-rex stomps up the corridor before disappearing a puff of gold stars as the magic wears off.

As you slide down the wall and into unconsciousness, you can see the millions of woodlice waving their little antennae. As you close your eyes you think: are they laughing?

............................................................

1. You lie down unconscious for an indeterminate length of time. ~ Go to number 200

58.
A visit to Spellwitches

You may have your spell book but you need to look like a wizard too.

The shop has large storefront windows. Inside the windows manikins have been arranged wearing black witch and wizard robes. The manikins are in a variety of action poses, such as just about to cast a spell, or frozen running away from a dragon.

But they have clearly been magically enchanted because every now and again one of the manikins will change their position to something else, moving smoothly with astonishing realism. You look at the manikins carefully - they really are amazingly life-like, even down to the expressions of surprise on their faces.

You and your mum make a little bell dingle as you push open the door.

In front of you are racks and racks of wizard robes, all black. Above some racks a sign says 'small', above others it says 'medium', and others 'large'.

Shelves cover the walls and the shelves are covered in pointy black hats.

"May I help you at all?"

You and your mum both jump - a witch with a totally green face leaps out from behind a rack of black robes just in front of you.

"Just browsing are you?"

You jump again as another witch, looking identical to the first, pops out from a rack of clothes behind you.

"Aargh!" you exclaim. You take a breath and calm yourself and clear your throat.

"Robes?" you squeak "For Hogsnorts?"

"You are in the right place my little dear" said green witch number 1. "Let's see how you measure up!"

The two witches take you to a side room where a magic tape measure is already taking the measurements of a pale looking boy about your age.

The boy looks at you with an expression that could either be a sneer or a smile, you can't quite be sure.

Do you:

............................................................

1. Strike up a conversation with the boy, he may be a future classmate ~ Go to number 11

2. Keep your mouth shut, you just want to get this done and get out of here ~ Go to number 48

59.
Picked for Hogggers

Hedgehog House! I want to be in Hedgehog House.

Coo coo are you sure it's Hedgehog House? asks Percy the pigeon, speaking directly into your mind now.

Yes please, you think back at him. Not a slimey Snakefang, not a meathead Lionpaw, not a smarty pants Ravenclaw. I don't want any trouble, I just want to be in Hedgehog House!

Coo coo as you wish young Arthur, speaks Percy into your brain.

Slowly the great yellow eyes shrink to normal size and you are just staring at a regular giant talking pigeon again.

Percy waddles over to the centre of the hole where the light from the hall shines down. He looks old and you wonder how long he has been doing this. For decades? Centuries even?

The giant pigeon settles down on the floor, and coos once or twice. He then stands up slowly and waddles back into the darkness at the edge of the hole that is his home. On the floor he has laid a large and beautiful egg.

The egg is a dull brown colour stripes. The colour of Hedgehog House!

Your heart pounding with excitement, you pick up the egg and slowly walk back up the wooden stairs to the noise and light of the Hogsnorts Great Hall.

As you emerge out of the pigeon hole, Slumblebore sees your egg and shouts: "Arthur Otley, Hedgehog House!"

............................................................

1. You walk over to the Hedgehog House table, holding your egg aloft. ~ Go to number 275

60.
The sorting song

A warbling tune floats into the hall from the hole:

"First years, first years, what will you do?
Which House do you like and which House likes you?
I've written this ditty while waiting in my hole
Listen very closely and figure out your role...

Leonard Lionpaw he fights for truth
With boot and fist, nail and tooth.
When injustice triumphs it makes him sick
He'll fight right back with a punch and a kick.

Rebecca Ravenwing, her mind's so quick,
She makes even Albert Einstein look a bit thick.
When evil lurks she knows just what to do:
Outwit the wicked witch with her brainbox crew.

Helen Hedgehog, she's reliable and calm
She'll never start trouble or cause you harm.
With bad magic in the air, she'll act fast:
She'll hide and curl up until the danger is past.

Sylvester Snakefang, seeking world domination
Power is his thing along with extirpation.
When darkness comes his eyes light up,
He'll do anything it takes to make it to the top."

The song warbles to a stop and there is smattering of polite applause from the children in the hall.

"Thank you Percy," says Slumblebore, directing his voice down into the hole. "Although I must say I thought last year's song was better."

Percy? What is this strange singing creature called Percy living in a hole underneath the Great Hall? you ask yourself.

"First years, please form a queue in front of me!"

You realise that you are soon going to find out whoever or whatever Percy is. You nervously stand up along with all the other first years. You decide to:

............................................................

1. Go to the front of the queue. Whatever happens you want to be first in line to see! ~ Go to number 7

2. Lurk around at the back of the queue. Fortune favours the prudent. ~ Go to number 13

61.
On the Hogsnorts Express

The boy in the bookshop seemed friendly so you decide to go and sit next to him. Your mind made up, you leap aboard the train just as the doors slam shut behind you.

"Hello," you say, "I'm Arthur, we saw each other in the spellbook shop in Hippoto Mews the other day."

You sit down in the spare seat next to him. He glances up from the spell book he is reading.

"Hello, I'm Daniel," he says then carries on reading his book and muttering to himself.

"What's that book you're reading?" you ask.

"Das Magical, by Lotso Larks. It's a collection of spells for coordinating large groups of people."

"Oh" you reply. "Would you like a Smarty?"

Daniel's eyes light up and he puts the book down. "I love Smarties. Have you got any purple ones?"

You share out the colourful chocolate treats companionably. Your favourite ones are blue ones which makes Daniel excited.

"Hey Arthur," he begins, "did you know that blue and copper are the colours of Ravenwing House? You like blue Smarties, maybe that's a sign that you will be in Ravenwing House like I will be?"

"Yeah maybe," you say "Ravenwing is for brain-boxes people right?"

"It's the house for people that love learning. What would life be like if you never learned new things? I want to find out as much as possible. I want to know the secret of teleportation, of space travel, of unlimited energy. I want to know everything! Don't you?"

"I guess I would" you reply although... that sounds like a lot of studying and even then you might not end up knowing everything.

While you are talking to Daniel the train chugs out from the dark tunnel into daylight, as the railway tracks emerge from the side of a hill.

You twist in your seat to peer out of the window. As far as you can see there are rolling hills covered in pine trees. In the distance, craggy mountains emerge, their tops clouded in mist. It looks like nowhere you have ever seen before, except perhaps in the illustrations to one of your favourite books, The Hobbit.

You feel like you have entered a magical new land and your adventure has truly begun.

A magically amplified voice interrupts your daydreams of dwarves and dragons, trolls and treasure.

"Train terminates here. All change please, all change. Mind the gap."

Hogsnorts station! This is it. You've arrived.

............................................................

1. Alight from the train ~ Go to number 66

62.
Snako Malboy

"Hello," you say to the boy "my name's Arthur Otley and I'm going to Hogsnorts. Who are you?"

The boy does his sneering smile at you again.

"Snako Malboy. Yes I too am going to Hogsnorts. My father went to Hogsnorts. My grandfather went to Hogsnorts. So did his father and so on up to 72 generations and the founding of the school. Sylvester Snake - yes the Sylvester Snake is my direct ancestor. And my mother and their mothers too. So yes I am going to Hogsnorts."

"Who is Sylvester Snake?"

"Sylvester Snake is only the founder of Snake House! The best house in the school. I'm going to be in Snake House. Snake House is for the really powerful wizards, like I will be one day. You will be in Hedgehog House I suppose."

"I haven't decided yet" you reply.

"Well if you want to be Snake House like me you have to be strong and ruthless. Snake House rules yah sssssssss!"

Snako Malboy sticks his tongue in and out of his mouth like a snake and hisses - not an easy thing to do at the same time. You are impressed.

At that point the magic tape measure is finished with Snako and moves over to you.

64.
Wanderful Wands

You decide to visit Wally's Wanderful Wands shop first. You want to get your hands on a wand as soon as possible and start doing some magic.

The sign above Wally's shop is a giant wand dangling from a chain above the shop door. It swings gently to and fro even though there is no breeze to speak of, and little crackles of electric-gold magic arc over its surface.

You can't help thinking that this wand must also double up as Wally's security system.

With a nervous glance upwards you and your Mum enter the shop.

The inside is sparklingly clean and glass cabinets are artfully arranged around the shop. Each cabinet contains three or four magic wands, resting on little red cushions with gold tassles. It all looks very expensive.

"Arthur are you sure this is the only wand shop?" asks your mum. "Perhaps there is another one that is not quite so err... so un..."

"Welcome!" a smooth rich voice startles them from the back of the room. "Welcome to Wally's Wanderful Wand shop! And madam I can assure you that this is the only wand shop in Hippoto Mews. But fear not I'm sure we can find a wand that is the perfect match for young Arthur."

"How did you know my name?" you ask in surprise.

"One of the many branches of magic in which I am an expert, young Arthur is mind reading. Just by looking into your eyes I can see the entire contents of your brain. I can also do it by looking in your ears, in your mouth, up your nose... any hole works to tell the truth. But I usually prefer the eyes. Also your Mum called you Arthur when you entered my shop."

"And you are Wally I suppose?" says your Mum.

"I am indeed, dear madam. Did you divine this from looking in my ear hole? Remarkable!"

"No I figured it out when you said this was your shop."

"Quite so. We are all mind-readers to some degree."

"Mr Wally" you interrupt "can I have a wand please?"

"No you cannot have a wand Arthur. But what you can have is the wand. Every wand is unique! You are unique! You require the exact match for your particular thaumaturgical resonance. Your thaumaturgic twin as it were. The most powerful - the only! - tool you will ever need as a magician."

"That sounds nice," says your Mum, "but we don't want anything too fancy. Or expensive."

"The wand is of course priceless. But you can buy one for 100 Golden Frigates."

"Golden what now?" asks your Mum. "Don't you take pounds? I don't have any Golden Frigates."

"It's wizard money only in this shop I'm afraid. I do offer a 10% discount for Hogsnorts' students in their first year... But for you I will increase this discount to 100% if - if! - Arthur and I can establish a true connection of minds, and I can see that you Arthur are a worthy wandholder."

"A 100% discount you say? That's a good deal. Arthur see if you can connect up your mind with Wally's love." your Mum suggests.

Wally crouches down in front of you and holds your ears gently but firmly forcing you to look deep into his blue grey eyes. At first nothing happens. But after just a few moments you get the strange sensation of being pulled towards his eyeballs; his black pupils feel like they are dragging you inwards.

"Good Arthur, very good!" says Wally. "I believe that the magical connection between our minds is now established, and astonishingly quickly too! You must have deep reserves of magic.

"Arthur I need you to think of a number. If I can read your mind and tell you the number you were thinking of this will be proof that the magical mind connection is working properly.

"First I need you to think of a number between 1 and 10. But don't tell me what it is! Have you got one?"

You think of a number and nod your head.

"Now" says Wally, "I need you to multiply this number by 9. 9 is a number with strong magical properties" he explains.

You multiply your number by 9.

"The next step" he says, "is to split your answer into the two digits and add those two digits together. For example if your answer is 13 (and I know it is not!) then you would split it into 1 and 3, then add that 1 and 3 together, so 1 + 3 = 4.

"Ok" you say as you do the sum in your head.

"Now take that answer and multiply it by 8. Can you do that?"

"Yes" you reply.

"Now turn to that number! And we will see if our minds are connected."

............................................................

1. Turn to the number that you have thought of ~ Go to the number of your answer

2. You are not in the mood for mindreading, go to Spellwitches for robes instead ~ Go to number 38

3. You don't feel like telepathy, head to Watertomes to get your spellbook ~ Go to number 37

66.
The Winged Monkeys

You step off the train with the other children, onto a platform that looks like something from the Victorian era a hundred years ago. There is steam coming from the train chimney, old fashioned signs saying Hogsnorts Station, a row of gargoyles on the station roof, and a lingering smell of pipe smoke.

You are momentarily distracted by the sight of something else stepping out, or more accurately climbing out of the train: hundreds of spiders filing out of the doors and onto the platform. How curious, you think.

"All students over here!" a deafening bellow startles you so much that you forget about the spiders. "Follow me!"

Through the crowds of children dressed up as miniature witches and wizards strides an impossibly large man. His enormous bristling black beard and thick bushy hair make his twinkling eyes and bulbous nose look like the epicentre of a hair explosion.

"Now then students!" says the giant, his tummy wobbling as he bellows. "Space yourselves out a bit and raise both arms in the air."

You and the other first years eye each other uneasily.

"Monkeys!" yells the giant man into the sky.

At first nothing happens and you wonder if the giant isn't just a total madman who likes to hang out in train stations. But then... you hear lots of faint cracking sounds and look up to see the gargoyles on the station roof come to life.

Your jaw drops as the stone statues transform into flesh, blood and fur monkeys, each with a pair of feathered wings and, for some reason, a little red hat.

"Two flying monkeys to a child!" shouts out the fat giant. The monkeys - or are they actually some species of chimpanzee? - chatter and grimace to show they understand, then jump down to the station platform and scamper up to the children.

Two winged monkeys, both about the same size as you are, grab you underneath one arm each, scream and bare their teeth in excitement and launch themselves into the sky.

You decide to:

............................................................

1. Hang on for dear life as you soar up into the air. ~ Go to number 12

67.
On the Hogsnorts Express

You leap nimbly into the carriage with the boy from the robe shop - it will be fun to chat on the journey. You go and sit next to him.

"Hello," you say "I'm Arthur, we saw each other in the robe shop."

The boy does his sneer-smile. "Yes I know, you're the boy who didn't have any wizard money. I'm Snako Malboy, the richest boy in the school, so why should I talk to you?"

You decide to change your approach.

"I've got some Smarties, would you like one?"

"Smarties?" replies Snako, "what are you, some kind of smarty pants?" He snorts with laughter and looks round the carriage to see if anyone is laughing at his rubbish joke. No-one reacts.

Sitting back in his seat Snako adds more quietly: "Yes please, have you got any blue ones? They're my favourite."

For the next few minutes you happily share out the colourful chocolate treats. Snako likes the blue ones and your favourite are the green, which makes him excited.

"Hey Arthur, did you know Snakefang House colours are green and silver? And you like green Smarties. Maybe that's a sign that you will be in Snakefang House too, like I will be!"

"What's Snakefang House like?" you ask curiously.

"Oh it's great," replies Snako. "All the most powerful wizards have been in Snakefang House. It teaches you how to make other people do what you want."

"I'm not sure I want to make people do stuff" you say.

"Do you want to change the world when you grow up? I know I do. I don't want to just put up with how things are. And how are you going to change the world if everyone just ignores you? We can make them listen Arthur, then you can have all the green Smarties you want."

It's a good argument - you would like to have more green Smarties. You promise Snako to think about it and sit in companionable silence as the train chuffs onwards through a dark tunnel.

After what seems absolutely ages the Hogsnorts Express bursts into daylight, the train tracks emerging from the mouth of the tunnel in the side of a hill.

You twist in your seat to peer out of the window. As far as you can see there are rolling hills covered in pine trees. In the distance, craggy mountains emerge, their tops clouded in mist. It looks like nowhere you have ever seen before, except perhaps in the illustrations to one of your favourite books, The Hobbit.

You feel like you have entered a magical new land and your adventure has truly begun.

A magically amplified voice interrupts your daydreams of dwarves and dragons, trolls and treasure.

"Train terminates here. All change please, all change. Mind the gap."

Hogsnorts station! This is it. You've arrived.

But this doesn't really bother you, it's so exciting to be around real magicians!

"Do you feel better after some fresh air Arthur?" asks your mum. "We still need to get your wand before you can go to Hogsnorts. Come on, let's go back to talk to that Wally fellow."

69.
A spellbook puzzle

You walk further into the book shop and spy a cheerful looking old witch wearing a black t-shirt with the word Watertomes on the back in white letters.

"Excuse me," you say "Can you show me where the year 1 spellbook is?"

"Off to Hogsnorts are you young man?" replies the old witch with a little cackle. "Yes I can show you, follow me!"

You and your mum follow the Watertomes witch as she shuffles off to the back of the bookshop. She picks up a heavy red book.

"That will be 14 Frigates please."

"14 Frigates?" replies your mum, "Don't you take pounds?"

"Wizard money only I'm afraid, but..." the old lady tails off.

"Yes?" you say.

"Well to tell the truth I don't really need money because I can magic up anything I like anyway. But I can't just give it to you for nothing... Tell you what, if you can solve my puzzle you can have it."

"What's the puzzle?" you reply nervously, you never did like puzzles that much.

"My lovely spell books are all about turning words into magic. And one of the magic things about words is that you can turn them into numbers.

For example the word CAB can turn into the number 6. C is the third letter of the alphabet, A is the first letter and B is the second. 3 + 1 + 2 = 6 so CAB turns into 6.

If you can magically turn my name into a number I will give you this book. My name is MEG. The old witch called Meg smiles at you encouragingly.

"Hmmm let's see" you say. As you are thinking the boy you saw at the front of the bookshop pushes a piece of paper into your hand.

"Here!" he says, "this should help!"

The piece of paper has all the letters of the alphabet next to their numbers:

A=1, B=2, C=3, E=4, D=5, F=6, G=7, H=8, I=9, J=10, K=11, L=12, M=13, N=14, O=15, P=16, Q=17, R=18, S=19, T=20, U=21, V=22, W=23, X=24, Y=25, Z=26

71.
Spelling trouble

"I know I am called Arthur Otley," you say. "But is my name who I really am?"

"Excellent point Arthur! I can see by your question that you are already on the path to enlightenment. Because it is only when we realise that we don't know everything that we can learn."

Madame Blavatsky smiles at you. "And because you are ready to learn I will now teach you your first spell."

"But first can anyone tell me," she says addressing the whole class now, "what is the most common cause of death for wizards and witches? Anyone?"

"Fighting dragons?" suggests Snako.

"Zombies?" proposes another child.

"Soul suckers? Werewolves? Vampires?"

"No, no and no again." replies Professor Blavatsky. "The one thing that is most likely to kill you more than anything else is: each other."

"Let me explain. Imagine it is night time, 3am in the morning. You hear a noise downstairs. Immediately you are on the alert. It could be burglars. Or more likely dark wizards on the attack. You creep downstairs, wand at the ready. You can hear them rummaging around in the kitchen. You leap out shouting the most deadly spells you can think of. Only to discover... it is your Uncle Brian who is visiting for the weekend and has come down in the night to help himself to a biscuit. Now he is paralysed on the kitchen floor, a look of horror on his face and the packet of biscuits grasped so tightly in his hand that no-one else will be eating them ever again."

"Yes I'm afraid to say that the most common cause of death is 'friendly fire', accidentally hitting your friends and family with dangerous or deadly spells. The sad fact is that you are all in far more danger from each other than from any evil sorcerer. Which is why the spell I am going to teach you to protect against dark magic is a sleeping spell. It is one I designed myself. The benefit of this spell is that it is completely reversible. To wake someone up, you just need to tickle them under their armpits."

Blavatsky then whips out her wand and points it at Snako.

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa!" she screams.

A dart of pure golden light shoots out of the end of her wand and hits Snako right in the middle of his forehead. In less than a half a second his head has sunk down to his arms on his desk and he is snoring like a sailor.

The class breaks out into a round of applause.

"Make sure you get the pronunciation just right when you cast the spell" Blavatksy advises as she walks over to Snako and tickles him under the armpits.

"He he he! What happened?" says Snako, confused.

The class splits into pairs and you practice sending each other to sleep. Because Snako is still a bit drowsy you go first, pointing your wand at his forehead just as the teacher did:

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa..." you repeat carefully.

You feel a wonderful feeling of magical power gathering in your tummy. In an instant it has whooshed up out of your arm, channelled by the wand into a golden dart that zaps Snako on the head, for the second time in as many minutes.

In no time at all he is asleep and snoring again.

"I did it!" you shout. "The magic spell worked!"

Delighted with your success you tickle Snako under the armpits. As he wakes up giggling you try hard to memorise the spell 'Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa' - you never know when it may come in handy.

Another chance

Opening your eyes you find you are at the bottom of a great stone well, with a circle of light far above. Somehow you know that you have also travelled back in time to before, when you had just arrived at the school. You are that Arthur once again in Percy's hole, but this time you can make a new choice.

This time you know you will make a good choice...

74.
The final decision

"What did you do that for?" you cry. "I thought he was your friend!"

Azog stepped delicately over the snoring form of Professor Knid and advances towards you.

"Just think Arthur. Together we could achieve so much. You, the chosen one with your one-of-a-kind wand and me with all the armies of the arthropods at my command! We could do anything. We could do everything!"

While Azog is talking he is getting steadily closer and closer to you. You find yourself mesmerised by his eight tiny compound eyes.

Perhaps you should take a stand, remake the world with Azog and the insect hordes, take over the school... on the other hand if you were to stop Azog now you would be a hero and would surely win the house cup for Lionpaw.

"You must choose now Arthur," says Azog quietly. "Are you with me? Or against me?"

75.
Inner peace

"I'm Arthur Otley and I want to learn some spells" you say to Professor Blavatsky.

"Ah so impatient. And yet this impatience stops you learning about yourself. I can see that you are very far from self control as yet."

The teacher stands up and raises one hand.

"But do not worry, any of you. Because we will start with a simple meditation session to help you gain control."

You groan inwardly. This sounds boring.

"Close your eyes everyone," begins Professor Blavatsky. "Make sure you are comfortable in your seats. Now I want you to focus on your breathing. Breathe in. Breathe out. Breathe in... and breathe out.

"Feel the breath flowing into your nostrils. Concentrate on the sensation. Do you feel your nose hairs tickling? Perhaps a small bogey flapping around in your nasal passage? Just think about the breath, how it feels."

Despite yourself you feel your awareness sharpening, and you do indeed feel a small bogey in your nostril wobbling around as you breathe in and out.

"Now I want you to think about a special number. The special number is 42. A four and then a two. Forty two. This number is not just a number it is also a place. A location. A place of calm that you can always turn to in moments of difficulty or stress.

"This number 42 is a place within yourself, but it is a real place too that anyone can reach, if they just turn to that number... the number 42. As you turn to 42, just keep your thumb here so you know where to come back to."

Amazingly you feel a sensation as if you are floating somehow, except with your thumb stuck down in front of you. Concentrating fiercely you try with all your might to turn to 42. You float away...

...

"Did anyone manage to meditate and reach 42?" asks Madam Blavatsky.

You definitely feel you went... somewhere. You think this is what Professor Blavatsky meant.

"Any time you find yourself in need of quiet and peace, just repeat this meditation exercise and think of the number 42 and you will find a place of calm and relaxation - but keep your thumb right where you are and you will be able to turn back whenever you want."

"Class dismissed! We will meet again."

............................................................

1. As if in a daze you and the other children rise slowly to your feet and walk out of the classroom. You do feel as if maybe you know yourself a little better now. ~ Go to number 117

77.
Battle rage

"Die beetles, die!" you cry, running towards the three giant bombardier beetles.

In your battle rage you forget all about magic and your wand, you just want to reach the beetles and grapple them with your bare hands, mano a beetlo.

"Yaaaah!" you cry most uncharacteristically, closing the distance fast...

...but not fast enough. The three beetles swiftly raise up their bottoms, and shoot out three streams of superheated acid, accompanied by three loud popping sounds.

One stream misses your head by inches, another strikes the wall beside you, the third the floor in front.

"Ha! You missed me! You'll have to get up earlier in the morning than that to..."

But you never get the chance to tell them what they will have to do when they get up early in the morning, because at that moment your foot slips on the pool of acid on the floor and slides out from underneath you. You fly through the air very briefly before slamming into the floor, bumping your head hard enough to knock you out cold.

78.
Professor Eric Knid Explains

A voice, strong and commanding, emerges from the darkness. "You? The saviour, a mere stripling first year? Impossible!"

Another voice, high pitched and chittery, answers him. "Yes Eric, this is him. He is the wand holder."

As your eyes adjust to the gloom, you can make out a figure standing in the centre of the room. A wizard - and someone you recognise.

"Professor Knid!" you exclaim.

"Yes Professor Eric Knid at your service! Or perhaps I should say that you will be at my service... Arthur isn't it?"

"Yes my name's Arthur. Arthur Otley." A sensation of fear congeals in your throat. "What do you mean? And who were you talking to just now?"

"All in good time, Arthur..." with an unexpectedly swift movement Professor Knid draws his wand and shoots a spell of locking at the iron gate which clangs shut.

You are trapped.

"What are you going to do?"

Eric Knid smiled. Even in the dark you can see the mad gleam in his eye: "Revolution!"

"Explain why Eric." That chittering voice again, appearing out of nowhere.

"Yes - why. Why?" Professor Knid takes a deep breath. "Ever since I was a young boy Arthur I have felt an affinity with insects, spiders, crabs. With the Arthropods. A dog will bite you, not so an earwig! A lion may eat you, not so a woodlouse! A human may betray you, a spider will not.

"My faithful friends growing up were slugs, ants, flies and beetles. But my friends were mercilessly crushed, poisoned, and swatted by humans.

"The final straw? Slumblebore sat on a spider - and laughed."

"I couldn't bear it. I sought out the Great Spider King Azog himself. What joy when I found him in the forbidden bushes and entered his service. Together we have been gathering supporters here in this dungeon, insects and spiders in their millions. For revenge. For a revolution. To take over the school!

"No longer will it just be Lionpaw House, Ravenwing House, Snakefang House, and Hedgehog House! We will have a new house mightier than all of them. The Order of the Arthropods! And I will be headmaster."

"But why me?" fear chills you. "What has this got to with me?"

"You are the only one who can stop us Arthur," says the mysterious high pitched voice. "But with you on our side we will be invincible!"

"Who is that?" you cry.

"This is the Great Spider King Azog himself. And you are honoured to stand in his presence." Professor Knid explains.

"Where?" You can't see anyone other than the Professor.

"Here!"

"Where, I can't see!"

"Right here, look! Closer!"

So slow in fact that the farmer is worried they might not get to market before it closes for the day. Anyway they come across an old man sitting by the side of the road. 'That cow looks like he's on his last legs' says the old man, and he hands the farmer two red pills. 'Now,' says the old man, 'If you stick one of these red pills up the cow's bottom he will be as right as rain.' Well the farmer sticks one of the red pills up the cow's bottom. The cow twitches three times and then he's off! He runs down the road towards the market as fast as a race horse. 'That's amazing!' says the farmer, 'Thanks a million for the pills. But what I don't understand is: why did you give me two pills?' 'Well,' says the old man, 'you want to catch him don't you?'

Professor Jape bursts into uncontrollable high pitched giggling and lots of the other children laugh too.

"Right children," says Jape. "That's all we've got time for in this lesson. I hope you had a good laugh, I know I did. See you next time."

80.
Dinner time

Joining a file of other Ravenwing students you head off on the long winding route back to the Hogsnorts Great Hall to get your dinner.

You take a seat at the Ravenwing table and look around you, flabbergasted.

Tonight Slumblebore has enchanted the walls and ceiling of the Great Hall to look like the whole hall is itself placed upon another table, as big as a parade ground, with great giants at either side ready to eat. An image of a candlestick towers above you and the ceiling in this giants dining hall is far above that. The enchantment is unbelievably realistic.

"Don't forget to eat Arthur!" Daniel reminds you, with a grin.

You look down to see yet another incredible feast.

Huge succulent poached salmon lie head to tail down the table, each one laid to rest in a solid silver tureen. Small mountains of roasted new potatoes, studded with salt crystals and veined with melted butter. Steamed broccoli the size of small trees, standing upright and giving off a wonderful green fresh aroma. Piles of chestnuts, slathered with marmalade and honey. Cunningly artificed marzipan animals, generously daubed in tomato ketchup.

It is all so delicious you can't stop an involuntary slobber which you quickly wipe from your chin with the table cloth.

You cram food into your mouth and gulp it down.

You are just gobbling up your eleventh marmalade and honey coated chestnut, when all of a sudden Slumblebore's enchanted imagery on the walls shows one of the giants reaching for the students in the hall: a colossal hand outstretched.

You scream and shout with the other students - Slumblebore's enchantment looks so real - when the hand appears to pick up the Hogsnorts Hall and carry it to his mouth!

Chairs are leaning crazily as the simulation progresses to show the inside of the giant's mouth as he chomps and swallows the hall. It looks as if you are falling, falling down the giant's throat, into his stomach. There are cries of dismay from some of the other younger students who have to be reassured that it is all just an amazing illusion.

As you continue your own meal, the simulation shows you pass through the giant's stomach, into the small intestine, then the large intensive until finally you emerge with a plop and drop into a bucket.

The students break into wild applause - this is one of Slumblebore's best ceiling enchantments yet!

"Bravo, bravo!" shouts Daniel Colliers-Wood, "Now I know how this chestnut feels, ha ha! Bravo!"

This signals the end of the best dinner you have ever had.

Turning to Daniel you say.

82.
Epilogue

The next day all the children are called to the school hall for a special announcement.

As you take your seats at the house tables you notice that the ceiling has been enchanted to a beautiful sky blue with fluffy clouds scudding past on one side and a flock of pterosaurs fighting to the death on the other.

"Students," announces Slumblebore from the front of the hall. "I have a very special announcement. Yesterday, unbeknownst to us, we were threatened by a vast and evil insect horde gathering in the school dungeon."

Slumblebore casts a severe glance at professor Knid, who looks down sheepishly at the table.

"We were saved thanks to the bravery, resourcefulness and gumption of one boy.

"That boy is Arthur Otley."

You feel your cheeks go red as all the students in the school turn round to get a look at you and you hear whispers of "yes that's him", "defeated the insects single handed!", "still just a first year!".

"In recognition of his outstanding services to Hogsnorts School I am pleased to award: one million points to Lionpaw House!"

Deafening cheers come from the Lionpaw House students all around you.

"Did you hear that?" cries Aaron Bleezeley. "A million points! Last year the Lionpaw house only got 600 points for the whole year! We'll win the House Cup for sure, well done Arthur!"

"What is more," continues Slumblebore, "any unused Lionpaw House points will carry over from one year to the next. Which by my calculation means that Lionpaw House will win the House Cup for approximately the next... one hundred years." Slumblebore beams at you through his beard.

"Lastly I hereby announce a new order of wizardry: the Order of the Arthropods. Arthur I grant you first class membership of the Order. Three cheers for Arthur Otley, hero of the school and founding member of the Order of the Arthropods!"

The cheers ring out over and over again. The Lionpaw students raise you up on your shoulders and carry you round and round the school hall in triumph shouting "Hooray for Arthur, hero of the school!"

CONGRATULATIONS - YOU HAVE ACHIEVED THE HERO OF THE SCHOOL ENDING

83.
Woodlouse warfare

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa," you cry, brandishing your wand fiercely.

A surge of magical power flows through your body, down your arm and out through the wand. A shower of golden sparks races down the corridor raining down onto the three beetles.

Each beetle glows gold for an instant before slowly rolling onto their side and then their backs, six legs waggling gently in the air.

"Did you kill them?" asks Aaron.

"No that was a sleeping spell. Look you can see their legs are still moving."

They must be dreaming some pleasant beetle dream, perhaps of cantering through a leafy carboniferous glade, as their legs make little wiggles in the air.

"Let's get past them before they wake up."

You and Aaron carefully step over the sleeping beetles and onwards down the corridor.

You descend a spiral staircase now and the air is getting dank and stale. It can't be long before you arrive in the dungeon.

At the bottom of the staircase it is pitch black.

You raise your wand and the tip emits a faint golden light, just enough to see by.

You almost wish you hadn't.

Revealed by the dim light of your wand you can see the floor and the walls are completely covered in woodlice. Millions upon millions of them cling to the damp stone slabs that make up the corridor. Millions more cover the flagstones, waving their repulsive little antennae. Others have curled up into balls and are rolling around irresponsibly.

Do woodlice even have eyes? You don't know but when you turned on your light they all seemed to turn and look at you.

"Oh my gosh Arthur, what are we going to do? There are too many of them to fight!"

"Don't move a muscle Aaron" you say in reply. "I have an idea."

84.
The magical infinite

Putting your hand into a stream of golden sparkles arcing by, you close your eyes and breathe slowly.

A sense of peace and serenity passes through you. You feel light, translucent: almost as if you have become one of the golden sparkles floating away.

Not floating up but somehow floating through, and you become aware of a subtle change in the air around you.

When you open your eyes you realise that you are now outside the infinite void that you had been floating in moments before.

In front of you is a large iridescent bubble, that has - impossibly but undeniably - wrapped up the infinite void that you were inside moments before. Peering closely through the bubble membrane, you can just make out the shimmering ribbons of golden magic arcing within it.

You realise that you have in some way gone further up and further out, onto another higher plane.

You notice other large iridescent bubbles floating around you.

One bubble in particular catches your eye.

In it you see another boy, about your age, with a mop of black hair, wizard robes and a peculiar scar on his forehead. Even though you have never met him before you feel you know who he is and a great feeling of warm friendliness comes over you.

Almost as if the boy in the bubble senses your thoughts he looks up and smiles.

You have a sudden insight that this place must be a place of almost infinite possibilities. Myriad bubbles fill the space around you - each bubble a different universe, each bubble a different possibility. You realise that together the bubbles must represent every possibility.

If you can imagine yourself in this place, you can be in any place.

You smile back at the boy with the funny scar on his forehead in the bubble next to you. Even though he can't see you, he must be able to sense you as you can sense him.

After contemplating the multiverse for a moment, or perhaps an eternity, you idly wonder whether you will head back to plane 42, or will you float out of and away from this story altogether?

86.
Defense against Dark Magic

You decide to go to the Defense Against Dark Magic class next. With Slumblebore warning of danger lurking in the dungeon, you want to be prepared.

Professor Madame Blavatsky's classroom is tucked away in an inconspicuous side passage and you almost miss it as you walk past. The inside is much more impressive though, with the floor and walls covered in inky black runes and pictograms, protecting the room against baleful influences.

The professor herself is sitting cross-legged on a little platform at the front of the classroom with her eyes closed while the children file in.

She is a short lady, wearing black robes and, because she is sitting with her legs crossed, looks a little like a large black frog. Her face is pale, almost white, and you can see networks of blue veins under the skin near her temples, like a river draining into a swamp.

As the last child sits down, she opens her eyes.

Her eyeballs gleam white, her irises a brilliant blue.

"Welcome children, to Defence Against Dark Magic. The most important lesson you will learn today is..." Blavatsky's melodious, soothing voice pauses for a moment.

"...control over your own mind. Because it is only when you have full control over yourself that you can hope to resist the control that dark forces may wish to exercise upon you."

"And what is the path to self control?"

There is silence in the room.

"It is self awareness. It is only by knowing yourself that you can control yourself."

You look over at Kensley and frown. This seems a long way from good old practical down-to-earth magic learning.

"But..." continues Madame Blavatsky, "I sense a doubter in the room. You!" She turns her blue eyes on yours and fixes you in her gaze.

"Have you already mastered yourself young man," she says to you. "Do you really know who you are?"

The blue eyes bore into you and you reply:

............................................................

87.
Battle rage

"Die beetles, die!" you cry, running towards the three giant bombardier beetles.

In your battle rage you forget all about magic and your wand, you just want to reach the beetles and grapple them with your bare hands, mano a beetlo.

"Yaaaah!" you cry, closing the distance fast...

...but not fast enough. The three beetles swiftly raise up their bottoms, and shoot out three streams of superheated acid, accompanied by three loud popping sounds.

One stream misses your head by inches, another strikes the wall beside you, the third the floor in front.

"Hahahaha, you missed me, you little..."

But you never get the chance to tell them exactly what type of little things they are because at that moment your foot slips on the pool of acid on the floor and slides out from underneath you. You fly through the air very briefly before slamming into the floor, bumping your head hard enough to knock you out cold.

88.
The final decision

"What did you do that for?" you cry. "I thought he was your friend!"

"Eric Knid is... weak," replies Azog. "His only purpose was to help me lure the chosen one - you - down here. Now that you have arrived, I no longer need him."

Azog stepped delicately over the snoring form of Professor Knid and advances towards you.

"Just think Arthur. Together we could achieve so much. You, the chosen one with your one-of-a-kind wand and me with all the armies of the arthropods at my command! We could do anything. We could do everything!"

While Azog is talking he is getting steadily closer and closer to you. You find yourself mesmerised by his eight tiny compound eyes. Daniel is also rooted to the spot.

Perhaps you should join with Azog and stand up for the down-trodden insect hordes - they have been most unfairly treated over the years. But on the other hand stopping Azog in his plan for school domination would go down well with the other students, and may give you the opportunity for dissecting a few of these fascinating little critters to learn about what makes them tick. And didn't Slumblebore promise you a million points?

"You must choose now Arthur," says Azog quietly. "Are you with me? Or against me?"

89.
The Hedgehog House Tower

You queue up patiently with the other Hedgehog House students as you prepare to leave the dining room. Standing next to Kensley Potato you smile shyly at her - it is funny to think that you will be friends for the next 6 years, or maybe for life.

"Hoggers, follow me!" calls out an older girl from the front of the line, and you all file after her obediently.

The girl leads you for what seems like ages, along long winding stone passageways that at times are so smooth that they must have been built by magic, at other times so rough and uneven that you keep tripping. They pass by soaring windows with beautiful stained glass scenes showing witches on broomsticks and unicorns jumping over rainbows. They run low underground in damp dark tunnels that are lit only by the occasional flickering torch.

At last just as your feet were starting to drag with tiredness, the girl leading the way stops abruptly.

"Well done everyone," she says. "We've arrived. Welcome to Hedgehog House tower."

You realise that you have stopped just before a stone archway painted in the Hedgehog House colours of brown. The stone arch itself is carved into the shape of a hedgehog stretched over the path.

"Now Hoggers," continues the girl. "Remember that it is only Hedgehog House students - Hoggers - who can enter this tower. So if you have friends in other houses..." the children around you make tutting and pshaw sounds "...you will have to meet them somewhere else!

"First years we still have a bit more walking to do but you will be able to rest soon so keep going."

With that she turns and strides through the archway. You, Kensley, and all the other children follow her. Beyond the archway is a winding stone staircase that spirals slowly upwards. After 500 steps you lose count and you just plod on, eyes only on the step in front.

Just at the point when you were beginning to wonder if there is any more tower left to climb you bump into Kensley who has come to a sudden halt in front of you. The whole line of children has stopped and you can hear them whisper to each other: "There's a door at the top, the girl is opening the door...".

You can't see the door yet because it is around another turn of the spiral staircase but you hear a creaking sound as it opens. Unexpectedly, a fresh earthy smell wafts down the staircase.

The children shuffle upwards.

When you reach the doorway you stop and stare. You can't believe what you are seeing. Rather than the top of a tower as you expected the stairs have led to a short tunnel that emerges from... the side of a hill. In the distance you can see - impossibly - Hogsnorts School. Somehow Hognsorts School is both just behind you in the passageway and at the same time it is far away across the broken countryside.

By some powerful magic the Hedgehog House staircase has taken you a mile away from the school and then deep underground.

You look around the grassy hillside that you have emerged onto and see a series of smooth stony paths branching out all over the hill. The paths lead past circular doors set into the hill. Over each circular door is a small sign.

You read the one closest to you: "Brian Banana" it says.

"Ah there we go!" You hear a voice behind you and someone shoulders past, walks to the door and goes inside.

"See you later Brian!" someone shouts out.

So that must be... Brian Banana, you think. And that door leads to his own little hole... and if he has a hole... everyone must have a hole, including me!

"Kensley," you cry out, full of energy again. "Let's find our holes!"

You both run off huffing down the path and before long you see a round door, painted green, with your name written on a sign above it: "Arthur Otley". Next to it is another door with "Kensley Potato" spelled out above.

You push on the shiny yellow brass knob in the centre of the green door and it swings open.

You are confronted by the most comfortable little living hole you could imagine: lined with wood, and carpeted, there are polished chairs and pegs for coats. The tunnel (because it was a tunnel really, not a hole as you had first thought) winds on into the side of the hill, with rooms leading off it left and right: bedrooms, bathrooms, cellars, pantries, wardrobes, all well stocked. In the rooms to the left of the tunnel deep-set round windows look out onto the hillside and meadows beyond, with Hogsnorts School far away.

After passing a dozen rooms, including one that seems dedicated to gaming with four different types of games console in it, plus a virtual reality headset, you arrive at your own bedroom, warm and comfortable. You lie down on the soft welcoming bed that occupies half the room. While you eat the mint chocolate that you found on the pillow, and cuddle the soft hedgehog toy, also left for you on the bed, you find yourself smiling.

In this little Hogger-hole safe underground you feel relaxed and secure. As your eyes close and you drift off to sleep your last thought is that, yes, I could be happy here.

94.
School hero

It takes you just an instant to decide.

No way are you going to join forces with a bunch of insects and take over the school! The school is just fine the way it is. The only problem is... you are not sure how Azog is going to react when you tell him you are not joining his insect army.

You fiddle nervously with something in your pocket and realise it is the golden ring that dropped out of Kensley's pocket. Almost without you noticing it slips onto your finger.

Immediately there is uproar in the dungeon.

"Where did he go!" Azog is roaring out. "Where is the chosen one!"

Insects are scuttling to and fro, Azog is still shouting, but not one of them is looking at you.

Then it dawns on you: the ring must be have made you invisible! You remember that the writing on the ring said 'In ghostly darkness shroud you' and now you are completely hidden by its powerful magic.

"Never mind the boy!" roars Azog. "We rise without him - follow me!"

From out of cracks in the walls, ceiling and floor crawl millions upon millions of arthropods: beetles, woodlice, ants, millipedes, earwigs, spiders in a great stream heading for the dungeon door and up into the school.

Back flat against the wall and hardly daring to breathe, you wait for them all to pass - a great river, a torrent of arthropods - and when the last millipede has marched out of the door, you wait another five minutes and then quietly tip toe after them.

Sometime later when you emerge out of the dungeon door into the school, the atmosphere is still, quiet, menacing. But there is a faint hum of noise - coming from the Great Hall.

You quietly slip into the Great Hall from a side door, and have to jam your fist into your mouth to stifle a shriek of horror.

The insects, led by Azog, have wasted no time in herding all the students and teachers out of their beds and into the hall. The students are sitting on their benches looking terrified, and at the front of the hall you see the teachers. They are wrapped up in an impossibly large spider web, stuck fast. Surrounding them all on the walls and the ceiling is the numberless insect army.

You look up and this time you can't prevent a little gasp. Slumblebore himself, the greatest wizard of the age, is spun up like a dead fly and is dangling upside from the ceiling, slowly spinning on an enormously thick silk thread fixed to his ankles.

On the stage Azog is haranguing the crowd with his harsh, strident voice.

"...and no more will insects be trodden on, squashed and abused. The Order of the Arthropods has begun and you will all acknowledge me, me me..." Azog's voice echoes strangely around the room.

Despite your crippling fear you know what you have to do.

Walking softly around the edge of the Hall, you creep on to the stage and behind Azog, the spider king.

Protected by the invisibility of your magic ring, no one notices you as you quietly, oh so quietly, step towards Azog, who continues to cajole and threaten the students.

You raise your foot and bring it down in one swift movement, right on top of Azog.

Squelch.

The spell transformed him permanently into the weasel you see now - and gave Wesley an enduring hatred of all Snakefang House students.

96.
The first feast

Everyone on Snakefang table cheers and greets you with the traditional 'welcome hiss' for new members.

"Welcome to Snakefang House Arthur!" says one girl who grins with pointed canines. "Hogsnorts is the best school in the country and Snakefang is the best house in the school. That means you are now the best of the best!"

She leaps to her feet suddenly and yells out "Snake House rules!"

The other children in Snakefang House stand up in a flash, answering her with their own shout of "Snake House rules, yah, sssssssss" sticking their tongues out and waggling them from side to side.

You grin broadly and let out a hiss of your own. This is the place for me alright, you think. Snakefang House: the best of the best. Oh yeah.

You are even happier when - the rest of the House Sorting complete - Slumblebore magically conjures up an incredible feast for dinner.

From out of thin air materializes platters of roast beef and boiled sprouts, Yorkshire pudding and mashed turnips, shepherds pie and boiled broccoli, toad in the hole and boiled potatoes, bubble and squeak and boiled carrots, apple crumble with strawberry ice cream, and spotted-dick drowning in custard.

"Strawberry ice-cream, my favourite!" Snako Malboy, who has also just been chosen for Snakefang House, licks his lips.

You and Snako get talking over dinner about your favourite flavours of ice-cream (his is strawberry, you like bubblegum flavour) and before long you are firm friends.

Halfway through the dinner, in a rite of initiation, all the first years crack open the eggs they received from Percy the Picking Pigeon. They pour the contents into a giant metal bowl on the Snakefang House table, and whisk them together. The older children heat the meal bowls with fiery jets from their magic wands and soon everyone in Snakefang House is sharing in a giant pigeon egg omelette.

As you chomp on your portion and feel the warm egg slide down your throat you feel your transformation into a Snakefanger is complete.

Then it's back to the regular food. You eat more than you have ever eaten before, enjoying yourself immensely. You wonder if Slumblebore is somehow making the food magically disappear after it enters your stomach, in a similar way to how he made the food appear on the table. But finally you realise you can't cram anything more into your belly, and let out a huge belch.

"Children!" Slumblebore stands, his beard streaked with mashed turnips and the odd boiled potato. He raises his hands for silence. "Children! Now we have eaten our fill it is time for bed. Prefects lead the students to the House towers. And remember: the dungeons are off limits this term. We don't know what's down there, and neither do we want to."

The children rise to their feet, clutching their distended tummies, and prepare to leave the hall.

You turn to Snako Malboy and say:

98.
The great Azog

Perched on the shoulder of Professor Knid you and Daniel can just make out an averagely sized spider gazing at you thoughtfully through his compound eyes.

"But, but... he's just a common spider... from the arachnid family paratropididae if I am not very much mistaken."

"Have some respect!" snaps the Prof. "The Great Azog is of average size for a spider. And he is from an impeccable blue blooded family."

"Size isn't everything, young Arthur," says King Azog the spider on the Prof's shoulder. "As you yourself - a first year - well know."

"But Mr Azog," you ask "What's so special about me?"

"Your wand shows that you are special Arthur. The core of your wand has a strand of silk from my bottom. Do you know how many other wands contain my silk? None whatsoever. Yours is the only one. You and the wand were made for each other.

"You and your wand therefore have an unmatched power over all spiders in the world, as I do. But with your wand you are also bonded to me. Our fates are entwined, threaded together. Together we could achieve anything.

"That's why I brought you here: to join me.

"You didn't bring me here!" you protest. "I came here by myself, I chose to come here."

"You may think you did but every step of the way I was guiding your steps, bringing you closer.

"Who guided you to the disabled toilet in Leeds Railway station, which led you to Hogsnorts? I was the spider that showed you the way.

"Who gave you the courage to face Percy the Picking Pigeon by biting you on the bum?" I was that spider.

"Who showed you the way to the dungeon door? I was that spider too."

"But what do you want from him?" interrupts Daniel suddenly. "You want Arthur to join you but what are you asking him to do?"

"The time will soon come" says the Great Azog "For you to make your choice. This time one that really matters. But first I have a decision to make."

With that the Great Spider King of average size, who had been talking to you from the shoulder of Professor Knid all this time, takes a few quick steps sideways over to the Professor's neck and, without warning, bites down with his fangs.

Instantly Professor Knid collapses to a heap on the dungeon floor and starts snoring.

102.
Cut through the web

"Vamos varita vencer vistosamente!" you exclaim as dramatically as you can manage.

You swipe the nearest strand of spider silk. Despite it being as thick as a steel cable and twice as tough, the light sword slices through it with no effort at all and the spider web flops to the floor.

You steadily walk forwards, cutting through the spider web with your magical golden light sword, feeling the magic from the wand course through your body. The falling cobwebs settle into overlapping spiral patterns on the floor.

103.
Epilogue

After taking over the school it was easy to recruit new students to your side. Attracted to your power the whole of Snakefang House joined you immediately. The Ravenclaws took a little bit longer to win over but after you had put a few of them in the dungeon for a while, most of them realised that you were serious and joined your force. The Hoggers of Hedgehog House joined you when the Ravenclaws gave in.

It was only the Lionpaws who didn't join you but by then you already had enough students to put the second part of your plan into action.

You split the students into groups of four. Each quartet was assigned a small insect army to help them. Using teleportation magic each group went to a different country and sneaked into the president's house.

At exactly the same minute of the same hour of the same day your magical minions appeared before the presidents of every country in the world, whether they were in their office, asleep in the bedrooms or having a bath.

You personally assigned yourself the President of the United States, Snako at your side.

"What the...? What's goin' on here? Who are you guys?" floundered the president of the United States as you, Snako, two other wizards and a million termites materialise out of thin air into the Oval Office.

"Don't bother to call your guards Mr President" you say with a wolfish grin, "They are fast asleep in the next room and they won't wake up until you tickle them under the armpits. I am here to inform you that a new world order has begun! The Order of the Arthropods! From now on you take orders only from me."

The President didn't like it - of course he didn't - but you menace him with the termites and he sees he has no choice.

Putting an enchanted earwig behind his ear, you explain to the president that whenever you have orders for him you will communicate through the earwig who will whisper into his ear hole.

"You'd better do whatever he says Mr President" adds Snako, "Otherwise we'll set the termites on you."

And then you vanish, leaving behind a puff of smoke and a million twenties who crawl into cracks in the floor and walls, ready to spring out if called.

The next morning the world wakes up to some startling news. All the presidents of every country in the world have simultaneously announced three new laws for everyone:

  • All the children of the world are allowed to play video games for as long as they like every day (even if it is bedtime).
  • Ice cream (at least three flavours) will be made available at every meal, as a starter.
  • Harming insects is a crime.

You smile happily as you listen to the news on the television while licking your breakfast ice cream.

You wonder what your next instructions will be...

CONGRATULATIONS - YOU HAVE ACHIEVED THE WORLD DOMINATION ENDING!

While Azog is talking he is getting steadily closer and closer to you. You find yourself mesmerised by his eight tiny compound eyes.

Perhaps you should take a stand, remake the world with Azog and the insect hordes, take over the school... on the other hand if you were to stop Azog now you would be a hero and would surely win the house cup for Snakefang - didn't Slumblebore promise you a million points?

106.
The great Azog

Perched on the shoulder of Professor Knid you see an average sized spider gazing at you thoughtfully through his compound eyes.

"But, but... he's just a little spider!"

"But King Azog," you ask "What's so special about me?"

"Your wand shows that you are special Arthur. The core of your wand has a strand of silk from my bottom. Do you know how many other wands contain my silk? None whatsoever. Yours is the only one. You and the wand were made for each other.

"You and your wand therefore have an unmatched power over all spiders in the world, as I do. But with your wand you are also bonded to me. Our fates are entwined, threaded together. Together we could achieve anything.

"That's why I brought you here: to join me.

"You didn't bring me here!" you protest. "I came here by myself, I chose to come here."

"You may think you did but every step of the way I was guiding your steps, bringing you closer.

"Who guided you to the disabled toilet in Leeds Railway station, which led you to Hogsnorts? I was the spider that showed you the way.

"Who gave you the courage to face Percy the Picking Pigeon by biting you on the bum?" I was that spider.

"Who showed you the way to the dungeon door? I was that spider too."

With that the Great Spider King of average size, who had been talking to you from the shoulder of Professor Knid all this time, takes a few quick steps sideways over to the Professor's neck and, without warning, bites down with his fangs.

"Watermelon?" you repeat.

"Yes: watermelon. I chose this password because it is my favourite fruit. Then you must descend the staircase that leads down into the very depths of the school. In the past students would be imprisoned in the dungeons for detention. Now they are mainly used to store broken chairs and Christmas decorations. But we go down there so infrequently there is no telling what evil is brewing in some dark corner."

Faint but clear, almost as if those feet were... marching."

108.
Taking cover

Dashing round the corner you raise your wand and yell "Paraguas pronto!"

To your astonishment, from the end of your wand pops out a translucent sparkly golden umbrella.

In a flash it opens up - it is big enough to cover both you and Snako, which is just as well because in that same moment there is another popping sound and three more splotches of superheated acid from the beetles bottoms fly through the air towards you.

Splat splat splat!

The acid hits the magical golden umbrella, protecting you from harm.

But not the golden umbrella. In a few moments the acid has dissolved it to nothing, just a little bit of umbrella handle is left poking out of the end of your wand.

The three giant bombardier beetles raise their rear ends at you, and make menacing chittering noises.

109.
Knid's insects

You raise your hand and ask "Aren't snakes better than insects? They're bigger and cleverer for a start."

"Spoken like a true Snakefang student! Snakes! Pshaw. But Snakefangers are not known for their perspicacity, are they? No boy, snakes are not better than insects.

"Firstly: snakes can't fly but insects can. Insects have been flying for over 350 million years! And to think we are always so impressed by the birds. Look at me, look at my feathers, I'm a bird! But insects have been flying for twice as long as birds - birds only evolved 150 million years ago. Pathetic.

"Secondly: a snake's cleverness is nothing compared even to an ant, who - working together - can build homes hundreds of times taller than they are. Skyscrapers! With air-conditioning, nurseries, storage chambers. And what is a snake's home? Just a pile of old logs. Pathetic.

"Thirdly: how many snakes are there in the world? Not many I can tell you. Or how many reptiles even? All the snakes, iguanas, and lizards put together?

Reptiles make up only 0.1% of all animal species.

Insects species make up 70% of all animal species, and if we include all arthropods that's over 80%. That means for every one reptile species (like a snake) there are more than 600 insect species.

"No, it is clear to me, as it should now be clear to you, that snakes are pitiful, almost inconsequential creatures compared to insects and arthropods."

"But sir," interrupts Snako, "insects are disgusting..."

"Oh the cheek of it! Who is to say that you are not disgusting young man with your.... goggly eyes and snotty nose? There will come a day - and maybe sooner than you think - when everyone will appreciate the magnificence of an insect, when people don't shudder when I brush past them with my cloak. Yes you will appreciate those 'disgusting' insects soon enough my boy."

Professor Jape paused and pinched the bridge of his nose with two fingers. "Class dismissed. Your homework is to write an essay with the title 'What I love most about insects and arthropods'. Two thousand words minimum."
