110.
Dinner time

Joining a gaggle of other Hogger students you head off on the long winding route back to the Hogsnorts Great Hall to get your dinner.

You take a seat at the Hedgehog table and look around you, amazed.

Tonight Slumblebore has enchanted the walls and ceiling of the Great Hall to look like a lush and humid jungle. But the perspective of the students sitting in the hall is as if they are a tiny creature in the undergrowth - blades of grass tower above them, giant ants scurry past and occasionally birds that appear to be the size of aeroplanes swoop overhead.

You stare wide eyed as a stag beetle lumbers past you, each footstep making the ground vibrate. It is a fantastic, incredible scene, and a bit scary

"Don't forget to eat Arthur!" Kensley reminds you with a smile.

You look down to see yet another incredible feast.

In keeping with the enchanted hall, where the ceiling and walls show everything huge, normal food has been enchanted to an enormous size. Garden peas the size of tennis balls are piled on a plate. Sausages the size of small boats lie lengthways on the table swimming in gravy. Roast potatoes bigger than your head sit in a dish that would be considered big if it was a bathtub.

It is all so delicious you can't stop an involuntary dribble which you quickly wipe from your chin with the table cloth.

You cram food into your mouth and gulp it down.

In a bizarre magical twist, as soon as the food is in your tummy it returns to its normal size, so you have to eat vast quantities of the enchanted sausage and veg to fill yourself up. This suits you and Kensley just fine - eating is one of your favourite things!

When you are finally reaching the end of the meal the enchanted scene suddenly transforms into a terrific battle as a stream of army ants overruns the jungle undergrowth attacking everything in their path with their fearsome mandibles. The Great Hall appears to be picked up and carried along by these implacable insects, and enchanted chairs tilt crazily as you ride along on the back of the army ant horde.

It is looking grim for the students and several Hedgehog House students, including Kensley, vomit on the floor, overcome with fright and motion sickness.

But just at the point the ants are taking the Great Hall down into their underground lair, in this intricate magical simulation, a small herd of ant-eaters charge onto the scene. Their long flexible tongues lash out from side to side, slurping up ants by the thousand and soon the army ant horde is no more, leaving the Great Hall in peace once more on the forest floor.

"Hooray for Hogsnorts, hooray for Slumblebore!" you shout, delighted at the evening's entertainment, even if it was a bit scary. You lead the Hoggers in a chant of "Hoggers up, Hoggers down, Hoggers hoggers stand your ground" and everyone cheers in general merriment, ending the best dinner you have ever had.

Turning to Kensley you say.

112.
The dark web

You and Kensley start pushing at the spider web with your hands.

It is amazingly strong and also sticky. When you push a strand it becomes harder and harder to unstick your hands.

"Arthur", cries Kensley, "Help me, I'm stuck!"

You turn to the side and see that somehow Kensley has got herself totally tangled up in the web - she is hanging upside down with spider webs curled round her ankles and her hair brushing the floor.

"Oh dear oh dear, I'm going to see if I can get through to help you Kensley" you reply but as you try to move over towards her you feel thick ropes of spider web curl around your legs and lift you up into the air. In an instant you are as helpless as she is.

You feel your panic rising as you struggle. Who is going to help you now? No-one even knows that you are here except perhaps Slumblebore.

"Oh no! Look Arthur - spiders! Millions of spiders!"

Kensley is right. Crawling out of the cracks of the walls, floor and ceiling is a host of spiders. They scurry along the webs heading towards you. In a sudden insight you realise that these spiders have made the webs themselves, working as a one enormous team to add strand after strand of spider silk until they had created these rope-thick cobwebs. So many spiders working as one! What could they not achieve together?

Then all thoughts flee from your mind as the wave of spiders reach you. They stop inches away.

One lone spider - no bigger than the rest - scuttles out of the pack, delicately steps onto your robes then up to your neck. You see a flash of tiny fangs then you fade into unconsciousness.

114.
Mirror mirror on the walls

You and Daniel decide to investigate the nearest stone staircase. From the bottom all you can see is that it winds up to some shadowy and little visited part of the school.

At the top of the stone stairs, you encounter a passageway lined with suits of armour. The empty helmets are turned in your direction and twist to follow you and Daniel as you walk past. You wonder what curious magical enchantment is making them move: the whole effect is rather clever.

At the end of the corridor there is a single door which swings open on silent hinges at your touch.

The room inside is small, dark and bare - but not quite empty.

Next to one wall there is a mirror, with the words above it 'Look at me if you dare, you will see your soul laid bare'.

Opposite, against another wall there's another mirror. Above this one it says 'Stare at me and you will see, what you want to come to be.'

Daniel relaxes. "I know what these are! They're mirrors of desire. They show you what you most want in your whole life, maybe even something you didn't even realise. We've got one of those back home in the bathroom."

"That's remarkable!" you breathe, and step up in front of one of the mirrors nervously.

You look at your reflection in the mirror and see...

...a taller, grown up version of yourself. You are wearing a flowing white gown, sun glasses and in your hand you are holding some papers. Squinting more closely you can just make out the title written in the papers: 'A synthesis of science and magic, how to join the two most powerful forces in the universe and create limitless, free electricity without any pollution'. Behind Arthur in the mirror you can make out a huge crowd of admirers.

"Look at me in the mirror Daniel, I look like the cleverest man in the world!"

Then you catch the reflection of the mirror behind you in the mirror in front of you - the reflection of the reflection.

In that reflection you are quietly reading a comic, sitting on a comfortable sofa, while drinking a steaming cup of hot chocolate.

"That's funny," you say. "The reflection of my reflection in the mirror behind me doesn't look quite as smart and cool at all..."

Then it dawns on you.

That famous brain box version of yourself doesn't want all that fame and attention. It's all too much. It would be too much for me! What you are seeing is the famous boffin version of you's most earnest desire - which is for a quiet life, reading a Dogman comic.

You angle your head to catch more reflections of reflections and see the images of yourself curve away into infinity.

With each reflection's reflection the boffin version of yourself is just that little bit less boffinated and the quiet version of yourself becomes a little bit less quiet. Far into the depths of the mirrors you can just make out an Arthur just like yourself, waving back at you.

You shake your head, confused, and tell Daniel what you saw.

"That's it!" he says. "Don't you see? The person you really want to be, when you get right down to it, is yourself."

1. Pondering the profound implications of this idea, you and Daniel leave the room of the mirrors, walk back along the corridor past the suits of armour, down the winding stone staircase to end up back where you started, at the centre of the school ~ Go to number 267

115.
The heart of the dungeon

You remember that woodlice are one of the few creatures that are completely immune to magic of any kind, and decide to cast a heat spell to clear a path indirectly.

You raise your wand. "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A magical flame whooshes out of your wand, sending golden sparks shooting.

The flame doesn't harm the woodlice, but it heats the air, and dries it. The woodlice have no option but to retreat: without moisture they can't absorb oxygen, they would suffocate.

This leaves a path.

"Wait!" says Aaron. "I... I can't go any further."

"What's wrong?"

"It's the woodlice. I have had a terrible fear of them ever since one rolled up my nose as a baby. I can't... I just can't go on."

"Listen Aaron, it's ok. I'll keep going but you should turn back and tell Slumblebore what we have found down here: the spider webs, the beetles, the woodlice. He needs to know what's going on."

"Yes, yes... thank you Arthur. Slumblebore needs to know," says Aaron in relief. "I'll go and get help."

Aaron turns and hot-foots it back the way you came.

As his hurried footsteps fade into the distant darkness, you breathe deeply and plunge forwards past the woodlouse army who are retreating to the still moist cracks in the stone.

After walking further down the dank, chilly passage you come to an iron bar door.

Just beyond you can hear a faint murmur of voices.

This is it: the heart of the dungeon. Whoever or whatever has been setting these traps for you and Aaron must be here, at the bottom of it all.

118.
Knid's spell

You sit still not wanting to encourage the professor, and none of the other students wants to disagree with him either.

"Good. Good." says Professor Knid. "Now we are all agreed, I can tell you that today we will be studying the marvellous woodlouse. Flies, deliver the woodlice!"

At this command, a hundred or so flies detach themselves from Knid's cape, zoom over to a box on the professor's desk and pick up the woodlice, one between four flies. The flies then carry one woodlice to each student and drop it onto the desk in front of them. The flies buzz back to Professor Knid and reattach themselves to his cloak.

The little woodlouse on your desk appears disturbed at this unexpected flight. It takes one look at you then rolls up into a ball.

"Now can anyone move their woodlouse using a magic spell?" asks Knid. "Try any magic spell that you know."

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlouse and mumble "abracadabra" rather hopefully.

You are delighted to see a little sparkle of gold stars shoot out of the end of your wand. The sparkles hit the woodlouse... and bounce right off! The woodlouse is unmoved.

Looking around the classroom you can see that the other children are having no more success than you did.

Aaron singed his own eyebrows when his lightning spell bounced off the woodlouse and hit him in the face. Kensley Potato's ice spell has frozen her desk into a solid block of ice but not touched the woodlouse. Brian Banana (another student from Hedgehog) has tried to make his woodlouse disappear but accidentally lost his wand in the process.

"The woodlouse, children, as you are discovering, is completely impervious to magic. So if you want to move the woodlouse you must first understand the woodlouse. And the one thing that scares the woodlouse more than anything else is drying out. As soon as they lose their moisture they die. Now - look at this."

Professor Knid raises his wand in an impressively expansive gesture and recites: "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A large flame whooshes out of the end of his wand and starts to bake the air around the woodlouse on his desk. Terrified of being dried out, the woodlouse unrolls and scuttles away as fast as he can.

"So we can see that indirect magic can be powerful against even magic resistant creatures. And we didn't have to harm any arthropods in the process. Now children it's your turn. Wands at the ready!"

You look down at your cowering woodlouse and, aiming with your wand, recite the words of the spell:

"Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

From the tips of your fingers to the ends of your toes you can feel a powerful magic charge building in your body. It concentrates in your chest and then zooms along your arm and out of your wand in a very impressive jet of flame.

You are overjoyed at the result, the first time you have cast such a powerful spell. Just think what you could do with such magic!

The woodlouse feels the magical flames heat the air and desk around him, and scarpers.

"I did it!" you cry, and commit the words of the spell to your memory: fiel fresa fusila fuego.

1. Feeling delighted you head back to the hall to decide what to do next ~ Go to number 225

119.
Bunking off

"Let's take a look around, lessons can wait!" you say to Daniel and the two of you walk down the wooden corridor (which is actually the hollow inside of just one great branch of this mighty tree) towards the trunk.

You enter the tree trunk about three stories up, and you can see Ravenwing students darting to and fro across the floor, heading off to their lessons. Some of them are whistling for parrots who fly off into the depths and retrieve arcane books, scrolls of ancient wisdom, and the occasional comic.

Soon they have all gone allowing you and Daniel the chance to explore uninterrupted.

The first place you go to is a room labelled 'FRUIT CORNER", just across the trunk from you. Fruit Corner turns out to be a large spherical room, with woody growths emerging from the walls and ceiling. At the end of each growth hangs a fruit that looks a bit like a giant strawberry and glows with a faint golden light.

You pick one from a branch and nibble the end tentatively. Immediately your eyes light up and you cram more into your mouth.

"It's..." scrunch "the best thing..." scrunch "I have ever tasted..." scrunch "in my whole life!"

It's like eating the best fruit salad you can imagine but also as if a luscious cream has been mixed in plus dollops of honey. After eating just one of these magical fruits you find you are completely full - and not in a feeling-sick-sort-of-way but in a totally-satisfied-and-not-at-all-feeling-sick kind of way.

The rest of the day is spent climbing up the inside of the tree trunk and sliding at tremendous speeds down the spiral wooden slides that are naturally polished with amber.

You also find a door in the tree to go outside and clamber around the branches for a while. You encounter the magical giant squirrels that live in the canopy - once normal red squirrels, eating the nuts of the tree has given them the power of speech as well as growing them to the size of kangaroos.

They invite you to climb on their backs, and they race to the top of the tree with you and Daniel clinging onto their fur and shouting with delight.

You swim in the pools of streaming water far out in the branches, captured in natural dips of the wood, and heated by some magic of the tree itself.

You meet the ancient raven with only one eye who lives at the very top of the tree, the raven that was befriended by the founder of Ravenwing House, Rebecca Ravenwing, all those centuries ago.

Finally you go back to the library inside the trunk of the tree and whistle for all the books you can think of.

Daniel reads 'Travels through the multiverse' by Daniel Colliers-Wood, a mind-blowing book which he will write in 25 years time. Also 'The Crying Potato' by his brother Robin Colliers-Wood, due to be published in only five years.

You enjoy 'Adventures with Dragons' by Arthur Otley and also 'Mr Poopy Head' by your brother Evan Otley, which he will write when he is only seven.

As you eat just one more delicious fruit-salad-fruit from the fruit corner room, the other Ravewing students traipse back into the massive trunk.

"Arthur, Daniel," shouts one anonymous bit-part student. "it's dinner time!"

120.
Back to the Tower

"Let's go back to the House Tower," you say to Aaron. "I'm tired out, it must be really late now."

The two of you trudge wearily back to the Lionpaw House Tower. It is a long way but somehow you remember the path perfectly - perhaps due to some 'homing' magic that all Lionpaw's absorb when they first go to the Tower.

Before long you have climbed the stone staircase and are in the Grand Lionpaw House Vestibule - the huge open space at the base of the tower, lit up with beautiful magical light-globes, and marble floor polished to a sheen by giant enchanted snails, and a faint smell of chlorine from the water park. You feel your spirits lift: could anyone have a better home to come back to than this?

You both wearily climb the final stone staircase to your sleeping apartments, and enter.

Throwing your robes over the sofa, you have a quick refreshing shower in the ensuite bathroom, dry yourself with an enormous fluffy white towel, tuck yourself up into your luxurious four-poster bed and drift off to sleep.

1. You wake up in the morning refreshed and happy. ~ Go to number 153

121.
Slumblebore's office

Slumblebore's office is easy to find, you just follow the signs pointing the way. When you reach it you see that the door is slightly ajar - and there is a light still on inside. Perhaps Slumblebore has gone to bed and forgotten to turn the light out.

You motion Snako to wait outside and he nods vigorously. "Don't get caught!" he whispers.

You push on the half open door and immediately hear a voice:

"Come in Arthur." It's Slumblebore - you've been rumbled!

"Don't worry," Slumblebore says as if reading your thoughts. "I have been waiting for you to come. I wanted to talk with you."

You walk into Slumblebore's office and look around you. Every inch of space has been used. Leather bound books on bookshelves line the walls. Paintings with ornate golden frames are hung all around, and ancient Hogsnorts headteachers stare down at you, blinking and sniffing. From the ceiling hang silver cages containing magical golden birds, tiny jewelled monkeys no bigger than your thumb and baby dragons curled up and sleeping. On the floor pentagrams have been marked out in yellow chalk and you almost trip over a live weasel dressed in a little red waistcoat that must be a weird pet. You resist the urge to give it a kick.

Slumblebore himself is sitting behind a massive wooden desk, piled high with manuscripts, scrolls, steaming goblets, plates of watermelon, little bowls of nuts and weasel droppings.

"Care for a raisin?" Slumblebore offers, brushing some weasel droppings onto the floor and proffering you a bowl.

"Err no, thank you," you reply, not entirely convinced that the bowl is 100% raisins.

"Arthur, I'm glad you have come. There is something very serious for us to discuss, which concerns the safety of the entire school. I need your help. But first tell me, how are you settling into the school? Do you feel happy in your new house?"

............................................................

1. "Yes it is amazing," you reply. "But what did you want to talk to me about?" ~ Go to number 238

2. "Well, I do like the school," you say. "But I'm not sure that I am in the right house. I don't feel like I really belong there." ~ Go to number 264

3. You idly reach out a hand to pat the weasel as you consider the question. ~ Go to number 95

122.
School hero

It takes you just an instant to decide.

Whipping out your wand you cry "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!" and flames shoot out, bathing the dungeon in flickering light. No way are you going to let Slumblebore down and the insects take over - you are going to save the school!

You were aiming your magical fire at Azog but he is too nimble and leaps out of the way.

"You will regret your choice Arthur," screams the spider king in outrage. "Insects, attack!"

From out of cracks in the walls, ceiling and floor crawl millions upon millions of arthropods: beetles, woodlice, ants, millipedes, earwigs, spiders in a great stream heading straight for you.

This time you don't hesitate. You turn and flee.

Your heart pounding, you run back out of the dungeon up towards the school. But you are not running out of cowardice. You have a plan.

When you reach the enchanted door that leads down into the dungeon you dash through and slam it shut. You can hear the enchanted locking mechanism clicking shut.

There's only one way for the insects to get past the door now - through the keyhole. You turn and wait, your wand at the ready.

As soon as you see the first hairy little leg poking out of the keyhole you use your wand as a flamethrower shouting "fiel fresa fusila fuego" again and again until your voice is hoarse.

The air is full of the harsh high pitched cries of dying arthropods and the sizzle of roasting chitin. But still the insects come, propelled onwards by the Great Azog's iron will.

You are getting tired now, your arm is sore from being held up so long and you can feel your reserves of magical energy running out. You cannot hold out much longer.

For a moment the magical fire from your wand flickers and dies.

Then three things happen simultaneously:

One: Azog, sensing his chance, launches himself through the keyhole aiming straight for your face.

Two: Aaron and Slumblebore run round the corner to see you standing alone against the numberless insect foe.

Three: You draw your compass from your pocket, thinking that even as your magic fails you will be able to stab a few more of the blighters with the pointy end before you are overwhelmed.

Then...

Azog flies through the air, fangs at the ready, just as your arm holding the compass comes up. He impales himself on the point of the compass, which buries itself deep in the spider king's abdomen.

The last words of Azog the Great are "Arthur... you have broken my heart...". Then a trickle of blue blood seeps out of the wound and Azog is no more.

With Azog a gonner the rest of the arthropod hordes lose all cohesion. When Slumblebore cautiously opens the door to the dungeon they are fleeing in all directions, and will trouble the school no more. Slumblebore lets off a few more blasts of fire to encourage them on their way.

"You did it Arthur!" cries Aaron. "You saved the school - the evil has gone!"

You stand still and listen carefully. Aaron is right. You cannot sense evilness any longer. The dungeons have been cleansed.

"Well done indeed Arthur," and Slumblebore, turning back to you. "I had a feeling that you were the special one. Without you I fear we would have been overrun by insects by now."

"It was Eric Knid," you say to Slumblebore. "It was Professor Knid who summoned the insect army, with Azog the spider king. He is down in the dungeon now unconscious. Azog bit him."

"Eric did you say? Well I'm not surprised. He always struck me as a bit of an odd fish. Nevermind we will pick him up in the morning and I shall give him an official reprimand. And if he does it again I will have no choice but to put him on a performance improvement plan."

"But you Arthur, what else can I give you but my most heartfelt thanks." You can't suppress a broad grin and feel a warm glow in your heart at Slumblebore's praise. "You truly are a hero, a hero of Hogsnorts School."

1. The next day... ~ Go to number 82

123.
The Order of the Athropods

You hold out your hand to Azog and he puts his tiny spider legs on the tip of your finger. Looking into your eyes, he nods his head and climbs up onto your hand then up your arm and onto your shoulder.

"Athropods, prepare yourselves!" shouts out Azog and out of the walls and ceiling untold millions of insects emerge, each one pitifully small but together forming a huge unstoppable army.

"Today we have a new leader! He is the chosen one whose coming to the dungeon was foretold. He stands here before you: Arthur Otley!"

Marvelling at the hordes of insects at your command you feel dizzy and excited. You realise that the insects of the world have been overlooked and deserve justice - with you in charge. You raise your arm and clench your fist.

"For too long has the insect world been downtrodden - literally - in this school," you say. "From now on there will be a new house, above the four houses of Lionpaw, Ravenwing, Snakefang and Hedgehog. It will be a new Order to rule them! The Order of the Arthropods!"

At the head of the insect army you and Azog pour out of the dungeon and into the school.

You stride into Slumblebore's office with Azog on your shoulder and millions of insects crawling on the floor, walls and ceiling just behind you.

Slumblebore is inside talking agitatedly to Aaron. You quickly appraise them of their situation: you have a vast insect army, they don't.

Offering Aaron a position as second in command of the Order of the Arthropods, you are delighted when he agrees to join your side.

You offer Slumblebore to continue in his role as headmaster, but only if he acknowledges you as Supreme Governor, and accepts that the Order of the Arthropods will from now on win the House Cup every year forever. Otherwise you will instruct your insect hordes to take over by force.

Slumblebore is reluctant, but he has no other option. If insects are seen running amok in the school it will be terrible publicity and the parents will withhold their school fees.

The next morning Slumblebore calls a general assembly of the school and announces the new order. The insect's army is hidden in cracks in the walls but ready to leap out if necessary.

"And so," Slumblebore concludes,"Arthur Otley must now be obeyed by everyone. Furthermore, there is a new school rule: anyone caught stepping on a spider or squashing an ant will be imprisoned within the dungeon - for life."

There are shocked gasps around the room. Only now do they truly realise the new reality - the Order of the Arthropods has begun!

Professor Jape

"Today we are going to learn some offensive magic. Now as you probably know offensive magic can be extremely dangerous. But that's not to say we can't have a bit of a laugh and a giggle as we go along eh? Eh children? Eh?"

125.
Cut through the web

"Vamos varita vencer vistosamente!" you exclaim as dramatically as you can manage.

A flickering golden light slowly extends from the top of your wand until it is about a metre long. You swing the "light sword" around and it makes a satisfying swishing zooming sound. This should do the trick.

You swipe the nearest strand of spider silk and despite it being as thick as a steel cable and twice as tough, the light sword slices through it with no effort at all and the spider web flops to the floor.

You steadily walk forwards, cutting through the spider web with your magical golden light sword, feeling the magic from the wand course through your body.

Soon the spider web has gone. You and Aaron race down the passageway and skid around a corner...

126.
Inner peace

"I'm Arthur Otley and I want to learn some spells" you say to Professor Blavatsky.

"Ah so impatient. And yet this impatience stops you learning about yourself. I can see that you are very far from self control as yet."

The teacher stands up and raises one hand.

"But do not worry, any of you. Because we will start with a simple meditation session to help you gain control."

You groan inwardly. This sounds boring.

"Close your eyes everyone," begins Professor Blavatsky. "Make sure you are comfortable in your seats. Now I want you to focus on your breathing. Breathe in. Breathe out. Breathe in... and breathe out.

"Feel the breath flowing into your nostrils. Concentrate on the sensation. Do you feel your nose hairs tickling? Perhaps a small bogey flapping around in your nasal passage? Just think about the breath, how it feels."

Despite yourself you feel your awareness sharpening, and you do indeed feel a small bogey in your nostril wobbling around as you breathe in and out.

"Now I want you to think about a special number. The special number is 42. A four and then a two. Forty two. This number is not just a number it is also a place. A location. A place of calm that you can always turn to in moments of difficulty or stress.

"This number 42 is a place within yourself, but it is a real place too that anyone can reach, if they just turn to that number... the number 42. As you turn to 42, just keep your thumb here so you know where to come back to."

Amazingly you feel a sensation as if you are floating somehow, except with your thumb stuck down in front of you. Concentrating fiercely you try with all your might to turn to 42. You float away...

...

"Did anyone manage to meditate and reach 42?" asks Madam Blavatsky.

You definitely feel you went... somewhere. You think this is what Professor Blavatsky meant.

"Any time you find yourself in need of quiet and peace, just repeat this meditation exercise and think of the number 42 and you will find a place of calm and relaxation - but keep your thumb right where you are and you will be able to turn back whenever you want."

"Class dismissed! We will meet again."

1. As if in a daze you and the other children rise slowly to your feet and walk out of the classroom. You do feel as if maybe you know yourself a little better now. ~ Go to number 133

127.
Jape's spell

Along with most of the other children you keep your hands down.

"You don't want to hear my jokes? Well I never!" Professor Jape looks genuinely hurt for a moment, but quickly recovers his composure.

"Perhaps you will be laughing on the other side of your face by the end of this lesson." Jape gives another high pitched giggle and you all shift on your seats uneasily.

"Maybe," he continues, "you will enjoy this one. I need a volunteer!"

No one volunteers so Jape scans the classroom. He points at Kensley.

"You! Come forward."

Kensley shuffles forward to the front of the class.

Without any warning Professor Jape whips out his wand, points it at Kensley and yells: "Vamos varita vencer vistosamente!"

A golden light extrudes from the tip of Jape's wand. The light looks like a solid sparkly golden beam and extends for one metre then stops emerging. Jape swings his wand around and you realise that he has created a magical golden light sword! As the golden beam swipes through the air it makes alarming swishing zoom noises.

"En guard!" snaps Jape to Kensley with a gleam in his eye before suddenly launching into a frenzied attack, swiping left and right with his light sword. In a flash he has covered the 5 metres to Kensley and he holds the light sword directly at Kensley's throat.

"If you don't laugh at my jokes I will kill you." Jape says simply.

There is dead silence in the class. Everyone is holding their breath.

Then, almost in exact unison, everyone screams and runs out of the door, except Kensley who is rooted to the spot in fear, and you partly because you don't want to abandon your friend, and partly because you are too afraid to move.

Professor Jape lowers the light sword and gives a high pitched giggle.

"I were just joking, didn't you know that?" he said to the fleeing children. "It were just a joke!" he shouted louder at their fleeing backs.

Professor Jape sighs and says to you and Kensley: "They can't take a joke, can they? Well lessons over now I suppose. But remember: Vamos varita vencer vistosamente that's a good one that is!"

You and Kensley nod and swallow, and without saying another word, flee out of the classroom.

129.
Spelling trouble

"I know I am called Arthur Otley," you say. "But is my name who I really am?"

"Excellent point Arthur! I can see by your question that you are already on the path to enlightenment. Because it is only when we realise that we don't know everything that we can learn."

Madame Blavatsky smiles at you. "And because you are ready to learn I will now teach you your first spell."

"But first can anyone tell me," she says addressing the whole class now, "what is the most common cause of death for wizards and witches? Anyone?"

"Fighting trolls?" suggests Aaron.

"Soul suckers?" proposes another child.

"Dragon fire? Werewolves? Vampires?"

"No, no and no again." replies Professor Blavatsky. "The one thing that is most likely to kill you more than anything else is: each other."

"Let me explain. Imagine it is night time, 3am in the morning. You hear a noise downstairs. Immediately you are on the alert. It could be burglars. Or more likely dark wizards on the attack. You creep downstairs, wand at the ready. You can hear them rummaging around in the kitchen. You leap out shouting the most deadly spells you can think of. Only to discover... it is your Uncle Brian who is visiting for the weekend and has come down in the night to help himself to a biscuit. Now he is paralysed on the kitchen floor, a look of horror on his face and the packet of biscuits grasped so tightly in his hand that no-one else will be eating them ever again."

"Yes I'm afraid to say that the most common cause of death is 'friendly fire', or over-reacting to an imagined threat. The sad fact is that you are all in far more danger from each other than from any evil sorcerer. Which is why the spell I am going to teach you to protect against dark magic is a sleeping spell. It is one I designed myself. To wake someone up from this spell you just need to tickle them under their armpits."

Blavatsky then whips out her wand and points it at Aaron.

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa!" she yells out.

A dart of pure golden light shoots out of the end of her wand and hits Aaron right in the middle of his forehead. In less than a half a second his head has sunk down to his arms on his desk and he is snoring like a sailor.

The class breaks out into a round of applause.

"Make sure you get the pronunciation just right when you cast the spell" Blavatksy advises as she walks over to Aaron and tickles him under the armpits.

"He he he! What happened?" says Aaron, confused.

The class splits into pairs and you practice sending each other to sleep. Because Aaron is still a bit drowsy you go first, pointing your wand at his forehead just as the teacher did:

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa..." you repeat carefully.

You feel a wonderful feeling of magical power gathering in your tummy. In an instant it has whooshed up out of your arm, channelled by the wand into a golden dart that zaps Aaron on the head, for the second time in as many minutes.

In no time at all he is asleep and snoring again.

"I did it!" you shout. "The magic spell worked!"

Delighted with your success you tickle Aaron under the armpits. As he wakes up giggling you try hard to memorise the spell 'Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa' - you never know when it may come in handy.

136.
Epilogue

The next day all the children are called to the school hall for a special announcement.

As you take your seats at the house tables you notice that the ceiling has been enchanted to a beautiful sky blue with fluffy clouds scudding past on one side and a huge flock of Monarch butterflies on the other.

"Students," announces Slumblebore from the front of the hall. "I have a very special announcement. Yesterday, unbeknownst to us, we were threatened by a vast and evil insect horde gathering in the school dungeon."

Slumblebore casts a severe glance at professor Knid, who looks down sheepishly at the table.

"We were saved thanks to the bravery, resourcefulness and cleverness of one boy.

"That boy is Arthur Otley."

You feel your cheeks go red as all the students in the school turn round to get a look at you and you hear whispers of "yes that's him", "defeated the insects single handed, with his friend Daniel!", "still just a first year!", and "wouldn't mess with that fella!".

"In recognition of his outstanding services to Hogsnorts School I am pleased to award: one million points to Ravenwing House!"

Deafening cheers come from the Ravenwings House students all around you.

"Did you hear that?" cries Daniel Colliers-Wood. "A million points! Last year Ravenwing house only got 600 points for the whole year! Now no-one will be able to beat us to the House Cup!"

"Lastly I hereby announce a new order of wizardry: the Order of the Arthropods. The purpose of this order is to further the study of insects under magical enchantment. And we will start with the source of all the trouble: the spider king Azog himself!"

The students cheer again as Slumblebore hands you a beautiful golden cage, with a still groggy Azog held prisoner within.

"Three cheers for Arthur Otley, hero of the school and founding genius of the Order of the Arthropods!"

With the cheers ringing in your ears you head straight for the magical laboratory with Daniel at your side, and Azog in his cage under your arm. Your head is full of all the insect related magical inventions you might create: enchanted chitin armour, spider silk swingers, acid blasters, who knows what else? With Azog to probe, you will be literally at the cutting edge of magical science and can't wait to see what you will learn!

CONGRATULATIONS - YOU HAVE ACHIEVED THE GENIUS OF THE SCHOOL ENDING

138.
Defense against Dark Magic

You decide to go to the Defense Against Dark Magic class next. With Slumblebore warning of danger lurking in the dungeon, you want to be prepared.

Professor Madame Blavatsky's classroom is tucked away in an inconspicuous side passage and you almost miss it as you walk past. The inside is much more impressive though, with the floor and walls covered in inky black runes and pictograms, protecting the room against baleful influences.

The professor herself is sitting cross-legged on a little platform at the front of the classroom with her eyes closed while the children file in.

She is a short lady, wearing black robes and, because she is sitting with her legs crossed, looks a little like a large black frog. Her face is pale, almost white, and you can see networks of blue veins under the skin near her temples, like a river draining into a swamp.

As the last child sits down, she opens her eyes.

Her eyeballs gleam white, her irises a brilliant blue.

"Welcome children, to Defence Against Dark Magic. The most important lesson you will learn today is..." Blavatsky's melodious, soothing voice pauses for a moment.

"...control over your own mind. Because it is only when you have full control over yourself that you can hope to resist the control that dark forces may wish to exercise upon you."

"And what is the path to self control?"

There is silence in the room.

"It is self awareness. It is only by knowing yourself that you can control yourself."

You look over at Aaron and raise your eyebrows. You were hoping for some good magic spells straight away, not this mumbo jumbo.

"But..." continues Madame Blavatsky, "I sense a doubter in the room. You!" She turns her blue eyes on yours and fixes you in her gaze.

"Have you already mastered yourself young man," she says to you. "Do you really know who you are?"

The blue eyes bore into you and you reply:

139.
Wesley the Weasel

You reach out a hand to pet the weasel, who allows you to pat him on the head.

"Ah, my pet weasel Arthur, do please go ahead and stroke him, by all means. Wesley craves human contact, as long as the human is not from Snakefang house. You see Arthur," Slumblebore explains as you stroke the weasel, "Wesley was not always a weasel. He was not always called Wesley either. Let me explain.

"Wesley used to be a real boy just like you Arthur. Then one day in an ill-tempered dispute with a Snakefang House student about who had the fastest broomstick, he was transformed by magic into the weasel you see before you. Unfortunately the spell was permanent."

Wesley listens to all this intently, and he leaps onto Slumblebore's desk, chattering his teeth in rage and frustration.

"As Wesley was an orphan I realised that the kindest thing to do would be to adopt him as my pet. My tailor on Hippotomews specially made his red waistcoat and matching hat. And I decided to give him his new name: Wesley, because Wesley the Weasel has a rather pleasing ring to it, don't you think? His boy name before that was Gary, which would never do. Or possibly it was Barry.

"Ever since then he has lived with me. We get along famously although I must admit that his table manners are not all that they might be - he has an unfortunate habit of defecating in the raisins."

Wesley hangs his head, shamefacedly.

"But do not let that worry you," says Slumblebore brightening. "Because every once in a while, I cast a spell to turn all the droppings in the room into raisins. Then they taste virtually identical in any case.

"Why do I tell you all this Arthur? Because I want you to know that for all my students I will always be there for them. I will always be there for you, when you need help the most. Always, Arthur, always. Metaphorically. Just like I was for Barry. Or was it Larry.

141.
Defense against Dark Magic

You decide to go to the Defense Against Dark Magic class next. With Slumblebore warning of danger lurking in the dungeon, you want to be prepared.

Professor Madame Blavatsky's classroom is tucked away in an inconspicuous side passage and you almost miss it as you walk past. The inside is much more impressive though, with the floor and walls covered in inky black runes and pictograms, protecting the room against baleful influences.

The professor herself is sitting cross-legged on a little platform at the front of the classroom with her eyes closed while the children file in.

She is a short lady, wearing black robes and, because she is sitting with her legs crossed, looks a little like a large black frog. Her face is pale, almost white, and you can see networks of blue veins under the skin near her temples, like a river draining into a swamp.

As the last child sits down, she opens her eyes.

Her eyeballs gleam white, her irises a brilliant blue.

"Welcome children, to Defence Against Dark Magic. The most important lesson you will learn today is..." Blavatsky's melodious, soothing voice pauses for a moment.

"...control over your own mind. Because it is only when you have full control over yourself that you can hope to resist the control that dark forces may wish to exercise upon you."

"And what is the path to self control?"

There is silence in the room.

"It is self awareness. It is only by knowing yourself that you can control yourself."

You look over at Snako and raise your eyebrows. You were hoping for some powerful magic spells straight away, not this mystic rubbish.

"But..." continues Madame Blavatsky, "I sense a doubter in the room. You!" She turns her blue eyes on yours and fixes you in her gaze.

"Have you already mastered yourself young man," she says to you. "Do you really know who you are?"

The blue eyes bore into you and you reply:

............................................................

2. "Well, I'm not sure. I know my name - it's Arthur Otley - but is that who I am or just what I others call me?" ~ Go to number 71

Lessons finished for the day

Strangely enough you find you can remember the way back there easily - the path had seemed so long and winding on your first day. Perhaps it was something to do with eating the Hedgehog Egg from Percy the Picking Pigeon that has given you a homing instinct for the Tower.

When you arrive, experiencing the odd sensation of going up the tower only to emerge out from a hole in the ground, you go straight to your Hogger Hole, sit down on the bench outside your front door, and put your feet up with a happy sigh.

143.
Spelling trouble

"I know I am called Arthur Otley," you say. "But am I defined by my name?"

"Excellent point Arthur! I can see by your question that you are already on the path to enlightenment. Because it is only when we realise that we don't know everything that we can learn."

Madame Blavatsky smiles at you. "And because you are ready to learn I will now teach you your first spell."

"But first can anyone tell me," she says addressing the whole class now, "what is the most common cause of death for wizards and witches? Anyone?"

"Cave trolls?" suggests Daniel.

"Dragons?" proposes another child.

"Harpies? Banshees? Herpes?"

"No, no and no again." replies Professor Blavatsky. "I'm afraid that the one thing that is most likely to kill you more than anything else is: each other."

"Let me explain. Imagine it is night time, 3am in the morning. You hear a noise downstairs. Immediately you are on the alert. It could be burglars. Or more likely dark wizards on the attack. You creep downstairs, wand at the ready. You can hear them rummaging around in the kitchen. You leap out shouting the most deadly spells you can think of. Only to discover... it is your Uncle Brian who is visiting for the weekend and has come down in the night to help himself to a biscuit. Now he is paralysed on the kitchen floor, a look of horror on his face and the packet of biscuits grasped so tightly in his hand that no-one else will be eating them ever again."

"Yes I'm afraid to say that the most common cause of death is 'friendly fire', accidentally hitting your friends and family with dangerous or deadly spells. The sad fact is that you are all in far more danger from each other than from any evil sorcerer. Which is why the spell I am going to teach you to protect against dark magic is a sleeping spell. It is one I designed myself. The benefit of this spell is that it is completely reversible. To wake someone up, you just need to tickle them under their armpits."

Blavatsky then whips out her wand and points it at Daniel.

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa!" she screams.

A dart of pure golden light shoots out of the end of her wand and hits Daniel right in the middle of his forehead. In less than a half a second his head has sunk down to his arms on his desk and he is snoring peacefully.

The class breaks out into a round of applause.

"Make sure you get the pronunciation just right when you cast the spell" Blavatksy advises as she walks over to Daniel and tickles him under the armpits.

"He he he! What happened?" says Daniel, confused.

The class splits into pairs and you practice sending each other to sleep. Because Daniel is still a bit drowsy you go first, pointing your wand at his forehead just as the teacher did:

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa..." you repeat carefully.

You feel a wonderful feeling of magical alertness gathering in your tummy. In an instant it has whooshed up out of your arm, channelled by the wand into a golden dart that strikes Daniel on the forehead, for the second time in as many minutes.

In no time at all he is asleep and snoring again.

"I did it!" you shout. "The magic spell worked!"

Delighted with your success you tickle Daniel under the armpits. As he wakes up giggling you try hard to memorise the spell 'Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa' - you never know when it may come in handy.

144.
Epilogue

The first kid to step forward is a boy named Snako Malboy from Snakefang house. Azog is perched on your shoulder and hisses in satisfaction as the pale boy approaches nervously.

Snako signs his name in your register and then utters a cry of alarm as Azog leaps onto his neck and sinks his sharp spider fangs into his ear lobe. But it is only to extract a harmless DNA sample from the boy's blood, and when the other children realise this more and more of them approach in the hopes that they too will be made superhuman.

Then the hard work begins.

With Azog, Daniel Colliers Wood and some of the more intelligent Ravenwing students you lock yourselves into a magical laboratory with the childrens' DNA samples. Collecting additional DNA from your insect army it is not long before you have created a powerful hybrid human-insect DNA serum, which you further refine into substrains for isolated traits: wings, antenna, hairy legs and so on.

By the time of school assembly on the following day you are ready.

"Fellow students!" you shout, holding up your hands for silence. "All those who signed up for the human-insect hybridisation program come to front of the hall!"

You instruct them to line up according to whichever insect enhancement they desire: one line for wings, another line for antennae, another for hairy legs and so on.

Each student swallows a magical pill the size and shape of a bluebottle and the transformations begin!

Yells of laughter and delight fill the great hall as the students sprout translucent wings out of their backs, long probing antennae from their foreheads and grow great ugly black hairs on their legs.

In no time at all they are zooming through the air, climbing up the walls and leaping from table to table, reveling in their amazing new powers - the age of the superhuman has begun!

But now it is time for the second - secret - part of your plan.

You and Daniel sneak back to the magical laboratory as the other kids fool around in the great hall. Even Azog doesn't know what you have planned now.

Back at the laboratory you quickly combine the different DNA serums into a single super fluid and mix in two hairs, freshly plucked from each of your heads. The liquid turns electric blue and froths golden bubbles.

You pour it into two matching goblets and hand one to Daniel. Clinking the glasses you look Daniel in the eye.

"See you on the next brain plane."

"I'll drink to that!" he replies and you both drain your glasses.

The other students and Azog have all of them been deceived. Into each serum you secretly added some termite DNA which has created a hive mind link directly to your and Daniel's brains, activated by your drink.

The brain power of all the children has been added to yours making you and Daniel 100 times cleverer than the cleverest person in human history. As an added bonus, every insect, and each student, is now under your direct control.

Too late the children flying around the Great Hall with their fantastic insect wings realise their predicament and their cries of dismay ring out.

You and Daniel smile at each other, a smile of superman intelligence and understanding. Communicating by pure brainwaves you speak directly into his mind:

"This experiment has been most satisfactory - what shall be our next invention?"

CONGRATULATIONS YOU HAVE ACHIEVED THE SUPERHUMAN MASTERMIND ENDING

145.
The prophecy

"Yes there is something I need to talk to you about Arthur, something very important," says Slumblebore.

"Ever since the end of the last school term I have sensed an evil presence in the school. An evil presence that is growing stronger by the day. All that I have been able to determine is that it is coming from the school dungeons. But what it is and where exactly it is down there I do not know. Whatever it is, is beyond my power."

Slumblebore looks at you directly, his bushy eyebrows waggling.

"This is where you come in Arthur. I need you to investigate what is going on in the dungeon. And deal with it."

"You want me to go to the dungeon!" you ask, amazed. "But you said at the school dinner that the dungeon was forbidden and no children were to go anywhere near!"

"Yes but Arthur don't you see? I can't just go around encouraging all the children to go down into the dungeons. Imagine if anything happened to them? Their parents would take Hogsnorts School to court, the fines could be crippling! No far better if you could just handle this quietly. And don't tell anyone that I told you to go down there."

"But I don't know hardly any magic!" you exclaim, "I've only just started magic school!"

"I agree you should learn one or two spells before you venture down. Pay attention to your teachers! What they teach you could save your life."

"But why me sir? Why not ask one of the older children to do it? Why don't you do it?"

"There is one thing I haven't told you Arthur. In the summer holidays I discovered an ancient prophecy concerning the school. It was written on a scroll that was so old that as soon as I touched it it turned to dust. It said:

'When darkness falls across your school. And evil threatens to rise and rule,
When monsters lurk around school ground. The boy called Arthur must be found.'

"Your coming has been foretold. If the prophecy is correct, only you can save us."

"And if you do this thing Arthur," Slumblebore adds, "I will personally award one million points for Lionpaw House."

146.
The Ravenwing House Tower

You and your new friend Daniel Colliers-Wood join the line of Ravenwing students flocking out of the dining hall. The older Ravenwings lead the way which is just as well as the route is so complicated you would have never found it on your own.

Down winding stone staircases that never seem to end. Over sloping flagstones that spiral upward for miles. Across innumerable stone courtyards where your steps echo from the walls.

You pass by magical stained-glass windows in which the colours change over time, making images of dragons breathing flames, or towering magicians leap over tree tops. You walk through dark stone tunnels which are only illuminated by occasional flickering torches.

At last your heart lifts as your weary feet take you to a stone archway framed in the Ravenwing colours of blue and copper.

"We've arrived everyone," announces a sixth year student from the front of the line. "First years, welcome to your home away from home for the next six years. Everyone else, welcome back! And remember - it is Wingers only who are allowed in here. The tree won't allow anybody else in."

"What tree?" you whisper to Daniel. "Is there a tree blocking the way?"

Daniel just shrugs his shoulders, his eyes wide.

Together with the other students you walk under the archway and you notice that the stone is carved in the shape of two intertwined wings. At the top of the arch is a carved-stone raven's head, beak open and pointing downwards.

On the other side of the arch is a stone staircase which you begin to climb.

As you climb you notice something strange: the air smells different, warmer somehow. And the stone steps themselves seem to be becoming softer, their edges smoother.

After a few more turns of the spiral stone staircase you realise that somehow the stone is morphing into a staircase made out of a single piece of wood. But it doesn't seem to be carved wood. Instead it is wood that has grown into this shape.

You keep walking upwards until your legs feel too tired to take another step, when at last you emerge into... a vast timber... room? But this enormous space is made of the same strange flowing, growing wood as the staircase. Then you realise where you are and your jaw drops open.

You and the other Ravenwing students have emerged into the inside of an impossibly giant living tree.

The hollow inside space - the tree trunk - where you are standing soars up seemingly forever. Living wooden ramps and stairs crisscross the space above your head, and you can see doorways scattered in the trunk at different levels. And lining the inside of the tree trunk for as far as you can see are what must be miles and miles of bookshelves, covered in books of every shape and colour imaginable.

"Arthur", says Daniel, "look at all those books!"

"That's right youngsters," says a kindly looking student a couple of years older than you. "This is the heart of the Ravenwing House Tower and the heart of the tree: the library. This is the largest library in the world. The largest in the magical and non-magical world," he adds proudly. "Every book that has ever been written and every book that will ever be written is somewhere on these shelves."

"But how do you find the one you want among so many?" you ask.

"Easy!" says the boy. "Just watch!"

Shaping a small hole with his lips, he lets out a warbling musical whistle. From high up in the trunk there is an answering warble, and you realise that perched up there is a whole flock of emerald green parrots. One of them flies down to your new companion and lands on his shoulder with a gentle squawk.

"What's your name first year?" the boy asks you with a smile.

"Arthur Otley."

"Ok. Polybius, bring me a book by Arthur Otley." The parrot launches himself into the air and flies up into the tree trunk.

You realise that Polybius must be the name of the parrot but you don't understand why the boy is asking for a book written by you. "But I haven't written any books," you explain.

"You mean you haven't written any books yet!" replies the boy. "Remember that this library contains all books including those that will be written in the future."

With that Polybius the parrot swoops down through the air, and drops a book from his claws into your hands. You look at the cover, which reads: "Adventures with Dragons, by Arthur Otley."

A huge smile appears on your face. "You mean I will write this?" you ask the boy.

"Of course you will, and if you are not sure what to write, you can just read it to find out."

As your head spins with possibilities, Daniel tugs on your sleeve. "Hey Arthur, let's go and find our bedrooms."

You allow Daniel to lead you off up one of the spiralling wooden ramps to a doorway high above the tree trunk floor. Above the doorway is a sign saying "BEDROOMS".

The doorway leads to a wide wooden corridor which you realise must be the inside of a branch of this great tree. Every now and again to the left and right are doorways with the names of students written above them. After a short while you come across a doorway that says "ARTHUR OTLEY" above it, next to one where the sign says "DANIEL COLLIERS-WOOD".

You go in and find yourself in a beautiful cosy little living room with some flow-wood armchairs and a sofa, leading to a spacious bathroom and a bedroom. As you go into the bedroom you can see the sun sinking below the horizon through an open window: the grounds of Hogsnorts School are far below you. At the centre of the bedroom is a luxurious circular bed. On top of the pillow is a foil-wrapped mint chocolate and a little raven cuddly toy.

You take off your shoes, throw yourself backwards on the bed and munch on the mint chocolate. Yes I think I can be happy here, you say to yourself, as you drift off to sleep with a smile on your face.

148.
Epilogue

The next day all the children are called to the school hall for a special announcement.

As you take your seats at the house tables you notice that the ceiling has been enchanted to a beautiful sky blue with fluffy clouds scudding past on one side and a fleet of giant floating zeppelins racing each other on the other.

"Students," announces Slumblebore from the front of the hall. "I have a very special announcement. Yesterday, unbeknownst to us, we were threatened by a vast and evil insect horde gathering in the school dungeon."

Slumblebore casts a severe glance at professor Knid, who looks down sheepishly at the table.

"We were saved thanks to the bravery, resourcefulness and pure gumption of one boy.

"That boy is Arthur Otley."

You feel proud and important as all the students in the school turn round to get a look at you and you hear whispers of "yes that's him", "defeated the insects single handed!", "still just a first year!", and "wouldn't mess with that fella!".

"In recognition of his outstanding services to Hogsnorts School I am pleased to award: one million points to Snakefang House!"

Deafening cheers come from the Snakefang House students all around you.

"Did you hear that?" cries Snako Malboy. "A million points! Last year the Snakefang house only got 500 points for the whole year! Now no-one will be able to beat us to the House Cup!"

"What is more," continues Slumblebore, "any unused Snakefang House points will carry over from one year to the next. Which by my calculation means that Snakefang House will win the House Cup for approximately the next... one hundred years." Slumblebore beams at you through his beard.

"Lastly I hereby announce a new order of wizardry: the Order of the Arthropods. Arthur I grant you first class membership of the Order. Three cheers for Arthur Otley, hero of the school and founding member of the Order of the Arthropods!"

The cheers ring out over and over again. The Snakefang students raise you up on your shoulders and carry you round and round the school hall in triumph shouting "Hooray for Arthur!"

"Wait!" you cry. "Professor Slumblebore, there is one more thing that I demand as my price for saving the school. I want all students, even the lumps in Lionpaw, to repeat after me."

Slumblebore nods - he knows how much he owes you.

"Snakefang House rules! Yah sssssssss!"

As you stick your tongue out and waggle it from side to side you are delighted to see all the other students in the school copy you.

You are even more delighted to see the expressions of extreme reluctance and distaste on the faces of the Lionpaw students as they repeat the Snakefang House chant, the chant of their oldest enemies.

You savour the sweet taste of victory and sneer at everybody.

Slumblebore's office

Beetle battle

151.
Dinner time

Joining a gang of other Snakefang students you head off on the long winding route back to the Hogsnorts Great Hall to get your dinner.

You take a seat at the Snakefang table (after a minor scuffle with some thick headed Lionpaw students) and look around amazed.

Tonight Slumblebore has enchanted the walls and ceiling of the Great Hall to look like the sub-tropical, volcano strewn world of the Jurassic. The effect is made even more magical by enchanting the floor to make it appear as if the Great Hall is strapped to the back of a huge lumbering sauropod - a brontosaurus perhaps - the chairs ensorcelled to vibrate with every lumbering step.

You stare wide eyed at the other giants of the sauropod herd to your left and ride, their long necks stretching forward as you cross an ancient Jurassic plain.

"Don't forget to eat Arthur!" Snako reminds you, elbowing you in the side.

You look down to see yet another incredible feast.

An entire flock of roast swans laid out in a row along the long table. Huge piles of frankfurter sausages, sizzled a beautiful golden brown. Crispy potato chips carved into all manner of spirals, whorls, and helixes. Pears smothered in mayonnaise. Baked bananas wrapped in delicious streaky bacon, stuffed with ketchup. Profiteroles the size of your head, full of light fluffy cream.

It is all so delicious you can't stop an involuntary slobber which you quickly wipe from your chin with the table cloth.

You cram food into your mouth and gulp it down.

When you are full you have a brisk food fight with Lionpaw table, pelting them with profiteroles and bread soaked in gravy - they return the attack with giant strawberries and chicken drumsticks. You shout with laughter when you hit one of the Lionpaw students, a boy called Aaron, full on the face with a giant profiterole and cream explodes everywhere. Snako gets hit in the eye with a boiled potato.

The food fight ends when the dinosaur enchantment on the walls and ceiling suddenly transforms into a battle scene as a gang of huge tyrannosaurus rexes charge from the side at the sauropods that you are riding. You scream and shout with the other students - Slumblebore's enchantment looks so real you can't help ducking as a huge t-rex slashes at you with claws the size of hockey sticks.

Chairs are leaning crazily as the sauropod carrying the Dining Hall tries to evade the ferocious T-Rex attack. The sauropods moan distress cries and fight back with tail whips and neck slams. Several Hedgehog House students vomit on the floor, overcome with fright and motion sickness.

It's complete pandemonium, which ends with the T-Rexes fleeing, defeated but blood dripping from their jaws where they have bitten off hunks of sauropod flesh.

"Snakehouse rules yah ssss!" shouts Snako at the top of his voice at the retreating T-Rexes, overcome with excitement, sticking out his tongue and flapping his hands by the side of his head.

This signals the end of the best dinner you have ever had.

Turning to Snako you say.

............................................................

1. I'm pooped, let's go back to the Tower and get some rest. ~ Go to number 268

2. "Hey, let's sneak out and explore the castle! It's too early to go to bed just yet." ~ Go to number 289

152.
Balls up

"Let's just walk over the woodlice," you say to Daniel. "I mean, we _are_ about a million times heavier than them. We _should_ just be able to squash them as we go."

"I don't know Arthur," replies Daniel, a look of trepidation in his eyes. "Do you really think it will work?"

In answer you take a determined stride forwards, towards the waiting woodlice hordes. They look back at you from their tiny little compound eyes, their little antenna waving in the air. Daniel sets off behind you.

The first couple of steps pass without mishap. A few of the woodlouse stragglers on the edge of the multitudinous crowd are flattened under the soles of your shoes and you smile, your confidence growing.

But then, as if some kind of telepathic signal passed between the woodlice, in exactly the same moment, there is a whisper of chitin and they simultaneously roll into tight balls - their defensive posture.

You try to stop your forward momentum but it is too late.

Your left foot propels itself through the air and comes down. Onto hundreds and hundreds of little woodlice balls. It is like stepping on a tray of marbles - you don't stand a chance. Your foot rolls on the little balls, grip on the floor hopelessly lost. It shoots forwards and your body shoots backwards - and downwards.

"Aaaargh!" you cry out, landing on the floor with a terrible crash, banging your head. Your fall has crushed to death thousands of woodlice but it is not enough, there are millions more to take their place.

As you slip into unconsciousness, you are vaguely aware of Daniel falling next to you, like a felled tree among the woodlice. You are not sure, but you think you can hear millions of tiny cheers.

Then - everything goes dark.

159.
Inner peace

"I'm Arthur Otley and I want to learn some spells" you say to Professor Blavatsky.

"Ah so impatient. And yet this impatience stops you learning about yourself. I can see that you are very far from self control as yet."

The teacher stands up and raises one hand.

"But do not worry, any of you. Because we will start with a simple meditation session to help you gain control."

You groan inwardly. This sounds boring.

"Close your eyes everyone," begins Professor Blavatsky. "Make sure you are comfortable in your seats. Now I want you to focus on your breathing. Breathe in. Breathe out. Breathe in... and breathe out.

"Feel the breath flowing into your nostrils. Concentrate on the sensation. Do you feel your nose hairs tickling? Perhaps a small bogey flapping around in your nasal passage? Just think about the breath, how it feels."

Despite yourself you feel your awareness sharpening, and you do indeed feel a small bogey in your nostril wobbling around as you breathe in and out.

"Now I want you to think about a special number. The special number is 42. A four and then a two. Forty two. This number is not just a number it is also a place. A location. A place of calm that you can always turn to in moments of difficulty or stress.

"This number 42 is a place within yourself, but it is a real place too that anyone can reach, if they just turn to that number... the number 42. As you turn to 42, just keep your thumb here so you know where to come back to."

Amazingly you feel a sensation as if you are floating somehow, except with your thumb stuck down in front of you. Concentrating fiercely you try with all your might to turn to 42. You float away...

...

"Did anyone manage to meditate and reach 42?" asks Madam Blavatsky.

You definitely feel you went... somewhere. You think this is what Professor Blavatsky meant.

"Any time you find yourself in need of quiet and peace, just repeat this meditation exercise and think of the number 42 and you will find a place of calm and relaxation - but keep your thumb right where you are and you will be able to turn back whenever you want."

"Class dismissed! We will meet again."

168.
Knid's spell

You sit still not wanting to encourage the professor, and none of the other students wants to disagree with him either.

"Good. Good." says Professor Knid. "Now we are all agreed, I can tell you that today we will be studying the marvellous woodlouse. Flies, deliver the woodlice!"

At this command, a hundred or so flies detach themselves from Knid's cape, zoom over to a box on the professor's desk and pick up the woodlice, one between four flies. The flies then carry one woodlice to each student and drop it onto the desk in front of them. The flies buzz back to Professor Knid and reattach themselves to his cloak.

The little woodlouse on your desk appears disturbed at this unexpected flight. It takes one look at you then rolls up into a ball.

"Now can anyone move their woodlouse using a magic spell?" asks Knid. "Try any magic spell that you know."

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlouse and mumble "abracadabra" rather hopefully.

You are delighted to see a little sparkle of gold stars shoot out of the end of your wand. The sparkles hit the woodlouse... and bounce right off! The woodlouse is unmoved.

Looking around the classroom you can see that the other children are having no more success than you did.

Snako singed his own eyebrows when his lightning spell bounced off the woodlouse and hit him in the face. Kensley Potato's ice spell has frozen her desk into a solid block of ice but not touched the woodlouse. Brian Banana (another student from Hedgehog) has tried to make his woodlouse disappear but accidentally lost his wand in the process.

"The woodlouse, children, as you are discovering, is completely impervious to magic. So if you want to move the woodlouse you must first understand the woodlouse. And the one thing that scares the woodlouse more than anything else is drying out. As soon as they lose their moisture they die. Now - look at this."

Professor Knid raises his wand in an impressively expansive gesture and recites: "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A large flame whooshes out of the end of his wand and starts to bake the air around the woodlouse on his desk. Terrified of being dried out, the woodlouse unrolls and scuttles away as fast as he can.

"So we can see that indirect magic can be powerful against even magic resistant creatures. And we didn't have to harm any arthropods in the process. Now children it's your turn. Wands at the ready!"

You look down at your cowering woodlouse and, aiming with your wand, recite the words of the spell:

"Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

From the tips of your fingers to the ends of your toes you can feel a powerful magic charge building in your body. It concentrates in your chest and then zooms along your arm and out of your wand in a very impressive jet of flame.

You are overjoyed at the result, the first time you have cast such a powerful spell. Just think what you could do with such magic! Just imagine how frightened people will be of your powers!

The woodlouse feels the magical flames heat the air and desk around him, and scarpers.

"I did it!" you cry, and commit the words of the spell to your memory: fiel fresa fusila fuego.

Just in time

1. You sit down in a chair next to Slumblebore's desk and prick up your ears. ~ Go to number 283

170.
Knid's spell

You sit still not wanting to encourage the professor, and none of the other students wants to disagree with him either.

"Good. Good." says Professor Knid. "Now we are all agreed, I can tell you that today we will be studying the marvellous woodlouse. Flies! Deliver the woodlice!"

At this command, a hundred or so flies detach themselves from Knid's cape, zoom over to a box on the professor's desk and pick up the woodlice, one between four flies. The flies then carry one woodlice to each student and drop it onto the desk in front of them. The flies buzz back to Professor Knid and reattach themselves to his cloak.

The little woodlouse on your desk appears disturbed at this unexpected flight. It appears to be of the species armadillidium vulgare - apparently they make good pets. It takes one look at you then rolls up into a ball.

"Now can anyone move their woodlouse using a magic spell?" asks Knid. "Try any magic spell that you know."

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlouse and mumble "abracadabra" rather hopefully.

You are delighted to see a little sparkle of gold stars shoot out of the end of your wand. The sparkles hit the woodlouse... and bounce right off! The woodlouse is unmoved.

Looking around the classroom you can see that the other children are having no more success than you did.

Daniel zapped his own ear when his lightning spell bounced off the woodlouse and zoomed back over his shoulder. Brian Banana (a student from Hedgehog House) has tried to make his woodlouse disappear but accidentally lost his wand in the process.

"The woodlouse, children, as you are discovering, is completely impervious to magic. So if you want to move the woodlouse you must first understand the woodlouse. And the one thing that scares the woodlouse more than anything else is drying out. As soon as they lose their moisture they die. Now - look at this."

Professor Knid raises his wand in an impressively expansive gesture and recites: "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A large flame whooshes out of the end of his wand and starts to bake the air around the woodlouse on his desk. Terrified of being dried out, the woodlouse unrolls and scuttles away as fast as he can.

"So we can see that indirect magic can be powerful against even magic resistant creatures. And we didn't have to harm any arthropods in the process. Now children it's your turn. Wands at the ready!"

You look down at your cowering woodlouse and, aiming with your wand, recite the words of the spell:

"Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

From the tips of your fingers to the ends of your toes you can feel a powerful magic charge building in your body. It concentrates in your chest and then zooms along your arm and out of your wand in a very impressive jet of flame.

You are delighted at the result, the first time you have cast such a complex spell. If you can cast a spell like this all by yourself you will be able to learn anything!

The woodlouse feels the magical flames heat the air and desk around him, and scampers away.

"It worked!" you cry, and commit the words of the spell to your memory: fiel fresa fusila fuego.

174.
Mirror mirror on the walls

You and Aaron decide to investigate the nearest stone staircase. From the bottom all you can see is that it winds up to some shadowy and little visited part of the school.

At the top of the stone stairs, you encounter a passageway lined with suits of armour. The empty helmets are turned in your direction and twist to follow you and Aaron as you walk past. Even though you know they are just regular suits of enchanted magical armour the effect is rather creepy.

At the end of the corridor there is a single door which swings open on silent hinges at your touch.

The room inside is small, dark and bare - but not quite empty.

Next to one wall there is a mirror, with the words above it 'Look at me if you dare, you will see your soul laid bare'.

Opposite, against another wall there's another mirror. Above this one it says 'Stare at me and you will see, what you want to come to be.'

Aaron relaxes. "I know what these are! They're mirrors of desire. They show you what you most want in your whole life, maybe even something you didn't even realise. My mum's got one of those in the downstairs toilet."

"That's amazing!" you breathe, and step up in front of one of the mirrors nervously.

You look at your reflection in the mirror and see...

...a taller, more handsome version of yourself. You are festooned with gold medals from the Olympics, and people keep approaching you from the side of the mirror to take your photo. Your hair is styled into a quiff and you are grinning with a fine set of bright white teeth.

"Wow look at me, I look so cool!"

Then you catch the reflection of the mirror behind you in the mirror in front of you - the reflection of the reflection.

In that reflection you are quietly reading a book sitting on a comfortable armchair with a fluffy dog at your feet.

"That's funny," you say. "The reflection of my reflection in the mirror behind me doesn't look cool at all..."

Then it dawns on you.

That gold medal champion version of yourself doesn't want all that fame and attention, he's tired of it - I would be tired of it. What you are seeing is the cool version of you's most earnest desire - which is for a quiet life, reading a book, with just a faithful dog as a companion.

You angle your head to catch more reflections of reflections and see the images of yourself curve away into infinity.

With each reflection's reflection the cool version of yourself is just that little bit less cool and the quiet version of yourself becomes a little bit less quiet. Far into the depths of the mirrors you can just make out an Arthur just like yourself, waving back at you.

You shake your head, confused, and tell Aaron what you saw.

"That's it!" he says. "Don't you see? The person you really want to be, when you get right down to it, is yourself."

When monsters lurk around school ground. The boy called Arthur must be found.'

"My faithful friends growing up were slugs, ants, flies and beetles. But my friends were mercilessly crushed, poisoned, and swatted by humans.
