178.
The Order of the Athropods

You hold out your hand to Azog and he puts his tiny spider legs on the tip of your finger. Looking into your eyes, he nods his head and climbs up onto your hand then up your arm and onto your shoulder.

"Wait - what?" enquires Daniel looking troubled.

"Trust me," you tell him. "I have a clever idea."

Azog is not troubled at all, he is delighted that you have joined him.

"Athropods, prepare yourselves!" shouts out Azog from his position on your shoulder. Out of the walls and ceiling untold millions of insects emerge, each one pitifully small but together forming a huge unstoppable army.

"Today we have a new leader! He is the chosen one whose coming to the dungeon was foretold. He stands here before you: Arthur Otley!"

Marvelling at the hordes of insects at your command you feel amazed and excited. You realise that the insects of the world do deserve justice. You wonder what they are capable of and how easy they will be to control - or not.

"For too long has the insect world been downtrodden - literally - in this school," you say. "From now on there will be a new house, above the four houses of Lionpaw, Ravenwing, Snakefang and Hedgehog. It will be a new Order standing aside from all the rest! The Order of the Arthropods! Our purpose will be human-insect harmony but first... we must earn the respect of the school."

At the head of the insect army you, Daniel and Azog pour out of the dungeon and into the school.

You stride into Slumblebore's office with Azog on your shoulder and millions of insects crawling on the floor, walls and ceiling just behind you.

Slumblebore is inside and you explain to him that there are about to be some big changes around here, and with a vast insect army behind you there is nothing he can do to stop them.

With a defeated sigh Slumblebore agrees to your demands.

The next morning Slumblebore calls a general assembly of the school and reads out your demands. The insect army is hidden in cracks in the walls but ready to leap out if necessary.

"Firstly" Slumblebore begins, "No one must squash, damage or belittle an insect, unless it is for the purpose of magical study."

"Secondly there will be a new House, the Order of the Arthropods, which will take precedence over all other houses, and even over myself as headmaster. Arthur Otley is the head of the Order of the Arthropods and he will rule for life. Daniel Colliers-Wood is second in command."

"Thirdly, a new program of insect-human magical hybridisation will begin. A tribe of new super-children will be formed. Anyone wishing to be enhanced with magical insect powers must provide a DNA sample to Arthur or Daniel at the end of this assembly."

There are murmurs of surprise and shock. The students realise that nothing will be the same again - the Order of the Arthropods has begun!

186.
Spelling trouble

"I know I am called Arthur Otley," you say. "But is my name who I really am?"

"Excellent point Arthur! I can see by your question that you are already on the path to enlightenment. Because it is only when we realise that we don't know everything that we can learn."

Madame Blavatsky smiles at you. "And because you are ready to learn I will now teach you your first spell."

"But first can anyone tell me," she says addressing the whole class now, "what is the most common cause of death for wizards and witches? Anyone?"

"Broomstick failure?" suggests Kensley.

"Poisoned potions?" proposes another child.

"Manitees? Dragons? Ghouls?"

"No, no and no again." replies Professor Blavatsky. "The one thing that is most likely to kill you more than anything else is: each other."

"Let me explain. Imagine it is night time, 3am in the morning. You hear a noise downstairs. Immediately you are on the alert. It could be burglars. Or more likely dark wizards on the attack. You creep downstairs, wand at the ready. You can hear them rummaging around in the kitchen. You leap out shouting the most deadly spells you can think of. Only to discover... it is your Uncle Brian who is visiting for the weekend and has come down in the night to help himself to a biscuit. Now he is paralysed on the kitchen floor, a look of horror on his face and the packet of biscuits grasped so tightly in his hand that no-one else will be eating them ever again."

"Yes I'm afraid to say that the most common cause of death is 'friendly fire', accidentally hitting your friends and family with dangerous or deadly spells. The sad fact is that you are all in far more danger from each other than from any evil sorcerer. Which is why the spell I am going to teach you to protect against dark magic is a sleeping spell. It is one I designed myself. The benefit of this spell is that it is completely reversible. To wake someone up, you just need to tickle them under their armpits."

Blavatsky then whips out her wand and points it at Kensley.

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa!" she screams.

A dart of pure golden light shoots out of the end of her wand and hits Kensley right in the middle of his forehead. In less than a half a second her head has sunk down to her arms on his desk and she is snoring like a sailor.

The class breaks out into a round of applause.

"Make sure you get the pronunciation just right when you cast the spell" Blavatksy advises as she walks over to Kensley and tickles her under the armpits.

"Ha ha ha! What happened?" says Kensley, confused.

The class splits into pairs and you practice sending each other to sleep. Because Kensely is still a bit drowsy you go first, pointing your wand at her forehead just as the teacher did:

"Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa..." you repeat carefully.

You sense an unnerving feeling of magical power gathering in your tummy. In an instant it has whooshed up out of your arm, channelled by the wand into a golden dart that zaps Kensely on the head, for the second time in as many minutes.

In no time at all she is asleep and snoring again.

"I did it!" you shout. "It worked!"

Delighted with your success you tickle Kensley under the armpits. As she wakes up giggling you try hard to memorise the spell 'Somnolencia salchicha sabrosa' - you never know when it may come in handy.

187.
Knid's insects

You raise your hand and ask "Aren't hedgehogs better than insects? They eat insects don't they."

"What an awful little squeaker you are! Hedgehogs! Pah! No boy, hedgehogs are not better than insects.

"Firstly: hedgehogs can't fly but insects can. Insects have been flying for over 350 million years! And to think we are always so impressed by the birds. Look at me, look at my feathers, I'm a bird! But insects have been flying for twice as long as birds - birds only evolved 150 million years ago. Pathetic.

"Secondly: a hedgehog may eat an insect, but after a hedgehog dies who has the last laugh? Insects that's who. Insects, working together will devour the hedgehog carcass until nothing is left, not even the bones. If it wasn't for insects we would have dead hedgehogs all over the place - you would be tripping over them every time you went out of your front door!

"Thirdly: how many hedgehogs are there in the world? Not many I can tell you. Or how many mammals even? All the hedgehogs, deer, humans, rabbits and elephants put together?

Mammals make up only 0.4% of all animal species.

Insects species make up 70% of all animal species, and if we include all arthropods that's over 80%. That means for every one mammal species (like a hedgehog) there are more than 170 insect species.

"No, it is clear to me, as it should now be clear to you, that hedgehogs are pitiful, almost inconsequential creatures compared to insects and arthropods."

"But sir," interrupts Kensley, "insects are disgusting..."

"Oh the cheek of it! Who is to say that you are not a disgusting young lady with your.... goggly eyes and grubby fingers? There will come a day - and maybe sooner than you think - when everyone will appreciate the magnificence of an insect, when people don't shudder when I brush past them with my cloak. Yes you will appreciate those 'disgusting' insects soon enough my girl."

Professor Jape paused and pinched the bridge of his nose with two fingers. "Class dismissed. Your homework is to write an essay with the title 'What I love most about insects and arthropods'. Two thousand words minimum."

188.
The dungeon door

You enter the passageway sloping downwards and after many twists and turns in the passageway you are hopelessly lost.

You notice a fascinating little spider running around a corner ahead of you - possibly a member of the paratropididae spider family. Curiously it then comes back round the corner, looks at you and waits, then lifts up a spindly leg and points.

"Arthur" says Daniel, "I think that spider wants us to follow him."

"Truly remarkable," you reply. "It appears to be demonstrating significantly more intelligent behaviour than the average spider. Let's see where it is going."

You follow the spider as it turns this way then that and are amazed and delighted to finally arrive at what must surely be the entrance to the dungeon.

"This is it Daniel," you say. "We've found it!"

A huge wooden door, banded with silver inlaid iron, stands within a stone archway. Either side of the door two antique sets of armour are positioned upright as if on guard.

The spider you were following scurries through the keyhole of the door and disappears.

Above the door there is a sign written in some archaic font, which reads: "DUNGEON".

You try the doorknob but it doesn't budge.

"There's a magical enchantment of locking on the door!" says Daniel. "We will need to cast a counter spell if we are to get through."

As you lift up your wand, you think carefully about a spell that could work.

189.
Balls up

"Let's just walk over the woodlice," you say to Snako. "I mean, we _are_ about a million times heavier than them. We _should_ just be able to squash them as we go."

"I don't know Arthur," replies Snako, a look of fear in his eyes. "Do you really think it will work?"

In answer you take a determined stride forwards, towards the waiting woodlice hordes. They look back at you (do they have eyes?) their little antenna waving in the air. Snako sets off behind you with a little whimper.

The first couple of steps pass without mishap. A few of the woodlouse stragglers on the edge of the multitudinous crowd are flattened under the soles of your shoes and you smile, your confidence growing.

But then, as if some kind of telepathic signal passed between the woodlice, in exactly the same moment, there is a whisper of chitin and they simultaneously roll into tight balls - their defensive posture.

You try to stop your forward momentum but it is too late.

Your left foot propels itself through the air and comes down. Onto hundreds and hundreds of little woodlice balls. It is like stepping on a tray of marbles - you don't stand a chance. Your foot rolls on the little balls, grip on the floor hopelessly lost. It shoots forwards and your body shoots backwards - and downwards.

"Aaaargh!" you cry out, landing on the floor with a terrible crash, banging your head. Your fall has crushed to death thousands of woodlice but it is not enough, there are millions more to take their place.

As you slip into unconsciousness, you are vaguely aware of Snako falling next to you, like a felled tree among the woodlice. You are not sure, but you think you can hear millions of tiny cheers.

Then - nothing.

191.
The dungeon door

As the other Hedgehog House students file off into the corridor on their way to Hedgehog House tower you and Kensley quietly tip-toe away to one side, making no more noise than little mice. After two or three turns of the passageway the hubbub of the other students has faded away to nothing.

"Where do we go now?" asks Kensley, her voice shaking a little with the audacity of what you have done.

You look around trying to get your bearings. You realise that the school is absolutely huge. There must be hundreds of corridors, archways, passageways and staircases. How will you even find the way to the dungeons?

But just at that moment you notice five spiders walking along the floor, lined up one after the other. How curious, you think, what are those little fellows up to? You and Kensley start to follow them along the corridor.

They turn left, right, right again, then left before disappearing under a door.

You look up. Above the door is a sign scrawled in thick black letters: DUNGEONS.

"I think this is the door to the Dungeons!" you whisper to Kensley, afraid to speak too loud in the silence. With a trembling hand you reach out to turn the great brass doorknob and open the door. But it doesn't budge, and as you pull on the doorknob the edge of the door glows golden.

"Look!" says Kensley to you quietly, "The door is locked with an enchantment. That means it will only open when you say the magic password."

Before you have time to speculate what the magic password might be, you hear the tramp of many feet coming towards you from around a corner. It must be a group of students on their way to their house tower! Before you have time to hide, they turn the corner and spot you.

"Arthur and Kensley isn't it? How did you two get here? Well never mind: join the line, we are all going to Hedgehog Tower now" To your surprise you are addressed by one of the older Hedgehog House students. You must have somehow taken a hidden shortcut when following the spiders.

Picked for Snakefang

Snakefang House! I must be in Snakefang House.

Coo coo Snakefang House is it? I can see that in this house you would be strong and powerful. But are you sure? asks Percy the pigeon, speaking directly into your mind now. Snakefangs are a bit, you know: evil..."

Yes yes, you think back at him. Not a do-gooder Lionpaw, not a too-clever-by-half Ravenclaw, not a boring old Hedgehog. I want to be a Snakefang - better than all of them!

Coo coo as you wish young Arthur, speaks Percy into your brain.

Slowly the great yellow eyes shrink to normal size and you are just staring at a regular giant talking pigeon again.

Percy waddles over to the centre of the hole where the light from the hall shines down. He looks old and weak - you wonder how long he has been doing this. For decades? Centuries even?

The giant pigeon settles down on the floor, and coos once or twice. He then stands up slowly and waddles back into the darkness at the edge of the hole that is his home. On the floor he has laid a large and beautiful egg.

The egg is striped in colours of silver and green. The colours of Snakefang House!

Your heart pounding with excitement, you pick up the egg and slowly walk back up the wooden stairs to the noise and light of the Hogsnorts Great Hall.

As you emerge out of the pigeon hole, Slumblebore sees your egg and shouts: "Arthur Otley, Snakefang House!"

194.
Defense against Dark Magic

You decide to go to the Defense Against Dark Magic class next. With Slumblebore warning of danger lurking in the dungeon, you want to be prepared.

Professor Madame Blavatsky's classroom is tucked away in an inconspicuous side passage and you almost miss it as you walk past. The inside is much more impressive though, with the floor and walls covered in inky black runes and pictograms, protecting the room against baleful influences.

The professor herself is sitting cross-legged on a little platform at the front of the classroom with her eyes closed while the children file in.

She is a short lady, wearing black robes and, because she is sitting with her legs crossed, looks a little like a large black frog. Her face is pale, almost white, and you can see networks of blue veins under the skin near her temples, like a river delta draining into a swamp.

As the last child sits down, she opens her eyes.

Her eyeballs gleam white, her irises a brilliant blue.

"Welcome children, to Defence Against Dark Magic. The most important lesson you will learn today is..." Blavatsky's melodious, soothing voice pauses for a moment.

"...control over your own mind. Because it is only when you have full control over yourself that you can hope to resist the control that dark forces may wish to exercise upon you."

"And what is the path to self control?"

There is silence in the room.

"It is self awareness. It is only by knowing yourself that you can control yourself."

You look over at Daniel and raise your eyebrows. You were hoping for some useful spells, this just sounds like nonsense.

"But..." continues Madame Blavatsky, "I sense a doubter in the room. You!" She turns her blue eyes on yours and fixes you in her gaze.

"Have you already mastered yourself young man," she says to you. "Do you really know who you are?"

The blue eyes bore into you and you reply:

196.
Dinner time

Joining a gaggle of other Lionpaw students you head off on the long winding route back to the Hogsnorts Great Hall to get your dinner.

You take a seat at the Lionpaw table (after shouldering some snivelling Snakefangs out of the way) and look around amazed.

Tonight Slumblebore has enchanted the ceiling and the walls to look exactly as if the Great Hall had become a giant spaceship exploring the galaxy. Stars whizz by on either side and every now and again you skirt a giant whirling black hole vortex. He has even enchanted the chairs to lean to the side when the spaceship turns a corner. You stare at the stars and nebulae whooshing past with wide eyes.

"Don't forget to eat Arthur!" Aaron reminds you, elbowing you in the side.

You look down to see yet another incredible feast laid out on the table. An entire roast hog with an apple in its mouth. Hundreds of chicken drumsticks covered in a delicious deep fried sauce, Kentucky style. Chips cooked to crispy perfection with overflowing bowls of tomato ketchup and mayonnaise to dip them into. Forests of broccoli, with cooked prawns hanging from the branches. Baked bananas, smothered in condensed milk and peanut butter. Strawberries, each the size of your fist with amusing faces carved into them and raisins for eyes.

It is all so delicious you can't stop an involuntary slobber which you quickly wipe from your chin with the table cloth.

You cram food into your mouth and gulp it down.

When you are full you have a brief food fight with Snakefang table, pelting them with giant strawberries and chicken drumsticks - they return the attack with profiteroles and bread soaked in gravy. You are particularly pleased to hit Snako Malboy in the eye with a boiled potato.

The fight ends when the space-scape enchantment on the walls and ceiling reveals a full scale alien spaceship attack. You scream and shout with the other students as Slumblebore simulates a spectacular laser battle.

Chairs are leaning crazily as the Dining Hall spaceship takes evasive action. Pretend laser bolts zap chicken drumsticks to ashes. Several Hedgehog House students vomits on the floor, overcome with motion sickness.

It's complete pandemonium, which ends with the total alien defeat, their broken vessels drifting through the void.

"North paw, south paw, we score, Lionpaw!" shouts Aaron at the top of his voice, overcome with excitement, boxing an imaginary foe.

This signals the end of the best dinner you have ever had.

Turning to Aaron you say.

197.
Epilogue

The next few years pass happily at the school.

You construct a dizzyingly high tower at the centre of the school, taller than all of the other house towers put together. The insects assist you with the building work, with the ants and termites being particularly helpful.

You make sure that it has the best waterslides, the best lava pools, the best library in the school and invite select other students to join you, such as Daniel Colliers-Wood, Kensley Potato and the rest of the Bleezeley family. Even Eric Knid is allowed a room in the tower. Snako Malboy is not allowed in.

Azog teaches you all a new spell: how to shoot sticky spider web from your wand. You soon get the hang of swinging from the ceilings with the spider web silk.

The insects are treated better now. They are allowed to come and go as they please. Even Slumblebore has come around to the new order and can often be seen conversing with the Great Azog in his office.

And you: you are content. You have come a long way since that first day when you flew into the Hogsnorts school hall. You rule Hogsnorts now, from the highest tower, and the insects are back on top.

CONGRATULATIONS - YOU HAVE ACHIEVED THE SCHOOL TAKEOVER ENDING!

201.
The Snakefang House Tower

Together with Snako Malboy, who is fast becoming your best friend, you join the line of Snakefang house children leaving the dining room on their way to the House Tower.

The route winds its way through the stone corridors of Hogsnorts School for what seems like hours: along high walls with battlements on one side and a steep drop on the other. Through dingy underground stone tunnels lit only by the occasional flickering torch. Up and down stone staircases with steps which sometimes seem built for a giant, and you have to clamber up one at a time, and at other times seem built for a gnome and you almost trip over them they are so small.

But at last you can sense from the excited chatter of the other students that you are getting closer. It also seems to be getting warmer - the cold dank of the school corridors has been replaced by a dry heat radiating from the walls.

Finally you reach a stone archway painted in the Snakefang House colours of silver and green.

"We're here Snakefangs, our home sweet home," states one of the older boys. "Everyone remember that only Snakefangs are allowed in the House Tower. Anyone else who tries to enter will get swallowed by the Blood Squirter, if they even get that far!" The children give a low chuckle.

"What's the Blood Squirter?" you whisper to Snako.

"I don't know," he whispers back with a bloodthirsty grin, "but whatever it is, it sounds super cool."

"In we go then!" commands the older boy and you all file through the arch. As you pass through you realise the arch is carved in the shape of an enormous open snake's mouth, its fangs dripping down like giant stalactites.

When you enter the tower your mouth drops open as you are confronted by a fantastic, almost otherworldly scene.

You are in a wide circular space paved with a shiny black stone. It is walled all around with a stone wall that rises upwards for as far as you can see, leaving a small circle of open sky at the top. It would be dark if it wasn't for the pool in the middle of this strange courtyard.

That's because the pool is full of glowing orange lava.

This must be the source of the heat you noticed in the corridor as you approached the tower. And basking on the edges of the lava pool are some huge snakes, each a different colour.

"This is so cool," you say to Snako, and walk forwards to get a closer look. When you reach the pool of lava, one of the snakes lifts his head (as big as yours) and flickers his tongue out in your direction. You carefully reach out a hand and stroke the snake's scaly chin. He makes a satisfied hissing noise.

"I can see he likes you," says an older girl who has walked over. "Say hello to Blood Squirter."

"So this is Blood Squirter - what a beautiful creature!" You turn to the girl: "This place is amazing, I love the snakes, the lava lake... But it doesn't look very... comfortable. Where does everyone sit down for a rest or to go to sleep?"

"This is just the central courtyard of the tower," shrugs the girl. "We don't hang out here much, it's mainly for the snakes or when we want to toast marshmallows. No - around the edge of this big tower everyone has their own personal smaller tower which you can get to by climbing the stairs."

You look at where the girl is gesturing and realise that this giant tower has a long stone staircase winding its way up the inside of the wall. Every now and again the staircase has a small landing leading to a locked door.

"You mean I have a tower just for me?" you ask, your eyes wide, and the girl nods.

"We have got to check this out," you say to Snako and the two of you run over to the stone staircase. As you climb you pass the locked doors that you noticed earlier and you see that each one has a name above them: Gertrude Viper-Collins, Bartholomew Beetlebottom, Lyra Poisonwood read a few.

After you have climbed the staircase high above the lava pool you notice two doors next to each other. Above one it says Snako Malboy and above the other Arthur Otley. You notice a much smaller sign next to the door too, which reads: 'Insert wand into key hole'.

With a thrill of excitement you slowly put the end of your wand into the keyhole of the door. After a moment the whole doorway is outlined in a magical golden glow and then - without a sound - the door swings inwards. At the door next to you Snako has done the same.

You and Snako take a deep breath, nod goodbye to each other, and enter.

You find yourself in the most wonderful room.

Whereas the courtyard below was bare and dim, this place is comfortable, light and airy. There are two or three sofas and comfy armchairs scattered around, tall windows on the room, looking down on the Hogsnorts School grounds, and a low table in front of the fireplace. You notice that the fireplace contains a little bubbling pool of lava, no doubt fed from the same source deep below the earth as the lava pool you saw earlier. A large TV and games console are nestled next to a window.

Kicking your shoes off and bouncing down onto a sofa, you notice a spiral iron staircase leading up to the second floor above you and realise that the girl you were talking to before was absolutely right. This is a whole tower just for you. The main Snakefang House Tower must be studded with hundreds of student towers, sprouting out the side of it like mushrooms.

Racing up the spiral iron staircase you find yourself in a large circular study room with a curved desk against one wall, some bookshelves against another, and a set of cupboards fully stocked with potent magical ingredients.

The next floor is a small kitchen with a magically replenishing larder to one side. Above that is the bathroom with a huge bath in the middle, propped up on four iron feet cast in the shape of snakes baring their fangs.

Above this is the bedroom, and above the bedroom under the sloping tower roof is a little astronomical observatory, complete with telescope.

Coming back down to the bedroom, you lie back on the enormous four-poster bed and crunch on a mint flavoured chocolate that you found on your pillow, next to a cuddly toy snake.

Through the window outside you can see the sun sinking slowly below the horizon.

You put your hands behind your head and smile. Yes, I could be happy here, you say to yourself as you slip into a deep untroubled sleep.

203.
Knid's spell

You sit still not wanting to encourage the professor, and none of the other students wants to disagree with him either.

"Good. Good." says Professor Knid. "Now we are all agreed, I can tell you that today we will be studying the marvellous woodlouse. Flies, deliver the woodlice!"

At this command, a hundred or so flies detach themselves from Knid's cape, zoom over to a box on the professor's desk and pick up the woodlice, one between four flies. The flies then carry one woodlice to each student and drop it onto the desk in front of them. The flies buzz back to Professor Knid and reattach themselves to his cloak.

The little woodlouse on your desk appears disturbed at this unexpected flight. It takes one look at you then rolls up into a ball.

"Now can anyone move their woodlouse using a magic spell?" asks Knid. "Try any magic spell that you know."

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlouse and mumble "abracadabra" rather hopefully.

You are delighted to see a little sparkle of gold stars shoot out of the end of your wand. The sparkles hit the woodlouse... and bounce right off! The woodlouse is unmoved.

Looking around the classroom you can see that the other children are having no more success than you did.

Kensley's ice spell has frozen her desk into a solid block of ice but not touched the woodlouse. Brian Banana (another student from Hedgehog) has tried to make his woodlouse disappear but accidentally lost his wand in the process. Snako has singed his own eyebrows when his lightning spell bounced off the woodlouse and hit him in the face.

"The woodlouse, children, as you are discovering, is completely impervious to magic. So if you want to move the woodlouse you must first understand the woodlouse. And the one thing that scares the woodlouse more than anything else is drying out. As soon as they lose their moisture they die. Now - look at this."

Professor Knid raises his wand in an impressively expansive gesture and recites: "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A large flame whooshes out of the end of his wand and starts to bake the air around the woodlouse on his desk. Terrified of being dried out, the woodlouse unrolls and scuttles away as fast as he can.

"So we can see that indirect magic can be powerful against even magic resistant creatures. And we didn't have to harm any arthropods in the process. Now children it's your turn. Wands at the ready!"

You look down at your cowering woodlouse and, aiming with your wand, recite the words of the spell:

"Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A strange tingling sensation builds in the tips of your fingers and toes and quickly builds until your entire body feels somehow charged up. Then with a feeling like a bit like doing a wee the magic zooms along your arm and out of your wand in a very impressive jet of flame.

You are delighted at the result, the first time you have cast such a wonderful spell! And a fire spell could be used for so many things - like roasting marshmallows or boiling the kettle.

The woodlouse feels the magical flames heat the air and desk around him, and scarpers.

"I did it!" you murmur with quiet satisfaction, and commit the words of the spell to your memory: fiel fresa fusila fuego.

............................................................

1. Feeling delighted you head back to the hall to decide what to do next ~ Go to number 135

204.
Professor Eric Knid Explains

A voice, strong and commanding, emerges from the darkness. "One of you? The saviour, a mere stripling first year? Impossible!"

Another voice, high pitched and chittery, answers him. "Yes Eric, I know him. He is the wand holder. The other one is a friend. Do not harm them - yet!"

As your eyes adjust to the gloom, you can make out a figure standing in the centre of the room. A wizard - someone you recognise.

"Professor Knid!" you exclaim.

"Yes Professor Eric Knid at your service! Or perhaps I should say that you will be at my service... Arthur isn't it? And Daniel?"

"Yes my name's Arthur. Arthur Otley." A sensation of fear congeals in your throat.

"And I'm Daniel Colliers-Wood," says your classmate. "Who were you talking to just now Professor Knid?"

"All in good time, Daniel..." with an unexpectedly swift movement Professor Knid draws his wand and shoots a spell of locking at the iron gate which clangs shut.

You are trapped.

"What are you going to do?" you ask.

Eric Knid smiled. Even in the dark you can see the mad gleam in his eye: "Revolution!"

"Explain why Eric." That chittering voice again, appearing out of nowhere.

"Yes - why. Why?" Professor Knid takes a deep breath. "Ever since I was a young boy I have felt an affinity with insects, spiders, crabs. With the Arthropods. A dog will bite you, not so an earwig! A lion may eat you, not so a woodlouse! A human may betray you, a spider will not.

"My faithful friends growing up were slugs, ants, flies and beetles. But my friends were mercilessly crushed, poisoned, and swatted by humans.

"The final straw? Slumblebore sat on a spider - and laughed."

"I couldn't bear it. I sought out the Great Spider King Azog himself. What joy when I found him in the forbidden bushes and entered his service. Together we have been gathering supporters here in this dungeon, insects and spiders in their millions. For revenge. For a revolution. To take over the school!

"No longer will it just be Lionpaw House, Ravenwing House, Snakefang House, and Hedgehog House! We will have a new house mightier than all of them. The Order of the Arthropods! And I will be headmaster."

"But why us?" fear chills you. "What has this got to with us?"

"It is Arthur who we need, he is the only one who can stop us now," says the mysterious high pitched voice. "But with you on our side we will be invincible!"

"Who is that speaking?" Daniel cries.

"This is the Great Spider King Azog himself. And you are honoured to stand in his presence." Professor Knid explains.

"Where?" You can't see anyone other than the Professor.

"Here!"

"Where, I can't see!"

"Right here, look! Closer!"

............................................................

1. You look closer. ~ Go to number 98

205.
Knid's insects

You raise your hand and ask "Aren't ravens better than insects? They're much smarter for a start."

"Ravens! Pshaw. I would have thought that a Ravenwing student like you would be a bit smarter yourself! No boy, ravens are not better than insects.

"Firstly: ravens may know how to fly but can't fly, but insects figured it out long before birds did. Insects have been flying for over 350 million years! But insects have been flying for twice as long as birds - birds only evolved 150 million years ago. Pathetic.

"Secondly: a raven's cleverness is nothing compared even to an ant, who - working together - can build homes hundreds of times taller than they are. Skyscrapers! With air-conditioning, nurseries, storage chambers. And what is a raven's home? Just a pile of twigs. Rubbish.

"Thirdly: how many ravens are there in the world? Not many I can tell you. Or how many birds even? 100 billion - at least that's what wikimagia says!

"But how many insects are there in the world? 10 quintillion! That's 10 followed by 18 zeros. For every one pitiful bird on the earth there are 100 million amazing insects.

"No, it is clear to me, as it should now be clear to you, that ravens are pitiful, almost inconsequential creatures compared to insects and arthropods."

"But sir," interrupts Daniel, "insects are a bit well, disgusting..."

"Oh the cheek of it! Who is to say that you are not disgusting to an insect young man? There will come a day - and maybe sooner than you think - when everyone will appreciate the magnificence of an insect, when people don't shudder when I brush past them with my cloak. Yes you will appreciate those 'disgusting' insects soon enough my boy."

Professor Jape paused and pinched the bridge of his nose with two fingers. "Class dismissed. Your homework is to write an essay with the title 'What I love most about insects and arthropods'. Two thousand words minimum."

Another chance

After a momentary sensation of vertigo, as if you have all of a sudden fallen, you sense that the golden light is fading away.

Opening your eyes you find you are at the bottom of a great stone well, with a circle of light far above. You realise that you have magically transported back to Percy the Picking Pigeon's hole in the Hogsnort's Great Hall, just as Slumblebore said you would. Somehow you know that you have also travelled back in time to before, when you had just arrived at the school. You are that Arthur once again in Percy's hole, but this time you can make a new choice.

207.
Balls up

"Let's just walk over the woodlice," you say to Aaron. "I mean, we _are_ about a million times heavier than them. We _should_ just be able to squash them as we go."

"I don't know Arthur," replies Aaron, a look of fear in his eyes. "Do you really think it will work?"

In answer you take a determined stride forwards, towards the waiting woodlice hordes. They look back at you (do they have eyes?) their little antenna waving in the air. Aaron sets off behind you with a little whimper.

The first couple of steps pass without mishap. A few of the woodlouse stragglers on the edge of the multitudinous crowd are flattened under the soles of your shoes and you smile, your confidence growing.

But then, as if some kind of telepathic signal passed between the woodlice, in exactly the same moment, there is a whisper of chitin and they simultaneously roll into tight balls - their defensive posture.

You try to stop your forward momentum but it is too late.

Your left foot propels itself through the air and comes down. Onto hundreds and hundreds of little woodlice balls. It is like stepping on a tray of ball bearings - you don't stand a chance. Your foot rolls on the little balls, grip on the floor hopelessly lost. It shoots forwards and your body shoots backwards - and downwards.

"Aaaargh!" you cry out, landing on the floor with a terrible crash, banging your head. Your fall has crushed to death thousands of woodlice but it is not enough, there are millions more to take their place.

As you slip into unconsciousness, you are vaguely aware of Aaron falling next to you, like a felled tree among the woodlice. You are not sure, but you think you can hear millions of tiny cheers.

Then - nothing.

208.
Magical mayhem

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlice menacingly and shout loudly:

"Dispara dinosaurio demente!"

From out of the end of your wand comes a faint but growing roaring sound, like an angry lion. The noise grows louder and louder until it is so loud it hurts your ears.

"Arthur, what did you do?" asks Daniel in alarm.

"I don't..." you begin, but before you can finish your sentence, a huge golden dinosaur head somehow forces it's way out of the tip of your wand, and roars again deafeningly.

"ROAR!!!"

"Did I ever tell you that I don't like giant angry tyrannosaurus rexes!" yells out Daniel, eyes with fear.

But there's nothing you can do, the spell has been cast. The enormous magical t-rex squeezes its way out of your wand and charges its way towards the woodlice, waggling its ridiculous little front arms in a demented fashion.

It launches itself at the nearest woodlouse which has no time to react.

But instead of crushing the woodlouse in its banana sized teeth, the t-rex - impossibly - just bounces off.

It roars and tries again, with the same result.

Then it hits you - woodlice are completely immune to magic.

The dinosaur appears to understand this too. It looks around for a better target. And it's crazy little red eyes fix on you and Daniel.

With a sense of horror you realise that the t-rex is now hunting you!

The rabid dinosaur leaps at you and Daniel but instead of eating you it flings you both into the stone wall on each side and you bump your head painfully. The t-rex stomps up the corridor before disappearing a puff of gold stars as the magic wears off.

As you slide down the wall and into unconsciousness, you can see the millions of woodlice waving their little antennae. As you close your eyes you think: are they laughing?

215.
The Order of the Athropods

You realise that _this_ is your destiny, to command the insect horde, to lead them.

You hold out your hand to Azog, who extends a spindly leg and climbs up your arm and onto your shoulder.

"Well done Arthur" says Azog, "You have chosen... wisely."

Millions upon millions of insects are looking at you with their two, four or eight compound eyes, eyes on the sides of their heads, eyes on stalks, all waiting. Waiting for your command.

"Insects!" you exclaim. "Arthropods! Follow me!"

Looking back, the rest of that night seems more like a fantastic dream than reality.

You lead the insect army up through the passageways out of the dungeon and into the school. But instead of leading them to the centre of the school as Azog expected, you show them the way to Hedgehog House tower.

From there the whole streaming mass of ants, spiders, earwigs, woodlice and beetles emerges onto the cool night air of the hillside where the Hoggers live in their holes.

"But Arthur," protests Azog. "I thought we were taking over the school!"

"No," you replied simply. "Fighting only creates more fighting. Where will it end? What we need is peace."

You carry on walking, and hear the whispers of the insects as they follow you: "peeece" they say, "peeeeeece".

Finally reaching the end of the lane of Hogger Holes you instruct them to dig.

Working together, before the sun has come up, the insects excavate a magnificent, glorious Hogger Hole of their own. While the door looks normal, and the initial tunnel is cosy enough to deceive the casual visitor - with umbrella stands and varnished wooden chairs with green velvet seats - soon the tunnel branches out into smaller and smaller passages, until they match the size of the insects that will live in them.

When the labour is complete, you turn to the tired, muddy, but happy insect multitude, and smile.

"Insects," you say, "welcome home."

216.
The heart of the dungeon

You remember that woodlice are one of the few creatures that are completely immune to magic of any kind, and decide to cast a heat spell to clear a path indirectly.

You raise your wand. "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A magical flame whooshes out of your wand, sending golden sparks shooting.

The flame doesn't harm the woodlice, but it heats the air, and dries it. The woodlice have no option but to retreat: without moisture they can't absorb oxygen, they would suffocate.

This leaves a path.

"Wait!" says Snako. "I... I can't go any further."

"What's wrong?"

"It's the woodlice. I have had a terrible fear of them ever since I accidentally ate one thinking it was a small nut. The feeling of its little legs wriggling in my stomach is something that has haunted me ever since. I can't... I just can't go on."

"Listen Snako, it's ok. I'll keep going but if you're too afraid you are no good to me down here anyway. You should turn back and tell Slumblebore what we have found down here. Tell him that I wasn't afraid and decided to carry on"

"Yes, yes... I will Arthur. Slumblebore needs to know," says Snako in relief. "I'll go and tell him."

Snako turns and hot-foots it back the way you came.

As his hurried footsteps fade into the distant darkness, you breathe deeply and plunge forwards past the woodlouse army who are retreating into the still moist cracks in the stone.

After walking further down the dank, chilly passage you come to a door made of iron bars.

Just beyond you can hear a faint murmur of voices.

This is it: the heart of the dungeon. Whoever or whatever has been setting these traps for you and Snako must be here, at the bottom of it all.

219.
The Lionpaw House Tower

You and Aaron join the train of students from Lionpaw house. All the first years are chattering to each other, excited to visit their house tower for the first time.

Your route twists and turns, down passageways and corridors, through archways and cloisters. At times you pass by stained glass windows that stretch far up to the high ceiling and coloured light streams through the passageway. At other times the stone lined walls are dark and low with just the occasional torch flickering from the wall to illuminate your passage.

At last the line of Lionpaw students arrives at an archway framed in brilliant blue and gleaming gold.

"Well Lionpaws!" shouts out an older girl at the front of the line. "We have arrived at Lionpaw House tower! First years, this will be your home for the next 6 years - remember that only Lionpaws can pass this archway, so if you have any friends in other houses..." there are boos and laughter from the children at this remark "...you will have to fraternize elsewhere! Into the Lion's den everyone!"

With that she turns and leads you all inside.

You realise that the stone archway is carved in the shape of a lion's open mouth, with sharp stone fangs hanging down like stalagmites.

When you pass through the archway you can't help but stop and stare, your mouth hanging open almost as wide as the lion's jaws you have just passed through.

You are confronted by a large bright circular space. Dangling from the ceiling far above are golden globes enchanted with a magico-flourescent light that illuminates a patterned marble floor. As you enter the room a handful of spell-bound goat-sized magical snails swivel their eyes stalks in your direction - doomed to forever slither the marble flagstones, the snails buff them to a gleaming brightness as they go. Scattered around are luxurious sofas, comfy armchairs and expensive rugs.

Doorways leading to staircases are spaced at regular intervals around this enormous room. Above each doorway is a little sign and you read some of them:

"Bedrooms. Snack store. Swimming Pool. Virtual reality gaming room. Sauna. Infinity Pools. Steam Room...." you look at Aaron. "Did you know about this? This place is amazing!"

Alex Bleazely, Aaron's older brother hears you: "Listen Arthur, if Hogsnorts is going to attract the best talent and compete with the top international universities like Yale, Cambridge, Dorkstrang and Hull we need the best facilities. Right, I'm going to change into my swimming trunks - last one in the Jacuzzi is an eggy drifter!"

Alex and Robert Bleezely dash off, followed by two or three other Lionpaw students, whooping and hollering.

"Let's go and find our bedrooms Arthur," says Aaron.

You go up the staircase marked "Bedrooms" and when you reach the next floor you see two more doorways, one with a sign saying "Arthur" above it and another with an "Aaron" sign. By some magical warping of space the inside of the Lionpaw House tower must be much bigger than the outside.

You push open the door to your bedroom.

A softly carpeted corridor opens onto a cozy little living room. Another door leads to a spacious bathroom containing a large bathtub with four carved iron lion feet at each corner. Finally your bedroom itself, in the centre of which is a giant four-poster bed, festooned with blue and gold drapes. On the pillow is a cuddly little toy lion and a small mint chocolate. A window in your bedrooms looks out over the Hogsnorts school grounds far below where the sun is sinking below the horizon.

You take off your shoes and jump backwards onto the bed. I could be happy here you think to yourself as you crunch up the mint chocolate - already it feels like home. With a smile on your face you fall fast asleep.

221.
The dark web

You and Daniel start pushing at the spider web with your hands.

It is amazingly strong and also sticky. With every push you get more and more enmeshed in the web and it becomes harder and harder to unstick yourself.

"Arthur", cries Daniel, "I'm stuck!"

You turn to the side and see that somehow Daniel has got himself totally tangled up in the web - he is hanging upside down with spider webs curled round his ankles and his hair brushing the floor.

"Don't worry Daniel, let's see if we can figure out a way to free ourselves!" you reply but as you try to move over towards Daniel you feel thick ropes of spider web curl around your legs and lift you up into the air. In an instant you are as helpless as he is.

You feel your panic rising as you struggle. Who is going to help you now? No-one even knows that you are here except perhaps Slumblebore.

"Watch out Arthur, look! Spiders! Millions of spiders!"

Daniel is right. Crawling out of the cracks of the walls, floor and ceiling is a host of spiders. They scurry along the webs heading for you and Daniel. In a sudden insight you realise that these spiders have made the webs themselves, working as a one enormous team to add strand after strand of spider silk until they had created these rope-thick cobwebs. So many spiders working as one! You are amazed to see such well coordinated behaviour, so rare in most spider species. Has a new species evolved in the dungeon? you wonder.

Then all thoughts flee from your mind as the wave of spiders reach you. They stop inches away.

One lone spider - no bigger than the rest - scuttles out of the pack, delicately steps onto your robes then up to your neck. You see a flash of tiny fangs then you fade into unconsciousness.

223.
Professor Jape

You choose Offensive Magic with Professor Comicus Jape.

You find the classroom after only a few wrong turns, and take a seat next to Snako. You see a boy called Aaron Bleezely from Lionpaw class looking at you with a frown in his face. Stupid Lionpaws, you think to yourself, and sneer at him supersiliously.

"Now then children!" Professor Jape calls out at the front of the class. "Now then, now then! It's so lovely to meet you all."

Professor Jape is wearing a black cape with a red velvet lining and has a very pale almost white face. He smiles at the class warmly and gives a little wink.

"Today we are going to learn some offensive magic. Now as you probably know offensive magic can be extremely dangerous. But that's not to say we can't have a bit of a laugh and a giggle as we go along eh? Eh children? Eh?"

Professor Jape makes a loud high pitched giggling noise. Some of the other children laugh back nervously.

"In fact I always like to break the ice with my new children with a joke. Hands up if you want to hear one of my jokes children."

............................................................

1. You put your hand up - you could do with a laugh. ~ Go to number 147

2. You keep your hand down - this is a waste of time and you want to learn spells. ~ Go to number 298

224.
Magical mayhem

You raise your wand, point it at the woodlice menacingly and shout loudly:

"Dispara dinosaurio demente!"

From out of the end of your wand comes a faint but growing roaring sound, like an angry lion. The noise grows louder and louder until it is so loud it hurts your ears.

"Arthur, what did you do?" asks Snako in alarm.

"I don't..." you begin, but before you can finish your sentence, a huge golden dinosaur head somehow forces it's way out of the tip of your wand, and roars again deafeningly.

"ROAR!!!"

"Did I ever tell you that I'm terrified of giant angry tyrannosaurus rexes!" yells out Snako, too petrified to move.

But there's nothing you can do, the spell has been cast. The enormous magical t-rex squeezes its way out of your wand and charges its way towards the woodlice, waggling its ridiculous little front arms in a demented fashion.

It launches itself at the nearest woodlouse which has no time to react.

But instead of crushing the woodlouse in its banana sized teeth, the t-rex - impossibly - just bounces off.

It roars and tries again, with the same result.

Then it hits you - woodlice are completely immune to magic.

The dinosaur appears to understand this too. It looks around for a better target. And it's crazy little red eyes fix on you and Snako.

With a sense of horror you realise that the t-rex is now hunting you!

The rabid dinosaur leaps at you and Snako but instead of eating you it flings you both into the stone wall on each side and you bump your head painfully. The t-rex stomps up the corridor before disappearing a puff of gold stars as the magic wears off.

As you slide down the wall and into unconsciousness, you can see the millions of woodlice waving their little antennae. As you close your eyes you think: are they laughing?

............................................................

1. You lie down unconscious for an indeterminate length of time. ~ Go to number 232

226.
The dungeon door

As the other Ravenwing students file off into the corridor on their way to Ravenwing House tower you and Daniel quietly tip-toe away to the side. After two or three turns of the passageway the noise of the other students has faded to nothing.

"Now where?" asks Daniel, a tremor of fear and excitement in his voice.

You look around trying to get your bearings. You realise that the school is absolutely huge. There must be hundreds of corridors, archways, passageways and staircases. How will you even find the way to the dungeons?

Just then you notice five spiders walking along the floor, lined up one after the other. What are those curious little creatures up to? you think, and start to follow them along the corridor.

They turn left, right, right again, then left before disappearing under a crack in the doorway.

You look up. Above the door is a sign scrawled in thick black letters: DUNGEONS.

"This is it!" you whisper to Daniel, afraid to speak too loud in the silence. You reach out to turn the great brass doorknob and open the door. But it doesn't budge, and as you pull on the doorknob the edge of the door glows golden.

"Look!" says Daniel to you quietly, "The door is enchanted with an enchantment of locking. We'll never open it if we don't know the magic password. We need to figure out a way to get the password if we are going to get inside."

At that moment you hear lots of footsteps coming your way from around a corner. It must be a group of students on their way to their house tower! Before you have time to hide, they turn the corner and spot you.

"Arthur and Daniel isn't it? What are you two doing there, exploring the castle already? Come on back into line!" To your surprise you are addressed by one of the older Ravenwing students. You must have somehow taken a hidden shortcut when following the spiders.

............................................................

1. You head back into the line and head off into the passageway with the rest of the students. You glance back thoughtfully at the dungeon door as you walk away: you'll figure it out someday soon. ~ Go to number 146

227.
Another chance

The clock strikes one... two... three.

The golden glow shining all around you gets stronger and stronger and soon you have to shut your eyes to the blinding golden light.

After a momentary sensation of vertigo, as if you have all of a sudden fallen, you sense that the golden light is fading away.

Opening your eyes you find you are at the bottom of a great stone well, with a circle of light far above. You realise that you have magically transported back to Percy the Picking Pigeon's hole in the Hogsnort's Great Hall, just as Slumblebore said you would. Somehow you know that you have also travelled back in time to before, when you had just arrived at the school. You are that Arthur once again in Percy's hole, but this time you can make a new choice.

"Well Arthur," says a voice directly to your brain. "What will you choose, coo coo." It is Percy the giant pigeon and you see again his giant yellow eyes staring at you.

This time you know you will make a good choice...

228.
Cut through the web

"Vamos varita vencer vistosamente!" you exclaim as dramatically as you can manage.

A flickering golden light slowly extends from the top of your wand until it is about a metre long. You swing the "light sword" around and it makes a satisfying swishing zooming sound. You feel slightly terrified at the thought of all the damage you could do with this sabre made of light.

You take a tentative swipe at the nearest strand of spider silk. Despite it being as thick as a steel cable and twice as tough, the light sword slices through it with no effort at all and the spider web flops to the floor.

You steadily walk forwards, cutting through the spider web with your magical golden light sword, feeling the magic from the wand course through your body. You feel you are getting the hang of this magic thing!

Soon the spider web has gone. You and Kensley race down the passageway and skid around a corner...

230.
The dungeon door

You enter the passageway sloping downwards and after many twists and turns in the passageway you are hopelessly lost.

You notice a charming little spider running around a corner ahead of you. Curiously it then comes back round the corner, looks at you and waits, then lifts up a spindly leg and points.

"Arthur" says Kensley, "I think that charming little little spider wants us to follow him."

"I'm not sure if we should really be doing this..." you say. "But Let's see where it goes."

You follow the spider as it turns this way then that and are delighted to finally arrive at what must surely be the entrance to the dungeon.

A huge wooden door, banded with iron and patterned with silver swirls, stands within a stone archway. Either side of the door two antique sets of armour are positioned upright as if on guard.

The spider you were following scurries through the keyhole of the door and disappears.

Above the door there is a sign written in some archaic font, which reads: "DUNGEON".

"Arthur!" Kensley exclaims, "I think this may be the door to the dungeon!"

"You may be onto something Kensley", you reply. "But don't get carried away just yet."

You try the doorknob... but it doesn't budge.

"There's a magical enchantment of locking on the door!" says Kensley. "We will need to cast a counter spell if we are to get through."

As you lift up your wand, you rack your brains to try to think of a spell that might work.

231.
Beetle battle

You find yourself face to face with a trio of bombardier beetles, who seem to be guarding the way.

"Look how large these three fine specimens are!" says Daniel. "I wonder how they will react to a human presence?"

You find out immediately: as one of them makes an angry chittering sound. Even though you don't understand the beetle exactly, you are pretty sure he or she or it doesn't like you.

The three beetles turn around in the corridor to face away from you.

"How curious, they seem to be retreating" remarks Daniel with a puzzled look.

Suddenly there is a loud popping sound and an aqueous solution of hydroquinones and hydrogen peroxides shoots out of the beetles' posterior regions.

"Duck!" you cry, and you and Daniel throw yourself to one side. The liquid misses you by inches. The stone flagstone bubbles and fizzes where the liquid struck it.

You both pick yourself up off the floor and scramble back round the corner for safety.

"That was too close," you say. "We need to find a way to immobilise those beetles, or distract them somehow."

You think hard, there must be a spell that you can use that would incapacitate those three remarkable creatures, preferably without harming them so they can be studied later.

After a moment, with a determined spring in your step, you decide. You leap out from your hiding place, your wand at the ready.

232.
A speedy recovery

With a groan you open your eyes.

Looking around you you appear to be in the Hogsnorts School hospital. You see Snako lying next to you on an identical bed, also groaning. Various medical instruments hang on the walls: stethoscopes, ear trumpets, bone-saws, syringes and thaumometers.

How did I get here? you wonder. Then it comes back to you and you shudder: the dungeon.

Something bad is definitely going on down there. Now even more than before you realise that you have to find out what it is, and stop it. Or somehow claim its power for yourself. It is up to you - and for next time you know at least one choice that you should not make again...

"Hello Arther and Snako. I see you have returned to the conscious realm." Madame Blavatsky, the Professor of Defence Against Dark Magic walks into the room.

"Wssrrflbittit?" you mumble.

"Yes you had quite a shock back there I'm sure. When Slumblebore found you, you were both completely unconscious. But don't worry you will make a full recovery - the antiodarkotics I gave you will flush all the bad magic out shortly."

"Thank you" you manage to say.

"But the most important thing is that you get some rest. I'm going to cast a sleeping spell on you now, timed so that you will wake up tomorrow morning at 7am. When you are sleeping soundly I will teleport you to your own bedrooms in your House Tower."

As she chants the magic words "somnolencia salchicha sabrosa" you try to speak but you can't stop yourself drifting away.

What is in the dungeon? you desperately want to ask. Your lips form the word "Wha...?"...

............................................................

1. Then you drift off into a deep healing sleep. ~ Go to number 213

233.
The heart of the dungeon

With an uncharacteristic flash of inspiration, you remember that woodlice are one of the few creatures that are completely immune to magic of any kind... but! They detest dryness and heat. Ergo you can cast a heat spell to clear a path indirectly. Brilliant!

You raise your wand. "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A magical flame whooshes out of your wand, sending golden sparks shooting.

The flame doesn't harm the woodlice, but it heats the air, and dries it. The woodlice have no option but to retreat: without moisture they can't absorb oxygen, they would suffocate.

This leaves open a path.

"Wait!" says Kensley. "I... I can't go on."

"What's wrong? Why not?"

"It's the woodlice. I have had a terrible fear of them ever since one accidentally rolled into my cake mixture when I was a child. It got baked into a scone and I ate it by mistake. I can still feel the horrible crunch when I bit through its carapace, and the hideous tickle when I swallowed its roasted legs. I can't... I just can't get any closer to them."

"Listen Kensley, don't worry," you take a deep breath. "I'll keep going by myself, on my own. You get Slumblebore and tell him what is going on down here. And if should... if I should... die down here, tell him that I would like to be buried outside my lovely little Hogger Hole next to the potatoes."

"Yes, yes... I will Arthur. I'll get Slumblebore and we will bury you in the potato patch together," says Kensley with a little sniffle.

Kensley turns and walks quickly back up the passageway. As she walks you notice that she has put her hand in her pocket and is fiddling with something which then drops out of her pocket and hits the stone flagstones with a faint chink. Kensley doesn't notice and walks on, but the thing bounces and then rolls down the corridor towards you, stopping at your feet.

You bend down and pick it up. It is a ring of pure gold.

How curious, you think.

Even more curious, you can just make out some tiny writing engraved on the surface of the ring, which says:

One Ring to trick them all,
One Ring to cloud you,
One Ring to fool them all,
In ghostly darkness shroud you.

But there is no time to worry about mysterious rings: you breathe deeply and plunge forwards past the woodlouse army who are delving into the still moist cracks in the stone.

After walking further down the dank, chilly passage you come to a door made of iron bars.

Just beyond you can hear a faint murmur of voices.

This is it: the heart of the dungeon. Whoever or whatever has been setting these traps for you and Kensley must be here, at the bottom of it all.

............................................................

1. You push open the door and go inside. ~ Go to number 255

"Watermelon?" you repeat.

"Yes: watermelon. I chose this password because it is my favourite fruit. The juicy red flesh, so tasty!... the visual contrast with the green outer skin.... the crunchy black pips - delicious!"

Slumblebore stares into the distance for a few moments then snaps out of his reverie.

"Where was I? Yes: watermelon. Then you must descend the staircase that leads down into the very depths of the school. In the past students would be imprisoned in the dungeons for misbehaviour. Now they are mainly used to store broken chairs and Christmas decorations. But we go down there so infrequently there is no telling what evil is brewing in some dark corner."

"I advise you to keep your wand at the ready and your wits sharp Arthur. And remember all the lessons, all the spells, the teachers have taught you. You will be put to the test and I do not know how it will turn out."

"Sir," you ask. "What do you think is down there?"

"Long have I studied this question, seeking knowledge in ancient scrolls and consulting with the wisest of the wise. Not a sausage. All I can say is that in the dead of night when I listen hard at the dungeon door I can sometimes hear a faint murmuring noise... like the ghosts of a thousand lost souls groaning at their fate. Either that or it's the hot water system."

242.
Professor Eric Knid

Professor Eric Knid's classroom is on the ground floor, in a wing of Hogsnorts castle that sticks out a little from the main building. The windows look onto vegetable gardens on one side and some overgrown brambles on the other.

You walk into the class with Snako and sit down. For this lesson Snakefang House first years have combined with Hedgehog House first years. Kensley Potato - a first year Hogger - sits down on your other side and starts fiddling with her pencil case.

Professor Knid stands at the front patiently while the children settle. His long arms and legs poke out of his wizard's gown. A strange shimmery cloak dangles from his shoulders. Dressed all in black he looks rather like an overgrown spider.

When there is silence he raises his hands. His odd looking cloak flutters around him while he speaks:

"Today you will learn about the care of magical creatures.

"But before we do that let me take this opportunity to remind you of Slumblebore's warning at the house sorting dinner." Professor Knid looks out at the class with a piercing gaze and it appears to you that his eyes are focused directly on you.

"No-one must go into the dungeons this term. There is something mysterious and very probably dangerous down there this term, and no-one is allowed to interrupt. Is that clear?"

Nods all round from the class. You exchange raised eyebrows with Snako. What could be going on down there? And why was Professor Knid staring straight at you?

"Right!" Knid claps his hands."Can anyone tell me the most common type of magical creature?"

"Unicorns?" shouts out one boy.

"Witches cats!" shouts a girl at the back.

"Flying monkeys!" shouts someone else.

"These are all good answers. But not correct. The most common type of magical creature is the insect, or, more generally: the arthropod. Spiders, snails, flies, ants, beetles, woodlice, these are all infinitely more common than the unicorn. And many of them have been enchanted by a magician or witch at some point in the past making them effectively immortal until trodden on.

"For example, look closely at my cloak children." Eric Knid walks up and down the class so the children can see better.

You realise that the professor's cloak is not merely shimmering, it is moving. It seems to be made up of lots of tiny moving things. Then you realise what they are and your eyes widen in hideous fascination.

Eric Knid's cloak is made up of thousands upon thousands of flies, each fly grasping the flies next to it with their tiny hairy legs. As they flutter their wings or move their black and iridescent green bodies, the cloak appears to undulate as if in a breeze.

To you and the rest of the class it seems revolting, but Professor Knid is oblivious.

"Until you look closely my cloak is just an ordinary magician's cape. But it is actually made up of thousands of enchanted and specially trained flies. And each one can fly off at my command to do my bidding - to deliver a message perhaps, or sit on someone's dinner, or to distract a powerful wizard in the act of casting a spell.

"Yes the insect world is a vast and overlooked wonder and in this lesson I am going to teach you about a tiny portion of it.

"But before we learn any magic, does anyone doubt me that the arthropods - the insects - are the true marvels of the animal world?"

Professor Knid looks round expectantly, his eyebrows raised.

1. You don't like insects that much. You raise your hand to ask what makes them better than other animals. ~ Go to number 109

2. You don't say anything. Clearly Professor Knid had got a bugbear about insects and he is just itching to waste the whole lesson talking about them. You would rather learn some magic. ~ Go to number 168

243.
Battle rage

"Die beetles, die!" you cry, running towards the three giant bombardier beetles.

In your battle rage you forget all about magic and your wand, you just want to reach the beetles and grapple them with your bare hands, mano a beetlo.

"Yaaaah!" you cry, closing the distance fast...

...but not fast enough. The three beetles swiftly raise up their bottoms, and shoot out three streams of superheated acid, accompanied by three loud popping sounds.

One stream misses your head by inches, another strikes the wall beside you, the third the floor in front.

"Hahahaha, you'll never get me for I dance the dance of..."

But you never get the chance to tell them exactly what dance it is you are dancing because at that moment your foot slips on the pool of acid on the floor and slides out from underneath you. You fly through the air very briefly before slamming into the floor, bumping your head hard enough to knock you out cold.

245.
The heart of the dungeon

You remember that woodlice are one of the few creatures that are completely immune to magic of any kind, and decide to cast a heat spell to clear a path indirectly.

You raise your wand. "Fiel fresa fusila fuego!"

A magical flame whooshes out of your wand, sending golden sparks shooting.

The flame doesn't harm the woodlice, but it heats the air, and dries it. The woodlice have no option but to retreat: without moisture they can't absorb oxygen, they would suffocate.

This leaves a path.

You breathe deeply and plunge forwards past the woodlouse army who are retreating into the still moist cracks in the stone.

After walking further down the dank, chilly passage you and Daniel come to a door made of iron bars.

Just beyond you can hear a faint murmur of voices.

This is it: the heart of the dungeon. Whoever or whatever has been setting these traps for you and Daniel must be here, at the bottom of it all.

............................................................

1. You push open the door and go inside. ~ Go to number 204

246.
Just in time

You leap out of the clock just in time, you could already feel the magic sucking you down.

Breathing hard you look back at the clock face and see the hands of the clock spinning madly backwards.

"You have changed your mind about changing your mind have you?" Slumblebore observes, his bushy eyebrows waggling. "Well you can come and see me at any time and change your mind again if you want."

"I... I... I think I don't want to leave Ravenwing just yet," you stammer. You are not quite sure why you changed your mind at the last minute, but it just didn't feel... right.

"Well as you are not going anywhere just yet, let's get talking about the problem we have right now," says Slumblebore. "I'm talking of course about what we are going to do about the evil presence in the school dungeon. I fear it is something that may threaten the very existence of Hogsnorts."

247.
The dark web

You and Snako start pushing at the spider web with your hands.

It is amazingly strong and also sticky. When you push a strand it becomes harder and harder to unstick your hands.

"Arthur", cries Snako, "I'm stuck!"

You turn to the side and see that somehow Snako has got himself totally tangled up in the web - he is hanging upside down with spider webs curled round his ankles and his hair brushing the floor.

"Hang in there Snako, I'm going to see if I can get through!" you reply but as you try to move over towards Snako you feel thick ropes of spider web curl around your legs and lift you up into the air. In an instant you are as helpless as Snako.

You feel your panic rising as you struggle. Who is going to help you now? No-one even knows that you are here except perhaps Slumblebore.

"Aaargh! Look Arthur - spiders! Millions of spiders!"

Snako is right. Crawling out of the cracks of the walls, floor and ceiling is a host of spiders. They scurry along the webs heading for you and Snako. In a sudden insight you realise that these spiders have made the webs themselves, working as a one enormous team to add strand after strand of spider silk until they had created these rope-thick cobwebs. So many spiders working as one! What could they not achieve together?

Then all thoughts flee from your mind as the wave of spiders reach you. They stop inches away.

One lone spider - no bigger than the rest - scuttles out of the pack, delicately steps onto your robes then up to your neck. You see a flash of tiny fangs then you fade into unconsciousness.

248.
Jape's spell

Along with most of the other children you keep your hands down.

"You don't want to hear my jokes? Well I never!" Professor Jape looks genuinely hurt for a moment, but quickly recovers his composure.

"Perhaps you will be laughing on the other side of your face by the end of this lesson." Jape gives another high pitched giggle and you all shift on your seats uneasily.

"Maybe," he continues, "you will enjoy this one. I need a volunteer!"

No one volunteers so Jape scans the classroom. He points at Daniel.

"You! Come forward."

Daniel walks to the front of the class looking nervous.

Without any warning Professor Jape whips out his wand, points it at Daniel and yells: "Vamos varita vencer vistosamente!"

A golden light extrudes from the tip of Jape's wand. The light looks like a solid sparkly golden beam and extends for one metre then stops emerging. Jape swings his wand around and you realise that he has created a magical golden light sword! As the golden beam swipes through the air it makes satisfying swishing zoom noises.

"En guard!" snaps Jape to Daniel with a gleam in his eye before suddenly launching into a frenzied attack, swiping left and right with his light sword. In a flash he has covered the 5 metres to Daniel and he holds the light sword directly at Daniel's throat.

"Now you will die." Jape says simply.

There is dead silence in the class. Everyone is holding their breath.

Then, almost in exact unison, everyone screams and runs out of the door, except Daniel who is rooted to the spot in fear, and you because you don't want to abandon your friend.

Professor Jape lowers the light sword and gives a high pitched giggle.

"I were just joking, didn't you know that?" he said to the fleeing children. "It were just a joke!" he shouted louder at their fleeing backs.

Professor Jape sighs and says to you and Daniel: "They can't take a joke, can they? Well lessons over now I suppose. But remember: Vamos varita vencer vistosamente that's a good one that is!"

You and Daniel nod and swallow, and without saying another word, flee out of the classroom.

254.
Inner peace

"I'm Arthur Otley and I want to learn some spells" you say to Professor Blavatsky.

"Ah so impatient. And yet this impatience stops you learning about yourself. I can see that you are very far from self control as yet."

The teacher stands up and raises one hand.

"But do not worry, any of you. Because we will start with a simple meditation session to help you gain control."

You groan inwardly. This sounds boring.

"Close your eyes everyone," begins Professor Blavatsky. "Make sure you are comfortable in your seats. Now I want you to focus on your breathing. Breathe in. Breathe out. Breathe in... and breathe out.

"Feel the breath flowing into your nostrils. Concentrate on the sensation. Do you feel your nose hairs tickling? Perhaps a small bogey flapping around in your nasal passage? Just think about the breath, how it feels."

Despite yourself you feel your awareness sharpening, and you do indeed feel a small bogey in your nostril wobbling around as you breathe in and out.

"Now I want you to think about a special number. The special number is 42. A four and then a two. Forty two. This number is not just a number it is also a place. A location. A place of calm that you can always turn to in moments of difficulty or stress.

"This number 42 is a place within yourself, but it is a real place too that anyone can reach, if they just turn to that number... the number 42. As you turn to 42, just keep your thumb here so you know where to come back to."

Amazingly you feel a sensation as if you are floating somehow, except with your thumb stuck down in front of you. Concentrating fiercely you try with all your might to turn to 42. You float away...

...

"Did anyone manage to meditate and reach 42?" asks Madam Blavatsky.

You definitely feel you went... somewhere. You think this is what Professor Blavatsky meant.

"Any time you find yourself in need of quiet and peace, just repeat this meditation exercise and think of the number 42 and you will find a place of calm and relaxation - but keep your thumb right where you are and you will be able to turn back whenever you want."

"Class dismissed! We will meet again."

255.
Professor Eric Knid Explains

A voice, strong and commanding, emerges from the darkness. "You? The saviour, a mere stripling first year? Impossible!"

Another voice, high pitched and chittery, answers him. "Yes Eric, this is him. He is the wand holder."

As your eyes adjust to the gloom, you can make out a figure standing in the centre of the room. A wizard - and someone you recognise.

"Professor Knid! But what...?" you exclaim.

"Yes Professor Eric Knid at your service! Or perhaps I should say that you will be at my service... Arthur isn't it?"

"Yes my name's Arthur. Arthur Otley." A sensation of fear congeals in your throat so strong that you can barely speak. "What do you mean? And who were you talking to just now?"

"All in good time, Arthur..." with an unexpectedly swift movement Professor Knid draws his wand and shoots a spell of locking at the iron gate which... swings shut and then hits some invisible object and swings open again. There is a curious noise like a muffled cry, and then finally the clangs shut.

But there is no time to worry about the curious muffled cry - you are trapped.

"What are you going to do?" you exclaim in a fearful high pitched squeak.

Eric Knid smiled. Even in the dark you can see the mad gleam in his eye: "Revolution!"

"Explain why Eric." That chittering voice again, appearing out of nowhere.

"Yes - why. Why?" Professor Knid takes a deep breath. "Ever since I was a young boy Arthur I have felt an affinity with insects, spiders, crabs. With the Arthropods. A dog will bite you, not so an earwig! A lion may eat you, not so a woodlouse! A human may betray you, a spider will not.

"My faithful friends growing up were slugs, ants, flies and beetles. But my friends were mercilessly crushed, poisoned, and swatted by humans.

"The final straw? Slumblebore sat on a spider - and laughed."

"I couldn't bear it. I sought out the Great Spider King Azog himself. What joy when I found him in the forbidden bushes and entered his service. Together we have been gathering supporters here in this dungeon, insects and spiders in their millions. For revenge. For a revolution. To take over the school!

"No longer will it just be Lionpaw House, Ravenwing House, Snakefang House, and Hedgehog House! We will have a new house mightier than all of them. The Order of the Arthropods! And I will be headmaster."

"But why me?" fear chills you. "I'm just a first year, I don't want any trouble."

"You are the only one who can stop us Arthur," says the mysterious high pitched voice. "But with you on our side we will be invincible!"

"Who is that?" you cry.

"This is the Great Spider King Azog himself. And you are honoured to stand in his presence." Professor Knid explains.

"Where?" You can't see anyone other than the Professor.

"Here!"

"Where, I can't see!"

"Right here, look! Closer!"

Woodlouse warfare
